Amm and Khass — General and Specific
beginner
8 min
The Hanafi Classification of Nouns by Meaning and Coinage
Defines the complete tree of noun categories based on coinage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each category (sifah, ism jins, 'alam, mutlaq, muqayyad, 'amm, ma'hud, nakira, ma'rifa) and state its definition according to the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
All nouns fall into a precise tree: derived or non-derived, specific or generic, absolute or restricted, general or particular.

This passage from a commentary on al-Tawdih presents the complete second division of nouns (asma) based on their coinage (wad'). Understanding this tree is essential for interpreting legal texts correctly, as the type of noun determines the scope of its ruling. We will walk through the branches step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the root: Apparent nouns
The division applies only to apparent nouns (ism zahir), excluding pronouns and demonstratives. Recognize the term 'ism zahir' as the starting point.
Pronouns (damair) and demonstratives (asma isharat) are excluded from this classification.
2
Split by derivation: Sifah vs. non-derived
If the noun has a derived pattern (e.g., fa'il, maf'ul) and its meaning matches the source (masdar), it is a descriptor (sifah). Otherwise, check for specificity: if the meaning is determinate, it is a proper noun ('alam); if not, it is a generic noun (ism jins).
'Alam and ism jins may be derived or non-derived.
3
Consider restriction: Mutlaq vs. Muqayyad
For sifah and ism jins, if the meaning is intended without any qualification, it is absolute (mutlaq); if with a restriction, it is restricted (muqayyad).
Hanafi usul treats mutlaq as applying to the essence without conditions.
4
Consider individuals: 'Amm, Ma'hud, Nakira
For the individuals of a sifah or ism jins, if all individuals are intended, it is general ('amm). If some individuals with specification, it is the known (ma'hud). If some individuals without specification, it is indefinite (nakira).
Ma'rifa is defined by the listener's knowledge at utterance, not by coinage.
5
Understand the role of aspects (haythiyat)
These categories are not inherently contradictory; they combine or exclude based on the aspect considered. For example, 'amm and mushtarak can coexist under different aspects.
The same word can belong to multiple categories under different aspects.

Source Text

قال المصنف في التوضيح ثم ههنا تقسيم آخر اتم لفظ کی باعتبار وضع کے یہ دوسری تقسیم ہے اس کی معرفت اور اس سے حاصل شدہ اقسام کی معرفت ضروری ہے ۔ والضیا الاسم الظاهر المخ ضمائر اور اسماء اشارات کو خارج کرنے کی خاطر اسم ظاہر کی قید کی حاصل تقسیم یہ ہے کہ اسم ظاہر کا معنی اور مفہوم اگر بعینہ وہی ہے جو مفہوم مشتق منہ یعنی مصدر کا تھا اور اس کے ساتھ مشتق کے اوزان میں سے کوئی وزن بھی ہو تو نصفۃ اسے صفہ معہود . تکرہ اور معرفہ ان تمام کی تعریفات اس تقسیم سے معلوم ہوگئی ہیں ۔ داعلمان المطلق من اقسام الخاص کیونکہ مطلق کی وضع واحد نوعی کے لئے ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہ خاص النوع میں درج ہوگا۔ واعلم انه يجب في كل قسم آج یعنی ان تمام اقسام میں ہر ایک قسم کے ساتھ اعتبار حیثیت کیا جائیگا تاکہ ان کے مابین تمایز بر قرار رہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان اقسام کے اندر تنافی بالذات نہیں ہے بلکہ بالحیثیات ہے پھر بعض حیثیات ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ منافی نہیں ہیں اور بعض منافی ہیں سیاقی فی الشرح وبعض الاقسام قد يجتمع الخ یعنی بعض اقسام اور بعض کے ساتھ جمع ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اور بعض ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوتے مثل قوله جرت العيون لفظ عین بائیں حیثیت کہ ایک مرتبہ اس کی وضع باصرہ کے لئے اور مرة اخرمی اس کی وضع پانی کے چشمہ کے لئے ہے تو یہ مشترک قرار پائیگا اور اگر بائیں حیثیت ملحوظ کریں کہ اس کی وضع عین الماء کے لئے ہے تو اس معنی کے لحاظ جمیع افراد عیون الماء کو شامل ہے تو عام ہوگا تو واضح ہوا کہ عام و مشترک کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے لکن بين العام والخاص تناف لیکن خاص و عام کے درمیان منافات ہے اور یہ ممکن نہیں ہے کہ ایک لفظ ایک حیثیت سے خاص ہو اور دوسری حیثیت سے عام ہو ایسا ہونا ممکن نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح بواقی کا اعتبار کر لیا جائے خانہ سھل بعد الوقوف على الحدود التي ذكرنا فصل الخاص قال الشارح في التلويح قوله وايضاً الاسم الظاهر انا اسم کے ساتھ ظاہر کی قید لگا کر مضمر کو ان اقسام سے خارج کر دیا اور اسی طرح اسم اشارہ بھی خارج از اقسام ہے تو اسم ظاہر کہنے سے گویا کہ مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ اسم جو نہ مضمر ہو نہ اسم اشاره ـ والصفة بمقتضى هذا التقسيم تو اس تقسیم کے لحاظ سے صفہ اسم مشتق کا نام ہے جس کا معنی بعینہ وہی معنی ہو جو مشتق مز یعنی مصدر کا موضوع از معنی اور اس کے ساتھ وزن مشتق بھی ہو۔ فالضارب تو اس تعریف کے لحاظ سے ضارب ایسا لفظ ہے جو ضرب سے مشتق ہے اور اس کا معنی وہی ضرب والا معنی ہے اور ساتھ وزن فاعل بھی ملحوظ ہے جو وزن مشتق ہے اور مضروب بھی معنی ضرب کے ساتھ وزن مفعول بھی رکھتا ہے ۔ دھذا معنی قولهم الز یعنی ان کے قول کہ صفہ وہ اسم ہے جو ذات مہمہ پر دال ہو اور ایک معنی معین پر بھی جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہو یہی مراد ہے جو پہلے ہم نے واضح کردی ہے راحتر از بقوله مع وزن المشتق یعنی وزن مشتق پر ہونے کی جو قید کی ہے اس
The author said in al-Tawdih: Then here is another complete division of words according to coinage. This is the second division; knowledge of it and of the categories derived from it is necessary. And the apparent noun—the restriction of apparent noun excludes pronouns and demonstrative nouns. The resulting division is: The meaning and signification of the apparent noun, if it is exactly the meaning of the derived-from (i.e., the infinitive) and it also has one of the derived patterns, then it is called a descriptor (sifah). Otherwise, if the meaning is not exactly that of the derived-from—whether it has no derived-from at all (like 'amad?) or has a derived-from but the meaning is not identical, rather there is some difference—then if its meaning is specific and determinate, it is a proper noun ('alam); if it is not specific and determinate, it is a generic noun (ism jins). And proper noun and generic noun are sometimes derived and sometimes not derived. From the descriptor and generic noun: their intended meaning if it is intended without restriction is called absolute (mutlaq); if it is intended with some restriction, it is called restricted (muqayyad). Their individuals: if all individuals are intended, then it is general ('amm); if some individuals are intended, then if that some is determinate and intended, it is called the known (ma'hud); if some individuals are intended without specification (la 'ala al-ta'yin), then it is indefinite (nakira). So nakira is a noun coined for a thing unspecified. At the time of utterance for the listener, i.e., when it is uttered for the listener, it indicates something unspecified for the listener; that is called nakira. And ma'rifa is a noun coined for a thing specified at the time of utterance for the listener. And the reason I said 'at the time of utterance' is that at the time of coinage there is no difference between ma'rifa and nakira in specification and non-specification; rather this difference occurs at the time of utterance. And it is for the listener, so he also restricted it [to the listener], because when a speaker says 'rajulun came', it is possible that this 'rajul' is specified for the speaker but unspecified for the listener; then it is called nakira, even if it is specified for the speaker. So from this division, all the categories: descriptor, generic noun, proper noun, absolute, restricted, general, known, indefinite, and definite—all their definitions are learned from this division. Know that the absolute is among the types of specific (khass) because the absolute is coined for a single type, so it falls under the specific of the type. And know that in every category, one must consider the aspect (i'tibar haythiyat) so that distinction between them is maintained. From this it is understood that there is no intrinsic contradiction among these categories, rather [contradiction is] by aspects. Then some aspects are not contradictory with each other, and some are contradictory. They said in the commentary: 'And some categories may be combined...' i.e., some categories combine with others, and some do not combine with each other. Example: the statement 'the springs (al-uyun) broke forth'—the word 'ayn: if one considers that once it is coined for the seeing eye and another time for the spring of water, then it is considered homonymous (mushtarak). And if one considers that it is coined for the spring of water, then with respect to that meaning it includes all individuals of springs, so it is general ('amm). So it is clear that there is no contradiction between 'amm and mushtarak. But between 'amm and khass there is contradiction, and it is not possible for one word to be khass in one aspect and 'amm in another aspect; such is not possible. And similarly, consider the rest. It is easy after understanding the definitions we have mentioned. Chapter on the specific (fasl al-khass). The commentator said in al-Talwih: His statement 'and also the apparent noun'—he restricted it with 'apparent' to exclude pronouns from these categories, and similarly demonstrative nouns are excluded from the categories. So by saying 'apparent noun' it means the noun that is neither pronoun nor demonstrative. And 'descriptor' according to this division is the name of a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of the derived-from, i.e., the infinitive, and it also has the derived pattern. So 'al-darib' according to this definition is a word derived from 'daraba', and its meaning is exactly the meaning of 'darb', and it also has the pattern 'fa'il' which is a derived pattern. And 'madrub' also has the meaning of 'darb' with the pattern 'maf'ul'. This is the meaning of their statement: 'the descriptor is a noun that indicates a vague essence and also a specific meaning subsisting in it.' This is what we clarified earlier. And he restricted it with the phrase 'with the derived pattern'—the restriction that he mentioned...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic classification (taqsim) of nouns (asma) in the context of usul al-fiqh, as presented in a commentary on al-Tawdih. The author begins by stating that there is a second complete division of words according to their coinage (wad'), and it is essential to know this division and the categories that arise from it. The division applies only to apparent nouns (ism zahir), excluding pronouns (damair) and demonstrative nouns (asma isharat). The first major split: if the noun's meaning is exactly that of its source (masdar) and it has a derived pattern, it is called a descriptor (sifah), like 'darib' from 'darb'. If not, then if the meaning is specific/determinate, it is a proper noun ('alam); otherwise it is a generic noun (ism jins). Both 'alam and ism jins can be derived or non-derived.

From the categories of sifah and ism jins, further divisions are made: if the meaning is intended without restriction, it is absolute (mutlaq); if with restriction, it is restricted (muqayyad). If all individuals are intended, it is general ('amm); if some individuals with specification, it is the known (ma'hud); if without specification, it is indefinite (nakira). The definitions of nakira and ma'rifa hinge on the listener's understanding at the time of utterance: nakira is for a non-specific thing, ma'rifa for a specific thing (from the listener's perspective). The example of 'rajul' shows that a word can be specific for the speaker but still be nakira if the listener does not know the individual.

The commentator then notes that 'absolute' is a type of 'specific' (khass) because it is coined for a single type. Crucially, these categories are not mutually exclusive in themselves; rather, they are distinguished by the aspect (haythiyat) under which they are considered. Some aspects are compatible (e.g., 'amm and mushtarak can coexist, as in the word 'ayn: it is mushtarak between 'eye' and 'spring', and when considering its meaning as 'spring', it is 'amm for all springs). But 'amm and khass under the same aspect cannot combine. The passage ends with a quotation from al-Talwih clarifying that 'apparent noun' excludes pronouns and demonstratives, and further refining the definition of sifah as a derived noun with a specific meaning and pattern.

Key Terms
الصفة (al-sifah): A derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of its source (masdar) and has a derived pattern (e.g., fa'il, maf'ul).
اسم الجنس (ism al-jins): A noun that indicates a common genus or type, not specific, and may or may not be derived; it denotes the meaning without particularization.
العلم (al-ʿalam): A proper noun that specifically designates a particular individual or thing (e.g., Zayd, 'Amr).
المطلق (al-mutlaq): A noun (from sifah or ism jins) that is used without any qualification or restriction (qayd).
المقيد (al-muqayyad): A noun that is qualified by a restriction (qayd), limiting its application to a particular condition.
العام (al-ʿamm): A noun that encompasses all individuals of its category without exception (e.g., 'al-rijal' meaning all men).
المعهود (al-maʿhud): A noun that refers to a specific but previously mentioned or known subset (e.g., 'al-rajul' referring to a known man).
النكرة (al-nakira): A noun coined for a non-specific thing; at utterance, it indicates non-specificity to the listener.
المعرفة (al-maʿrifa): A noun coined for a specific thing; at utterance, it indicates specificity to the listener.
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A homonym that has multiple unrelated meanings (e.g., 'ayn for eye and spring).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes a descriptor (sifah) from other nouns?
A) It is always a proper noun.
B) It has a derived pattern and its meaning matches the source (masdar).
C) It is indefinite and non-derived.
D) It refers to all individuals of a type.

Key Takeaway
The second division of nouns provides a systematic framework for analyzing the linguistic scope of legal texts in Hanafi usul.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
beginner
6 min
Nakira vs. Ma'rifa: The Listener's Perspective
Defines nakira and ma'rifa with emphasis on listener's role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the definitions of nakira and ma'rifa, and apply the listener-based criterion to determine whether a noun is indefinite or definite in context.

Core Idea
A noun is nakira or ma'rifa based on the listener's knowledge at utterance, not the speaker's or the coinage's.

The passage provides precise definitions for nakira and ma'rifa, emphasizing that the distinction depends on the listener's understanding at the time of utterance. This is a key principle in Hanafi usul that affects how we interpret legal texts. We will dissect the definition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition of nakira
Nakira is coined for a non-specific thing, and at the time of utterance for the listener, it indicates non-specificity. The coinage (wad') is for non-specific meaning, but the operative criterion is the listener's understanding at utterance.
2
Recall the definition of ma'rifa
Ma'rifa is coined for a specific thing, and at utterance for the listener, it indicates specificity. The coinage itself does not determine specificity; it is the listener's recognition at utterance that matters.
3
Analyze the example of 'rajul'
When a speaker says 'jani rajul', the word 'rajul' may be specified for the speaker but unspecified for the listener. According to the passage, it is nakira for the listener. This illustrates that the criterion is listener-centric.
The speaker's knowledge does not affect the classification.
4
Understand the role of 'at the time of utterance'
The passage explains that at the time of coinage, there is no difference between nakira and ma'rifa; the difference emerges only at utterance. This is why the definition includes 'at the time of utterance for the listener'.
5
Apply to a new example
Consider 'al-rajul' (the man). With the definite article, it is ma'rifa because the listener can identify the specific man from context. Contrast with 'rajul' without article, which is nakira unless specified otherwise.
The definite article (alif lam) typically makes a noun ma'rifa, but context may override.

قال المصنف في التوضيح ثم ههنا تقسيم آخر اتم لفظ کی باعتبار وضع کے یہ دوسری تقسیم ہے اس کی معرفت اور اس سے حاصل شدہ اقسام کی معرفت ضروری ہے ۔ والضیا الاسم الظاهر المخ ضمائر اور اسماء اشارات کو خارج کرنے کی خاطر اسم ظاہر کی قید کی حاصل تقسیم یہ ہے کہ اسم ظاہر کا معنی اور مفہوم اگر بعینہ وہی ہے جو مفہوم مشتق منہ یعنی مصدر کا تھا اور اس کے ساتھ مشتق کے اوزان میں سے کوئی وزن بھی ہو تو نصفۃ اسے صفہ کہتے ہیں والا یعنی اگر اس اسم کا معنی بعینہ معنی مشتق منہ والا نہیں ہے خواہ اس کا مشتق منہ سرے سے نہ ہو جیسے جو امد یا اس کا مشتق منہ تو ہو لیکن معنی بعینہ نہیں ہے بلکہ کچھ تفاوت ہے خان تشخص معناه اگر اس کا معنی متشخص اور متعین ہے نعلم تو وہ علم ہے والا اگر تشخص و تعین نہیں ہے تو قاسم جنس وہ اسم جنس ہے اور یہ علم اور اسم جنس کبھی مشتق ہوتے ہیں اور کبھی بغیر مشتق تمكل من الصفة الخ یعنی صفہ اور اسم جنس کا جو مسمئی اور معنی ہے اگر وہ بلا قید مراد ہے تو اسے مطلق کہتے ہیں اگر کسی قید کے ساتھ معتبر اور مراد ہے تو اسے مقید کہتے ہیں ادا شخاصہ یعنی اس صفہ اور اسم جنس کے اگر اشخاص و افراد جن پر وہ صادق آتے ہیں مراد ہوں تو اگر اشخاص کل کے کل مراد ہیں نعام تو وہ عام ہے او بعضا بعض افراد مراد ہوں تو اگر یہ بعض معین ہے معصود تو اسے معہود کہتے ہیں او منکرا یعنی بعض افراد لا علی التعین مراد ہیں ۔ فنكرة تو اسے نکرہ کہتے ہیں تھی ما وضع لشئ الم تو یہ نکرہ ایک ایسا اسم ہے جس کی وضع شتی غیر معین کے لئے ہوتی ہے عند الاطلاق للسامع یعنی جس وقت اس کا اطلاق سامع کی خاطر کیا جائے تو سامع کے لئے یہ غیر معین پر دال ہوتا ہے اسے نکرہ کہا جائیگا والمعرفة اور معرفہ وہ اسم ہے جس کی وضع شتی معین کے لئے ہو عند الاطلاق للسامع وانما قلت عند الاطلاق یہ عند الاطلاق کی قید کیوں کی گئی ہے اذ لا فرق کیونکہ بوقت وضع معرفہ اور نکرہ میں تعیین و عدم تعیین کا فرق نہیں ہوا کرتا بلکہ یہ فرق عند الاطلاق ہوتا ہے اور ہوتا بھی للسامع ہے اس لئے سامع کی قید بھی کر دی لانه اذا قال کیونکہ جب کوئی قائل کہتا ہے جانی رجل تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ برجل متکلم کے نزدیک متعین ہو لیکن سامع کے نزدیک غیر متعین تو اسے نکرہ کہا جائیگا اگر چہ متکلم کے نزدیک متعین ہے۔ فعلم من هذا یعنی اس تقسیم سے تمام اقسام یعنی صفر - اسم جنس - علم مطلق - مقید عام معہود . تکرہ اور معرفہ ان تمام کی تعریفات اس تقسیم سے معلوم ہوگئی ہیں ۔ داعلمان المطلق من اقسام الخاص کیونکہ مطلق کی وضع واحد نوعی کے لئے ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہ خاص النوع میں درج ہوگا۔ واعلم انه يجب في كل قسم آج یعنی ان تمام اقسام میں ہر ایک قسم کے ساتھ اعتبار حیثیت کیا جائیگا تاکہ ان کے مابین تمایز بر قرار رہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان اقسام کے اندر تنافی بالذات نہیں ہے بلکہ بالحیثیات ہے پھر بعض حیثیات ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ منافی نہیں ہیں اور بعض منافی ہیں سیاقی فی الشرح وبعض الاقسام قد يجتمع الخ یعنی بعض اقسام اور بعض کے ساتھ جمع ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اور بعض ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوتے مثل قوله جرت العيون لفظ عین بائیں حیثیت کہ ایک مرتبہ اس کی وضع باصرہ کے لئے اور مرة اخرمی اس کی وضع پانی کے چشمہ کے لئے ہے تو یہ مشترک قرار پائیگا اور اگر بائیں حیثیت ملحوظ کریں کہ اس کی وضع عین الماء کے لئے ہے تو اس معنی کے لحاظ جمیع افراد عیون الماء کو شامل ہے تو عام ہوگا تو واضح ہوا کہ عام و مشترک کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے لکن بين العام والخاص تناف لیکن خاص و عام کے درمیان منافات ہے اور یہ ممکن نہیں ہے کہ ایک لفظ ایک حیثیت سے خاص ہو اور دوسری حیثیت سے عام ہو ایسا ہونا ممکن نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح بواقی کا اعتبار کر لیا جائے خانہ سھل بعد الوقوف على الحدود التي ذكرنا فصل الخاص قال الشارح في التلويح قوله وايضاً الاسم الظاهر انا اسم کے ساتھ ظاہر کی قید لگا کر مضمر کو ان اقسام سے خارج کر دیا اور اسی طرح اسم اشارہ بھی خارج از اقسام ہے تو اسم ظاہر کہنے سے گویا کہ مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ اسم جو نہ مضمر ہو نہ اسم اشاره ـ والصفة بمقتضى هذا التقسيم تو اس تقسیم کے لحاظ سے صفہ اسم مشتق کا نام ہے جس کا معنی بعینہ وہی معنی ہو جو مشتق مز یعنی مصدر کا موضوع از معنی اور اس کے ساتھ وزن مشتق بھی ہو۔ فالضارب تو اس تعریف کے لحاظ سے ضارب ایسا لفظ ہے جو ضرب سے مشتق ہے اور اس کا معنی وہی ضرب والا معنی ہے اور ساتھ وزن فاعل بھی ملحوظ ہے جو وزن مشتق ہے اور مضروب بھی معنی ضرب کے ساتھ وزن مفعول بھی رکھتا ہے ۔ دھذا معنی قولهم الز یعنی ان کے قول کہ صفہ وہ اسم ہے جو ذات مہمہ پر دال ہو اور ایک معنی معین پر بھی جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہو یہی مراد ہے جو پہلے ہم نے واضح کردی ہے راحتر از بقوله مع وزن المشتق یعنی وزن مشتق پر ہونے کی جو قید کی ہے اس
The author said in al-Tawdih: Then here is another complete division of words according to coinage. This is the second division; knowledge of it and of the categories derived from it is necessary. And the apparent noun—the restriction of apparent noun excludes pronouns and demonstrative nouns. The resulting division is: The meaning and signification of the apparent noun, if it is exactly the meaning of the derived-from (i.e., the infinitive) and it also has one of the derived patterns, then it is called a descriptor (sifah). Otherwise, if the meaning is not exactly that of the derived-from—whether it has no derived-from at all (like 'amad?) or has a derived-from but the meaning is not identical, rather there is some difference—then if its meaning is specific and determinate, it is a proper noun ('alam); if it is not specific and determinate, it is a generic noun (ism jins). And proper noun and generic noun are sometimes derived and sometimes not derived. From the descriptor and generic noun: their intended meaning if it is intended without restriction is called absolute (mutlaq); if it is intended with some restriction, it is called restricted (muqayyad). Their individuals: if all individuals are intended, then it is general ('amm); if some individuals are intended, then if that some is determinate and intended, it is called the known (ma'hud); if some individuals are intended without specification (la 'ala al-ta'yin), then it is indefinite (nakira). So nakira is a noun coined for a thing unspecified. At the time of utterance for the listener, i.e., when it is uttered for the listener, it indicates something unspecified for the listener; that is called nakira. And ma'rifa is a noun coined for a thing specified at the time of utterance for the listener. And the reason I said 'at the time of utterance' is that at the time of coinage there is no difference between ma'rifa and nakira in specification and non-specification; rather this difference occurs at the time of utterance. And it is for the listener, so he also restricted it [to the listener], because when a speaker says 'rajulun came', it is possible that this 'rajul' is specified for the speaker but unspecified for the listener; then it is called nakira, even if it is specified for the speaker. So from this division, all the categories: descriptor, generic noun, proper noun, absolute, restricted, general, known, indefinite, and definite—all their definitions are learned from this division. Know that the absolute is among the types of specific (khass) because the absolute is coined for a single type, so it falls under the specific of the type. And know that in every category, one must consider the aspect (i'tibar haythiyat) so that distinction between them is maintained. From this it is understood that there is no intrinsic contradiction among these categories, rather [contradiction is] by aspects. Then some aspects are not contradictory with each other, and some are contradictory. They said in the commentary: 'And some categories may be combined...' i.e., some categories combine with others, and some do not combine with each other. Example: the statement 'the springs (al-uyun) broke forth'—the word 'ayn: if one considers that once it is coined for the seeing eye and another time for the spring of water, then it is considered homonymous (mushtarak). And if one considers that it is coined for the spring of water, then with respect to that meaning it includes all individuals of springs, so it is general ('amm). So it is clear that there is no contradiction between 'amm and mushtarak. But between 'amm and khass there is contradiction, and it is not possible for one word to be khass in one aspect and 'amm in another aspect; such is not possible. And similarly, consider the rest. It is easy after understanding the definitions we have mentioned. Chapter on the specific (fasl al-khass). The commentator said in al-Talwih: His statement 'and also the apparent noun'—he restricted it with 'apparent' to exclude pronouns from these categories, and similarly demonstrative nouns are excluded from the categories. So by saying 'apparent noun' it means the noun that is neither pronoun nor demonstrative. And 'descriptor' according to this division is the name of a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of the derived-from, i.e., the infinitive, and it also has the derived pattern. So 'al-darib' according to this definition is a word derived from 'daraba', and its meaning is exactly the meaning of 'darb', and it also has the pattern 'fa'il' which is a derived pattern. And 'madrub' also has the meaning of 'darb' with the pattern 'maf'ul'. This is the meaning of their statement: 'the descriptor is a noun that indicates a vague essence and also a specific meaning subsisting in it.' This is what we clarified earlier. And he restricted it with the phrase 'with the derived pattern'—the restriction that he mentioned...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic classification (taqsim) of nouns (asma) in the context of usul al-fiqh, as presented in a commentary on al-Tawdih. The author begins by stating that there is a second complete division of words according to their coinage (wad'), and it is essential to know this division and the categories that arise from it. The division applies only to apparent nouns (ism zahir), excluding pronouns (damair) and demonstrative nouns (asma isharat). The first major split: if the noun's meaning is exactly that of its source (masdar) and it has a derived pattern, it is called a descriptor (sifah), like 'darib' from 'darb'. If not, then if the meaning is specific/determinate, it is a proper noun ('alam); otherwise it is a generic noun (ism jins). Both 'alam and ism jins can be derived or non-derived.

From the categories of sifah and ism jins, further divisions are made: if the meaning is intended without restriction, it is absolute (mutlaq); if with restriction, it is restricted (muqayyad). If all individuals are intended, it is general ('amm); if some individuals with specification, it is the known (ma'hud); if without specification, it is indefinite (nakira). The definitions of nakira and ma'rifa hinge on the listener's understanding at the time of utterance: nakira is for a non-specific thing, ma'rifa for a specific thing (from the listener's perspective). The example of 'rajul' shows that a word can be specific for the speaker but still be nakira if the listener does not know the individual.

The commentator then notes that 'absolute' is a type of 'specific' (khass) because it is coined for a single type. Crucially, these categories are not mutually exclusive in themselves; rather, they are distinguished by the aspect (haythiyat) under which they are considered. Some aspects are compatible (e.g., 'amm and mushtarak can coexist, as in the word 'ayn: it is mushtarak between 'eye' and 'spring', and when considering its meaning as 'spring', it is 'amm for all springs). But 'amm and khass under the same aspect cannot combine. The passage ends with a quotation from al-Talwih clarifying that 'apparent noun' excludes pronouns and demonstratives, and further refining the definition of sifah as a derived noun with a specific meaning and pattern.

Key Terms
النكرة (al-nakira): A noun coined for a non-specific thing; at utterance, it indicates non-specificity to the listener.
المعرفة (al-maʿrifa): A noun coined for a specific thing; at utterance, it indicates specificity to the listener.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines whether a noun is nakira or ma'rifa?
A) The speaker's intention at coinage.
B) The presence of the definite article.
C) The listener's understanding at the time of utterance.
D) The derived pattern of the noun.

Key Takeaway
The listener's perspective at utterance is the decisive factor in classifying nouns as nakira or ma'rifa in Hanafi usul.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
7 min
Compatibility of Categories: 'Amm, Khass, and Mushtarak
Discusses compatibility and contradiction of noun categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze how categories like 'amm, khass, and mushtarak can coexist or conflict under different aspects (haythiyat).

Core Idea
Categories can combine unless they are contradictory under the same aspect, e.g., 'amm and khass cannot, but 'amm and mushtarak can.

The passage discusses how the various noun categories interact. It emphasizes that contradictions are not inherent but arise only when the same aspect (haythiyat) is considered. Understanding this helps prevent misapplications in istinbat. We will explore the example of the word 'ayn and the general rules of compatibility.

Guided Path
1
Recall the principle of aspect (haythiyat)
The passage states that categories are not contradictory by nature (bil-dhat) but only by aspect (bil-haythiyat). Each noun can be considered under multiple aspects, leading to different classifications.
A single word can belong to several categories simultaneously under different aspects.
2
Analyze the example of 'ayn
The word 'ayn can be considered mushtarak (homonym) because it is coined for two different meanings: 'eye' and 'spring'. Alternatively, when considered as 'spring', it can be 'amm because it includes all springs. This shows that 'amm and mushtarak can coexist under different aspects.
Mushtarak is based on coinage, 'amm on the scope of a particular meaning.
3
Identify the impossible combination
The passage explicitly states that 'amm and khass cannot coexist under the same aspect. A word cannot be both general and specific regarding the same meaning. For example, 'al-rijal' (men) is 'amm for all men; it cannot be khass for a subset while remaining 'amm under the same aspect.
If a word is khass for a specific group, it is no longer 'amm for that group.
4
Apply to other categories
The passage says 'and similarly, consider the rest'. This implies the same principle applies to other pairs: e.g., mutlaq and muqayyad can coexist under different aspects? Actually, they are opposite under the same aspect, but may combine if different aspects are considered.
For instance, a word can be mutlaq in one context and muqayyad in another.
5
Understand the practical implication
When interpreting a legal text, one must identify which aspect is relevant. A word may be both 'amm and mushtarak, but only one meaning applies. The mujtahid must determine the intended aspect.
This is crucial in resolving apparent conflicts between texts.

معنی کے لحاظ جمیع افراد عیون الماء کو شامل ہے تو عام ہوگا تو واضح ہوا کہ عام و مشترک کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے لکن بين العام والخاص تناف لیکن خاص و عام کے درمیان منافات ہے اور یہ ممکن نہیں ہے کہ ایک لفظ ایک حیثیت سے خاص ہو اور دوسری حیثیت سے عام ہو ایسا ہونا ممکن نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح بواقی کا اعتبار کر لیا جائے خانہ سھل بعد الوقوف على الحدود التي ذكرنا فصل الخاص قال الشارح في التلويح قوله وايضاً الاسم الظاهر انا اسم کے ساتھ ظاہر کی قید لگا کر مضمر کو ان اقسام سے خارج کر دیا اور اسی طرح اسم اشارہ بھی خارج از اقسام ہے تو اسم ظاہر کہنے سے گویا کہ مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ اسم جو نہ مضمر ہو نہ اسم اشاره ـ والصفة بمقتضى هذا التقسيم تو اس تقسیم کے لحاظ سے صفہ اسم مشتق کا نام ہے جس کا معنی بعینہ وہی معنی ہو جو مشتق مز یعنی مصدر کا موضوع از معنی اور اس کے ساتھ وزن مشتق بھی ہو۔ فالضارب تو اس تعریف کے لحاظ سے ضارب ایسا لفظ ہے جو ضرب سے مشتق ہے اور اس کا معنی وہی ضرب والا معنی ہے اور ساتھ وزن فاعل بھی ملحوظ ہے جو وزن مشتق ہے اور مضروب بھی معنی ضرب کے ساتھ وزن مفعول بھی رکھتا ہے ۔ دھذا معنی قولهم الز یعنی ان کے قول کہ صفہ وہ اسم ہے جو ذات مہمہ پر دال ہو اور ایک معنی معین پر بھی جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہو یہی مراد ہے جو پہلے ہم نے واضح کردی ہے راحتر از بقوله مع وزن المشتق یعنی وزن مشتق پر ہونے کی جو قید کی ہے اس
The author said in al-Tawdih: Then here is another complete division of words according to coinage. This is the second division; knowledge of it and of the categories derived from it is necessary. And the apparent noun—the restriction of apparent noun excludes pronouns and demonstrative nouns. The resulting division is: The meaning and signification of the apparent noun, if it is exactly the meaning of the derived-from (i.e., the infinitive) and it also has one of the derived patterns, then it is called a descriptor (sifah). Otherwise, if the meaning is not exactly that of the derived-from—whether it has no derived-from at all (like 'amad?) or has a derived-from but the meaning is not identical, rather there is some difference—then if its meaning is specific and determinate, it is a proper noun ('alam); if it is not specific and determinate, it is a generic noun (ism jins). And proper noun and generic noun are sometimes derived and sometimes not derived. From the descriptor and generic noun: their intended meaning if it is intended without restriction is called absolute (mutlaq); if it is intended with some restriction, it is called restricted (muqayyad). Their individuals: if all individuals are intended, then it is general ('amm); if some individuals are intended, then if that some is determinate and intended, it is called the known (ma'hud); if some individuals are intended without specification (la 'ala al-ta'yin), then it is indefinite (nakira). So nakira is a noun coined for a thing unspecified. At the time of utterance for the listener, i.e., when it is uttered for the listener, it indicates something unspecified for the listener; that is called nakira. And ma'rifa is a noun coined for a thing specified at the time of utterance for the listener. And the reason I said 'at the time of utterance' is that at the time of coinage there is no difference between ma'rifa and nakira in specification and non-specification; rather this difference occurs at the time of utterance. And it is for the listener, so he also restricted it [to the listener], because when a speaker says 'rajulun came', it is possible that this 'rajul' is specified for the speaker but unspecified for the listener; then it is called nakira, even if it is specified for the speaker. So from this division, all the categories: descriptor, generic noun, proper noun, absolute, restricted, general, known, indefinite, and definite—all their definitions are learned from this division. Know that the absolute is among the types of specific (khass) because the absolute is coined for a single type, so it falls under the specific of the type. And know that in every category, one must consider the aspect (i'tibar haythiyat) so that distinction between them is maintained. From this it is understood that there is no intrinsic contradiction among these categories, rather [contradiction is] by aspects. Then some aspects are not contradictory with each other, and some are contradictory. They said in the commentary: 'And some categories may be combined...' i.e., some categories combine with others, and some do not combine with each other. Example: the statement 'the springs (al-uyun) broke forth'—the word 'ayn: if one considers that once it is coined for the seeing eye and another time for the spring of water, then it is considered homonymous (mushtarak). And if one considers that it is coined for the spring of water, then with respect to that meaning it includes all individuals of springs, so it is general ('amm). So it is clear that there is no contradiction between 'amm and mushtarak. But between 'amm and khass there is contradiction, and it is not possible for one word to be khass in one aspect and 'amm in another aspect; such is not possible. And similarly, consider the rest. It is easy after understanding the definitions we have mentioned. Chapter on the specific (fasl al-khass). The commentator said in al-Talwih: His statement 'and also the apparent noun'—he restricted it with 'apparent' to exclude pronouns from these categories, and similarly demonstrative nouns are excluded from the categories. So by saying 'apparent noun' it means the noun that is neither pronoun nor demonstrative. And 'descriptor' according to this division is the name of a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of the derived-from, i.e., the infinitive, and it also has the derived pattern. So 'al-darib' according to this definition is a word derived from 'daraba', and its meaning is exactly the meaning of 'darb', and it also has the pattern 'fa'il' which is a derived pattern. And 'madrub' also has the meaning of 'darb' with the pattern 'maf'ul'. This is the meaning of their statement: 'the descriptor is a noun that indicates a vague essence and also a specific meaning subsisting in it.' This is what we clarified earlier. And he restricted it with the phrase 'with the derived pattern'—the restriction that he mentioned...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic classification (taqsim) of nouns (asma) in the context of usul al-fiqh, as presented in a commentary on al-Tawdih. The author begins by stating that there is a second complete division of words according to their coinage (wad'), and it is essential to know this division and the categories that arise from it. The division applies only to apparent nouns (ism zahir), excluding pronouns (damair) and demonstrative nouns (asma isharat). The first major split: if the noun's meaning is exactly that of its source (masdar) and it has a derived pattern, it is called a descriptor (sifah), like 'darib' from 'darb'. If not, then if the meaning is specific/determinate, it is a proper noun ('alam); otherwise it is a generic noun (ism jins). Both 'alam and ism jins can be derived or non-derived.

From the categories of sifah and ism jins, further divisions are made: if the meaning is intended without restriction, it is absolute (mutlaq); if with restriction, it is restricted (muqayyad). If all individuals are intended, it is general ('amm); if some individuals with specification, it is the known (ma'hud); if without specification, it is indefinite (nakira). The definitions of nakira and ma'rifa hinge on the listener's understanding at the time of utterance: nakira is for a non-specific thing, ma'rifa for a specific thing (from the listener's perspective). The example of 'rajul' shows that a word can be specific for the speaker but still be nakira if the listener does not know the individual.

The commentator then notes that 'absolute' is a type of 'specific' (khass) because it is coined for a single type. Crucially, these categories are not mutually exclusive in themselves; rather, they are distinguished by the aspect (haythiyat) under which they are considered. Some aspects are compatible (e.g., 'amm and mushtarak can coexist, as in the word 'ayn: it is mushtarak between 'eye' and 'spring', and when considering its meaning as 'spring', it is 'amm for all springs). But 'amm and khass under the same aspect cannot combine. The passage ends with a quotation from al-Talwih clarifying that 'apparent noun' excludes pronouns and demonstratives, and further refining the definition of sifah as a derived noun with a specific meaning and pattern.

Key Terms
الحيثية (al-haythiyat): Aspect or perspective from which a noun is considered; different aspects yield different classifications.
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A homonym that has multiple unrelated meanings (e.g., 'ayn for eye and spring).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which pair of categories cannot coexist even under different aspects?
A) 'Amm and mushtarak
B) 'Amm and khass
C) Mutlaq and muqayyad
D) Nakira and ma'rifa

Key Takeaway
The categories 'amm and khass are mutually exclusive even under different aspects, while other pairs can combine under distinct aspects.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Principle of Consideration (Haysiyya) in Usul Categories
Explains that usul categories are defined by perspective, not essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between inherent and perspective-based contradictions among usul categories and classify words as ‘ām, khāṣṣ, muṭlaq, mushtarak based on their ḥaysiyya.

Core Idea
Usul categories coexist or conflict only by consideration, not by nature.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, words are classified into categories such as ‘ām (general), khāṣṣ (specific), muṭlaq (absolute), and mushtarak (homonym). These categories are not rigid labels but depend on the perspective (ḥaysiyya) from which the word is examined. The passage clarifies that there is no inherent incompatibility; rather, some categories can combine while others cannot. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly deriving rulings from textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usul categories
List the categories mentioned: ‘ām, khāṣṣ, muṭlaq, mushtarak. Note that muṭlaq is considered a type of khāṣṣ in Hanafi usul.
This comes from the passage's definition of muṭlaq as posited for a single type.
2
Understand ḥaysiyya (consideration)
Learn that each category is defined by a particular aspect or perspective. For example, ‘ām includes all individuals, khāṣṣ restricts, muṭlaq is for one type, mushtarak has multiple meanings. The same word can be classified differently under different considerations.
The passage emphasises that contradiction is based on ḥaysiyya.
3
Distinguish inherent vs. perspective contradiction
Some categories, like ‘ām and mushtarak, can coexist because they involve different ḥaysiyya. Others, like ‘ām and khāṣṣ, cannot coexist under the same ḥaysiyya because they are opposite.
The example of ‘ayn shows coexistence: mushtarak from multiple meanings, ‘ām from including all springs.
4
Apply the principle to the example of ‘ayn
Analyse the word ‘ayn: under one ḥaysiyya (multiple meanings) it is mushtarak; under another (all instances of one meaning) it is ‘ām. This proves compatibility.
The passage explicitly gives this example.
5
Generalise to other categories
The same logic applies to other combinations. For instance, muṭlaq and khāṣṣ are related, etc. The key is to identify the ḥaysiyya first.
The passage says 'and in this way the rest can be considered'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عام معہود . تکرہ اور معرفہ ان تمام کی تعریفات اس تقسیم سے معلوم ہوگئی ہیں ۔ داعلمان المطلق من اقسام الخاص کیونکہ مطلق کی وضع واحد نوعی کے لئے ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہ خاص النوع میں درج ہوگا۔ واعلم انه يجب في كل قسم آج یعنی ان تمام اقسام میں ہر ایک قسم کے ساتھ اعتبار حیثیت کیا جائیگا تاکہ ان کے مابین تمایز بر قرار رہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان اقسام کے اندر تنافی بالذات نہیں ہے بلکہ بالحیثیات ہے پھر بعض حیثیات ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ منافی نہیں ہیں اور بعض منافی ہیں سیاقی فی الشرح وبعض الاقسام قد يجتمع الخ یعنی بعض اقسام اور بعض کے ساتھ جمع ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اور بعض ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوتے مثل قوله جرت العيون لفظ عین بائیں حیثیت کہ ایک مرتبہ اس کی وضع باصرہ کے لئے اور مرة اخرمی اس کی وضع پانی کے چشمہ کے لئے ہے تو یہ مشترک قرار پائیگا اور اگر بائیں حیثیت ملحوظ کریں کہ اس کی وضع عین الماء کے لئے ہے تو اس معنی کے لحاظ جمیع افراد عیون الماء کو شامل ہے تو عام ہوگا تو واضح ہوا کہ عام و مشترک کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے لکن بين العام والخاص تناف لیکن خاص و عام کے درمیان منافات ہے اور یہ ممکن نہیں ہے کہ ایک لفظ ایک حیثیت سے خاص ہو اور دوسری حیثیت سے عام ہو ایسا ہونا ممکن نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح وبواقی کا اعتبار کر لیا جائے خانہ سھل بعد الوقوف على الحدود التي ذكرنا
The definitions of al-'am al-mahud, al-takrah, and al-ma'rifah are known from this division. Know that al-mutlaq is a type of al-khas because mutlaq is posited for a single type, so it falls within khas al-naw'. And know that in each division, a consideration (haysiyya) must be taken into account so that distinction between them is maintained. From this it is understood that there is no inherent contradiction between these divisions, but rather a contradiction in terms of consideration. Then some considerations are not contradictory with each other, and some are contradictory. As mentioned in the sharh: 'And some divisions may combine' i.e., some divisions combine with others, and some do not combine with each other. For example, the word 'ayn: if it is considered to be posited for the eye (bāsira) on one occasion and for a spring of water on another, then it is mushtarak. And if it is considered that it is posited for 'ayn al-ma' (spring of water), then by this meaning it includes all individuals of 'uyun al-ma', so it becomes 'am. So it is clear that there is no contradiction between 'am and mushtarak, but between 'am and khas there is contradiction. It is not possible for a word to be khas in one consideration and 'am in another consideration. And in this way the rest can be considered. It becomes easy after knowing the definitions that we mentioned.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage explains the relationship between different categories of words in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: 'am (general), khas (specific), mutlaq (absolute), mushtarak (ambiguous). The commentator clarifies that these categories are not inherently contradictory; rather, contradiction arises from the perspective (haysiyya) from which a word is considered. For example, the word 'ayn is mushtarak if it is considered to have multiple unrelated meanings (eye vs. spring), but 'am if considered for all instances of 'ayn al-ma'. 'Am and mushtarak can coexist in one word because they involve different considerations, but 'am and khas cannot because they are opposite categories from the same perspective. This principle helps in correctly classifying words and understanding their legal implications.

Key Terms
عام ('ām): A word that includes all individuals of its referent without restriction.
خاص (khāṣṣ): A word that is restricted to a specific individual or type.
مطلق (muṭlaq): A word that is posited for a single type without restriction to individuals.
مشترک (mushtarak): A word that has multiple distinct meanings, each posited separately.
حیثیت (ḥaysiyyah): The aspect or perspective from which a word is considered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, can the same word be classified as both ‘ām and mushtarak?
A) Yes, because they are not inherently contradictory.
B) No, because they are opposite categories.
C) Yes, but only if the word is used in a metaphorical sense.
D) No, because mushtarak requires multiple meanings.

Key Takeaway
Usul categories are not fixed labels; their compatibility depends on the perspective (ḥaysiyya) from which the word is considered.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Hanafi Definition of Sifat: Pattern and Meaning
Defining sifah and rebutting an objection about comprehensiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sifah, explain the role of derived patterns, and evaluate an objection regarding non-fa'il patterns.

Core Idea
A sifah must have both the meaning of its masdar and a derived pattern fa'il or maf'ul.

The definition of sifah (adjective) is crucial in Hanafi usul for identifying when a word is 'khas' (specific). This passage from al-Talwih refines the definition by addressing an objection that many adjectives use patterns other than fa'il and maf'ul, and shows that accepting those patterns would force inclusion of nouns of place and instrument, which are not sifah.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of sifah
Identify the three components: it is a noun, derived from a masdar, and carries both the meaning of the masdar and a specific derived pattern.
The definition is given in the opening: 'sifah is a derived noun whose meaning is that of the masdar and it has a derived pattern.'
2
Understand the purpose of the 'derived pattern' condition
It is used to exclude nouns of place, time, and instrument (like maqtal, miftah), which are derived but not adjectives.
These patterns (maf'al, mif'al) are not standard for expressing the doer or object.
3
Analyze the objection
The objector argues that many adjectives (e.g., abyad, afdal, atshan) are on other patterns (af'al, fu'lan, etc.) and are not covered by fa'il/maf'ul, making the definition insufficiently comprehensive.
The objector uses specific examples from the Arabic language.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The response uses a reductio: if we accept those patterns as valid for sifah, then we must also accept patterns like maf'al for nouns of place, which are not adjectives. The definition must exclude both or include both; since the latter is false, the former must hold.
This shows the definition is both comprehensive and restrictive when properly applied.
5
Apply the refined definition
Confirm that the standard for sifah is only patterns fa'il and maf'ul (and their feminine/plural forms). Other patterns are not considered sifah even if they describe attributes.
This is a firm principle in Hanafi usul for identifying khas.

Source Text

یہ ہے کہ وہ اسم جو نہ مضمر ہو نہ اسم اشاره ـ والصفة بمقتضى هذا التقسيم تو اس تقسیم کے لحاظ سے صفہ اسم مشتق کا نام ہے جس کا معنی بعینہ وہی معنی ہو جو مشتق مز یعنی مصدر کا موضوع از معنی اور اس کے ساتھ وزن المشتق یعنی وزن مشتق پر ہونے کی جو قید کی ہے اس سے مقصود اسم زمان اور مکان اور اسم آلہ سے احتراز کرنا مقصود ہے یہ صفہ میں درج نہیں ہیں اور اس جیسے اور مشتقات بھی اس سے خارج ہو جائیں گے مثلا مقتل جو اسم ظرف ہے اس کا معنی قتل مع المفعل نہیں ہے اور مفتاح اسم اگہ اس کا معنی بھی فتح مع المفعال نہیں ہے اذ التعبیر کیونکہ جس سے فعل صادر ہو اس کو تعبیر بالفاعل کرنا اور جس پر فعل واقع ہو اس کو تعبیر بالمفعول کرنا تو شائع ذائع ہے اور بخلاف مکان والہ کے ان کی تعبیر بالمفعول اور بالمفعال شائع نہیں ہے۔ ولقائل ان يقول صفہ کی تعریف میں مصنف کے قول مع وزن المشتق کی توجیہ کرتے ہوتے جو مع الفاعل والمفعول کی تخصیص کی ہے اسی پر یہ معترض کا اعتراض وارد کیا گیا ہے خلاصہ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ اس وقت یہ تعریف صفتہ جامع نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ یہ تفسیر صرف اس صفت پر صادق آسکتی ہے جو وزن فاعل یا وزن مفعول پر سو باقی اوصاف جوان اوزان پر نہیں میں صفات ہونے کے باوجود یہ تعریف ان پر صادق نہیں آئے گی کیونکہ جس کے ساتھ معنی مصدری قائم ہو اس سے تعبیر صرف بالفاعل یا بالمفعول کی جاتی ہے افعل ۔ فعلان۔ فعل مستفعل مفعلل وغیرہ سے نہیں کی جاتی حالانکہ یہ تمام صفات ہیں فلیس معنی الابیض دیکھئے کہ ابیض اور افضل کا معنی بیاض اور فضل مع الافعل نہیں ہے اور عطشان کا معنی عطش مع الفعلان اور خیر کا معنی خیریت مع الفعل اور مستخرج ومدحرج كا معنى استخراج مع المستفعل اور درجہ مع المفعلل نہیں ہے تو یہ تمام مصادیق صفتہ ہیں لیکن تعریف صیفہ انھیں شامل نہیں ہے دان منع ذلك یعنی اگر اس اعتراض کا جواب بالمنع دیا جائے کہ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ ان پر تعریف صفت صادق نہیں آتی کیونکہ ان کی تعبیر اسی طرح کی جائیگی یعنی مع الافعل اور مع الفلان وغیرہ کی جائیگی تو تمنع خروج اسم المكان الجد تو پھر ہم بھی یہ کہیں گے کہ تعریف صفہ سے اسم مکان اور اسم آلہ بھی خارج نہیں ہو سکتا بلکہ یہ صفت میں درج ہو جائیں گے حالانکہ یہ صفت نہیں ہے پھر تعریف مانع نہیں رہیگی ۔ للقطع بان القول یہ اسم مکان اور اسم آلہ کے عدم خروج کی سند پیش کر دی کہ یہ قبول کرنا اور کہنا کہ مقتل کا معنی قتل مع المفعل ہے تو یہ کوئی اس سے زیادہ بعید نہیں ہے جو یہ کہا جائے کہ ابیض کا معنی بیاض مع الانعل اور مد حرج کا معنی درجہ مع المفعلل ہے تو دونوں مشاوی میں اگر وہ خارج ہوتے ہیں تو یہ بھی خارج اگر وہ داخل ہیں تو پھر جمیع داخل ہیں ۔
Section on al-Khas. The commentator said in al-Talwih: His statement 'and also the apparent noun' — by adding the qualification 'apparent' to 'noun', he excludes the pronoun from these divisions. Similarly, the demonstrative noun is also excluded from the divisions. So by saying 'apparent noun', it means the noun that is neither a pronoun nor a demonstrative noun. And 'al-sifah' according to this division: based on this division, 'sifah' is the name of a derived noun whose meaning is precisely that of the derived from (i.e., the masdar) that is posited for the meaning, and along with that it has a derived pattern. So 'al-darib' according to this definition is a word that is derived from 'darb' and its meaning is the same as 'darb', and along with that the pattern 'fa'il' is observed, which is a derived pattern. And 'madrub' also has the meaning of 'darb' along with the pattern 'maf'ul'. This is the meaning of their statement that 'al-sifah' is a noun that indicates an indefinite essence and a specific meaning that is established in it. This is what we have clarified. And the purpose of his restriction 'with the derived pattern' is to exclude nouns of time, place, and instrument. These are not included in sifah, and similar other derivatives are also excluded. For example, 'maqtal' which is a noun of place—its meaning is not 'qatl with maf'al', and 'miftah' a noun of instrument—its meaning is not 'fath with mif'al'. Because expression: it is well-known to express the one from whom the action emanates with fa'il, and the one on whom the action falls with maf'ul. But for place and instrument, their expression with maf'ul and mif'al is not well-known. And someone may say: In the definition of sifah, the author's statement 'with the derived pattern' is explained by restricting it to patterns fa'il and maf'ul. On this, an objector raises an objection. The summary of the objection: This definition would not be comprehensive, because this explanation only applies to sifah that is on the pattern fa'il or maf'ul. The remaining adjectives that are on other patterns, despite being adjectives, this definition would not apply to them. Because the one with which the masdar meaning is established is expressed only with fa'il or maf'ul, not with af'al, fu'lan, fa'l, mustaf'il, mufa''il, etc., while all of these are adjectives. Indeed, the meaning of 'al-abyad' — see that the meaning of 'abyad' and 'afdal' is not 'bayad' with af'al; and 'atshan' is not 'atsh' with fu'lan; and 'khayr' is not 'khayriyyah' with fa'l; and 'mustakhraj' and 'mudahraj' are not 'istikhraj' with mustaf'il and 'darajah' with mufa''il. So all these are instances of sifah, but the definition of sifah does not include them. Then if we reply by denial: 'We do not accept that the definition does not apply to them, because they can be expressed similarly, i.e., with af'al, fu'lan, etc.,' then the objector would say: 'Then the exclusion of the noun of place and instrument would be denied. We would then say that the definition of sifah cannot exclude them; rather they would be included in sifah, while they are not sifah. Then the definition would not be restrictive.' For it is certain that the statement that the noun of place and instrument are not excluded — if one accepts and says that 'maqtal' means 'qatl with maf'al', then this is no more far-fetched than saying that 'abyad' means 'bayad with af'al' and 'mudahraj' means 'darajah with mufa''il'. So both are equal: if those are excluded, then these are also excluded; if those are included, then all are included.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage defines 'sifah' (adjective) in Hanafi usul and addresses an objection. The definition given by the author of al-Tawdih, as explained by the commentator in al-Talwih, is that a sifah is a derived noun (ism mushtaq) that has both the meaning of the masdar (root) and a derived pattern (wazn mushtaq). Examples: al-darib (fa'il) and al-madrub (maf'ul). The restriction to 'derived pattern' is to exclude nouns of place (ism al-makan), time (ism al-zaman), and instrument (ism al-alah), which are not considered adjectives. The objector argues that many adjectives are on other patterns (e.g., af'al, fu'lan) and are not included, so the definition is not comprehensive. The response is: if we accept that those patterns can be expressed similarly (i.e., considered as having their own derived patterns), then it would also force the inclusion of nouns of place and instrument, which are not adjectives. Thus, both the objector's examples and the excluded nouns must be treated consistently: either both are excluded (by not considering them as having the required pattern) or both are included. The commentator implies that the intended definition is only for patterns fa'il and maf'ul, which are the standard for expressing the doer and the object.

Key Terms
صفت (ṣifah): A derived noun that indicates an indefinite essence and a specific meaning established in it, and is on a derived pattern like fa'il or maf'ul.
اسم ظاهر (ism ẓāhir): An apparent noun that is not a pronoun or demonstrative noun.
وزن مشتق (wazn mushtaq): A derived pattern such as fa'il or maf'ul that indicates the doer or the object of an action.
فاعل (fāʿil): The pattern for the doer of an action, e.g., ضارب (one who hits).
مفعول (mafʿūl): The pattern for the object of an action, e.g., مضروب (one who is hit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi definition of sifah exclude the word 'مقتل' (maqtal)?
A) Because it is not derived from a masdar.
B) Because it indicates an action rather than a meaning.
C) Because its pattern is maf'al, which is for nouns of place, not for sifah.
D) Because it is not used in legal texts.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a sifah must have the masdar meaning and the specific patterns fa'il or maf'ul; nouns of place, time, and instrument are excluded despite being derived.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Defining Sifah: Scope and Responses to Objections
Commentary on sifah definition with objection and two responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of sifah to identify which derived patterns qualify as attributes and evaluate the two responses to the objection about its comprehensiveness.

Core Idea
Sifah includes all derived patterns with a masdar meaning and a form, not just fāʿil and mafʿūl.

This passage tackles a critical objection to the definition of sifah: that it is too narrow to cover common attribute patterns like afʿal (e.g., abyad) and fuʿlān (e.g., ʿatshān). The commentator offers two nuanced responses, clarifying that 'weight of the derivative' refers either to the general derived form or to the genus of derivation. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to apply the definition consistently across all attribute types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Pinpoint the objector's claim: the definition as interpreted (patterns fāʿil and mafʿūl only) fails to include many genuine attributes like abyad, afḍal, ʿatshān, etc.
The objector assumes the author meant only these two weights.
2
Analyze the first response
Understand that 'weight of the derivative' can mean the general derived form (hayʾah mushtaqqah), which includes any pattern that carries a masdar meaning and a form. This makes the definition comprehensive but risks including ism makān/zamān/ālāt.
The author accepts that risk; he may consider those as attributes (contrary to jumhūr).
3
Analyze the second response
See that 'weight of the derivative' refers to the genus of derivation (jins al-ishtiqāq), i.e., patterns common among attributes (fāʿil, mafʿūl, afʿal, fuʿlān, etc.) but not those specific to place/time/instrument (mafʿal, mifʿāl). This excludes non-attribute nouns cleanly.
This response preserves the exclusion of ism makān etc. without exception.
4
Distinguish derived vs. jamid nouns
Recognize that ism jins can be derived (e.g., Ḥātim from ḥatm, maktal from qatala) or jamid (e.g., Zayd, rajul). The term ḍārib cannot exemplify derived ism jins because it is a ṣifah, not an ism jins.
Ṣifah and ism jins are mutually exclusive categories in this context.
5
Grasp the cognitive definition of ishtiqāq
The cognitive (ʿilmī) definition: finding proportionality (tanāsub) between two words in original meaning and letters, and referring one to the other. This is a conceptual understanding, not practical derivation.
This contrasts with taṣrīfī (practical) derivation used in sarf.

لیتا ہے ۔ ثانياً اصل سوال کا جواب یہ بھی پیش کیا جاتا ہے کہ وزن مشتق سے مراد و زن جنس سحق ہے اسی مشتق کان تو جمیع صفات از جنس اسم الفاعل والمفعول میں بخلاف زمان و مکان اور اسم آلہ کے کہ ان کے اوزان از جنس صفات مشتقہ نہیں ہیں ۔ قولہ دھما ای العلم الخ یعنی اور اسم جنس یا تو مشتق ہوں گے جیسے حاتم علم ہو کر مشتق ہے اور مقتل اسم جنس ہو کر شقق ہے ولا يصح التمثیل ضارب کے ساتھ مثال دینا صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ صفت ہے اور مصنف نے صفتہ کو اسم جنس کا قسیم اور مقابل قرار دیا ہے لہذا ضارب اسم جنس مشتق کی تمثیل نہیں ہو سکتی ادرا یعنی علم اور اسم جنس یا مشتق نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ جامد ہوں گے علم جیسے زید اور اسم جنس جیسے رجبل یہ دونوں جامد ہیں ۔ والاشتقاق یفسر اشتقاق کی دو تفسیریں ہیں ایک علمی یعنی صرف اس تعریف سے علم ہو گا لیکن تصرف اور عمل نہیں ہوگا تو یہ تعریف علمی یوں پیش کی جاتی ہے ان تجد بين اللفظين تناسب یعنی دو لفظوں کے درمیان اصل معنی اور حروف ترکیبیہ میں تناسب پالیں اورمحسوس کرلیں اور علمی درجہ میں ایک کو دوسرے کی طرف رد کریں تو جس کو رد کر رہے ہیں یہ مشتق ہے اور جس کی طرف رد کیا گیا ہے وہ مشتق منہ ہے تو یہ صرف علمی حدتک ہے اس
From 'سے مقصود' ['satisfy'?] is intended to exclude ism zaman and ism makan and ism alat. These are not included in sifah, and other derivatives like them will also be excluded from it. For example, maktal, which is ism zarf, its meaning is not 'qatl with al-muf'al', and miftah, ism alat, its meaning is not 'fath with al-mif'al'. Because the expression: that from which the action emanates is expressed by al-fa'il, and that on which the action occurs is expressed by al-maf'ul, this is well-known and common. Unlike makān and ālah, their expression by al-maf'ul and al-mif'al is not common. And one could say: In the definition of sifah, the author's statement 'with the weight of the derivative' is interpreted as he specified with al-fā'il and al-maf'ūl. Upon this the objector's objection is raised. Summary of objection: Then this definition of sifah will not be comprehensive, because this interpretation applies only to that sifah which is on the pattern of fā'il or maf'ūl. So the remaining attributes that are not on these patterns, despite being attributes, this definition will not apply to them, because that with which the meaning of the masdar is associated is expressed only by al-fā'il or al-maf'ūl, not by af'al, fu'lan, fi'l, mustaf'il, mufa'll, etc., although all these are attributes. For example, the meaning of al-abyad is not bayād with al-af'al, and al-afdal is not fadl with al-af'al, and 'atshān is not 'atash with al-fu'lān, and khayr is not khayriyyah with al-fi'l, and mustakhraj and mudahraj are not istikhraj with al-mustaf'il and darajah with al-mufa'll. So all these are instances of sifah, but the definition of sifah does not include them. If one denies that, i.e., if the objection is answered by denial that we do not accept that the definition does not apply to them, because they will be expressed similarly, i.e., with al-af'al and al-fu'lān etc., then you prevent the exclusion of ism makān from the definition. Then we too would say that ism makān and ism ālāt are not excluded from the definition of sifah, rather they would be included in sifah, although they are not sifah. Then the definition would not be restrictive. For the definitive statement is that this is the proof for the non-exclusion of ism makān and ism ālāt, that to accept this and to say that the meaning of maktal is 'qatl with al-muf'al' is not more far-fetched than to say that the meaning of abyad is 'bayād with al-af'al' and mudahraj is 'darajah with al-mufa'll'. So both are similar: if those are excluded, these are also excluded; if those are included, then all are included. The answer to the objection has been given in two ways: Firstly, that by 'weight of the derivative' is not meant only the weight of fā'il and maf'ūl, as the commentator took it. Rather, by it is meant the form (hay'ah). Now the meaning will be that a manifest noun, when its meaning is not exactly what it was placed for, i.e., it is derived, and it has the weight of a derivative, i.e., a derivative form — in short, that it contains both matter (mādah) and form (sūrah) included in that for which it is placed — then the word 'with' (ma'a) pertains to the placement (wad'), and the weight of the derivative is concurrent with the derivative source in placement, and it is part of the placed-for. And this definition applies to all attributes, because in every attribute at the time of placement, just as the meaning of the masdar is considered, similarly its form is also considered, whether it is the form of fā'il or af'al, fu'lān, mufa'll, mustaf'il. In any case, by 'weight' is not meant the specificity of the weight of fā'il, but rather the general derivative form. But then the question arises: then ism makān and zamān and ism ālāt would also be included in sifah, because they also have a masdar meaning with a form considered. However, the majority (jumhūr) do not include them in sifah. So in answer to this question it is said that according to the author they are included in sifah, and the author in a research context adopts a position opposing the majority. Secondly, the original question is also answered as: by 'weight of the derivative' is meant the weight of the genus of derivation (jins al-ishtiqāq). So all attributes are of the genus of ism al-fā'il and ism al-maf'ūl, unlike ism zamān, makān, and ālāt, whose weights are not of the genus of derived attributes. His statement: 'dahmā' i.e., al-alam etc.: that ism jins either will be derived, like Hātim is a proper noun and derived, and maktal is a common noun and derived. And it is not correct to give ضارب as an example, because it is a sifah, and the author made sifah a counterpart and opposite of ism jins. Therefore, ضارب cannot be an example of a derived ism jins. 'Idrā': i.e., a proper noun and ism jins either are not derived, rather are jamid (solid). An proper noun like Zayd and a common noun like rajul — both are jamid. And al-ishtiqāq is interpreted in two ways: one is 'ilmī (cognitive), i.e., only knowledge will be gained from this definition, but no tasarruf (derivational manipulation) or 'amal. So this cognitive definition is presented as: 'an tajida bayna al-lafẓayni tanāsub' — that you find between the two words proportionality in original meaning and compositional letters, and you sense it, and in a cognitive manner you refer one to the other. Then that which you are referring is the derivative (mushtaq) and that to which it is referred is the derivative source (mushtaq minhu). This is only to the extent of knowledge.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of sifah (adjective/attribute) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author is responding to an objection that the definition given by the matn author (al-Musannif) is too narrow because it interprets 'weight of the derivative' (wazn al-mushtaq) as only the patterns fa'il and maf'ul, thus excluding other common attribute patterns like af'al (e.g., abyad), fu'lan (e.g., 'atshan), fi'l (e.g., khayr), mustaf'il, and mufa'll. The objector argues that these are genuine attributes yet they are not covered by the definition. The commentator then presents two responses. First, 'weight of the derivative' does not refer to specific patterns but to the general derived form (hay'ah mushtaqqah). Under this interpretation, all attributes are included because each has a form and a masdar meaning. However, this would also include ism makan, ism zaman, ism alat (place, time, instrument nouns) which the majority do not consider attributes. The commentator notes that the matn author himself may consider them attributes, diverging from the majority. The second response is that 'weight of the derivative' means the genus of derivation (jins al-ishtiqaq), i.e., patterns that are common among attributes (like fa'il, maf'ul, af'al, etc.) but not those specific to place/time/instrument (like maf'al, mif'al). Thus, the definition properly excludes those non-attribute nouns. Then the text moves to discussing ism jins (common noun) and whether it can be derived or jamid (solid). Examples are given: the proper noun Hatim is derived from 'hatm' (to break), while the common noun maktal is derived from 'qatala'. However, ضارب cannot serve as an example of derived ism jins because it is a sifah, not an ism jins. Finally, the definition of ishtiqaq is given in a cognitive sense: finding proportionality (tanasub) between two words in original meaning and letters, and referring one to the other. This is a purely conceptual understanding without practical derivation.

Key Terms
الصفة (al-sifah): A word that conveys a meaning along with a derived pattern that is not exactly the masdar itself, but rather a form that indicates an attribute.
الاشتقاق (al-ishtiqāq): Finding proportionality (tanāsub) between two words in original meaning and compositional letters, and referring one to the other (cognitive definition).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the advantage of the second response (jins al-ishtiqāq) over the first (hayʾah mushtaqqah)?
A) It includes ism makān and ism ālāt as attributes.
B) It excludes ism makān and ism ālāt from the definition of sifah.
C) It restricts sifah to only the patterns fāʿil and mafʿūl.
D) It eliminates the need for a masdar meaning.

Key Takeaway
The definition of sifah in Hanafi usul is not limited to fāʿil and mafʿūl but encompasses all derived patterns as long as they have a masdar meaning and a form, with the exclusion of place/time/instrument nouns achieved through the genus of derivation.

Two Responses to the Objection on the Definition of Mushtaqq
Defends the definition of mushtaqq via two responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi responses to the objection on the definition of mushtaqq and apply them to classify words as sifāt.

Core Idea
The definition of mushtaqq requires both meaning and form; 'wazn' can be general or restricted to attribute patterns.

This passage defends the definition of mushtaqq by addressing an objection that the term 'wazn mushtaqq' might be too narrow or too broad. The commentator provides two distinct answers, each clarifying the role of form and meaning in determining derived words that count as attributes in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the criticism against defining mushtaqq as 'ism zahir whose meaning is not exactly what it was placed for and has a derivative weight'?
The objection likely concerns the scope of 'wazn mushtaqq'.
2
Analyze the first response
The commentator argues that 'wazn' means general form (hay'ah), including all derivative patterns like fāʿil, afʿal, fuʿlan, mufaʿʿil, mustafʿil, etc. This makes the definition cover all attributes.
This response includes nouns of place/time/instrument, which the author accepts.
3
Examine the counter-objection
If form is general, nouns like مَضْرَب (place of hitting) and مِفْتَاح (key) would also be attributes, but the majority excludes them.
The author takes a research stance, accepting them as attributes.
4
Understand the second response
Alternatively, 'wazn' is restricted to patterns common to attributes (e.g., fāʿil, mafʿūl). Patterns for time/place/instrument are different, so they are excluded.
This preserves the majority view.
5
Apply the thamarah
The practical consequence in usul is which words qualify as sifāt for principles like 'umūm and khūṣūṣ.
Both responses are valid within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب اعتراض دو طرح سے دیا گیا ہے اولاً یہ کہ وزن مشتق سے مراد صرف وزن فاعل اور مفعول نہیں ہے جیسے شارح نے مراد لیا ہے بلکہ اس سے مراد ہیتہ ہے اب معنی یہ یہ ہوگا کہ اسم ظاہر جب اس کا معنی عین ما وضع نہ ہو یعنی مشتق منہ اور وزن مشتق ہو یعنی ہیبہ مشتق خلاصہ یہ کہ اس کے اندر مادہ اور صورۃ دونوں درج فی الموضوع لہ ہیں اس وقت مع کا لفظ متعلق بالوضع ہوگا اور وزن مشتق مقارن مع المشتق منه في الوضع ہو اور سیر جزء موضوع لہ ہو اور یہ تعریف جمیع صفات پر صادق آئیگی کیونکہ ہر صفہ میں بوقت وضع جیسے معنی مصدر معتبر ہوتا ہے اسی طرح اس میں ہیتہ کا اعتبار بھی ہوتا ہے خواہ وہ مہینہ فاعل ہو یا افعل و فعلان یا مفعلل و مستفعل بہر حال وزن سے مراد وزن فاعل کی خصوصیتہ نہ ہوئی بلکہ عام میتہ مشتق ہوئی لیکن اس وقت سوال یہ ہوگا کہ پھر اسم مکان و زمان اور اسم آلہ بھی داخل فی الصفة ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ ان کے اندر بھی معنی مصدری کے ساتھ ہیٹہ بھی معتبر ہے حالانکہ جمہور اس کو صفت میں درج نہیں کرتے تو اس سوال کا جواب میں کہا جاتا ہے کہ مصنف کے نزدیک یہ داخل فی الصفہ ہیں اور مصنف مقام تحقیق میں جمہور کا خلاف اختیار کر لیتا ہے ۔ ثانياً اصل سوال کا جواب یہ بھی پیش کیا جاتا ہے کہ وزن مشتق سے مراد و زن جنس سحق ہے اسی مشتق کان تو جمیع صفات از جنس اسم الفاعل والمفعول میں بخلاف زمان و مکان اور اسم آلہ کے کہ ان کے اوزان از جنس صفات مشتقہ نہیں ہیں ۔
The answer to the objection is given in two ways: First, that by 'derived weight' is not meant only the weight of fa'il and maf'ul as the commentator intended, but rather the form is meant. So the meaning becomes: a common noun (ism zahir) when its meaning is not exactly what it was placed for (i.e., the origin of derivation) and it has a derivative weight (i.e., the form is derived). In summary, both matter and form are included in its subject matter. In that case, the word 'with' relates to the act of placing, and the derivative weight is concurrent with the origin of derivation in the act of placing, and the form is part of the subject matter. This definition applies to all attributes because in every attribute at the time of placing, just as the meaning of the infinitive is considered, similarly its form is also considered, whether it is the pattern of fa'il, af‘al, fu‘lan, mufa‘‘il, or mustaf‘il. In any case, by 'weight' is not meant specifically the weight of fa'il, but the general derivative form. But then a question arises: then nouns of place and time and nouns of instrument would also be included in the category of attributes, because in them also both the infinitive meaning and the form are considered, although the majority do not include them in attributes. So in answer to this question it is said that according to the author they are included in attributes, and the author in a research context may adopt a view contrary to the majority. Second, another answer to the original objection is also presented: that by 'derived weight' is meant the weight of the generic root of derivation. All attributes are from the class of ism al-fa‘il and ism al-maf‘ul, unlike nouns of place, time, and instrument whose weights are not from the class of derived attributes.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection regarding the definition of mushtaqq (derived word) as it relates to attributes (sifāt). The objection concerned the meaning of 'wazn mushtaqq' (derived weight/form). The commentator provides two answers. First, that 'weight' here refers to the general form (hay'ah) of the word, not just the patterns fāʿil and mafʿūl. This allows all derived forms to be included. An objection arises that nouns of place/time/ instrument then become attributes, but the author (al-Musannif) accepts that. The second answer restricts 'weight' to patterns common to attributes like fāʿil and mafʿūl, excluding other patterns. Both answers aim to keep the definition precise and consistent within Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
وزن مشتق (wazn mushtaqq): The morphological pattern of a derived word, referring to either the specific pattern of fāʿil/mafʿūl or the general form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The root letters only
D) The meaning of the infinitive

Key Takeaway
The definition of mushtaqq requires both meaning and form, and the scope of derivative forms determines which words count as attributes in Hanafi usul.
