The Certainty of the General and Refutation of Shafi'i Objections
Defending the Hanafī view that ʿāmm is qatʿī and responding to Shāfiʿī arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi proof for the certainty of 'amm and evaluate the Shafi'i counterarguments using the concepts of ta'kid, takhsis, and wad'.

Core Idea
The general (ʿāmm) is certain unless evidence-based specification intervenes.

In Usul al-Fiqh, the status of general texts (ʿāmm) is a major point of divergence between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafis hold that ʿāmm is qatʿī (definitive) in its indication over all individuals unless a valid evidence for specification (takhṣīṣ) arises. The Shafiʿis consider ʿāmm to be ẓannī (speculative), opening it to specification more readily. This passage defends the Hanafi view with detailed rational arguments, addressing the use of emphasis (taʾkīd), the nature of probabilities, and the alleged widespread occurrence of takhṣīṣ. Understanding this dispute is foundational for interpreting legal texts in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Recognize that the debate is about whether 'amm is qat'i or zanni when no evidence for takhsis is present. The Hanafis affirm qat'i; the Shafi'is argue it remains zanni due to widespread takhsis.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof from wad' and ta'kid
Understand that the wad' (linguistic placement) of 'amm is for all individuals. Ta'kid with 'kull' or 'ajma' does not indicate deficiency but reinforces the general to reach muḥkam, removing only probabilities not based on evidence.
3
Examine the Shafi'i counterargument and Hanafi response
The Shafi'is claim that frequent takhsis in Shari'ah causes doubt. The Hanafis respond by distinguishing takhsis that creates doubt (connected independent statement, rare) from other specifiers (aql, hiss, separate naskh) that do not. Thus, the claim of widespread doubt-inducing takhsis is unfounded.
4
Address the argument of multiple probabilities
An opponent argues that 'amm has more probabilities (figurative and specification) than khass, making it weaker. The Hanafis respond that specification is itself figurative, so both are similar; multiplicity of probabilities without qarinah does not reduce certainty, as shown by equality of specific terms with differing figurative probabilities.
5
Apply the practical consequence
When a khass and an 'amm conflict and the chronology is unknown, Hanafis treat them as contemporary (hammalah 'ala al-muqaranah), requiring reconciliation or preference based on other criteria. Shafi'is specify the 'amm with the khass, resolving the conflict because 'amm is zanni. This shows the real-world impact of the disagreement.

Source Text

ہو، تو یہ دونوں لفظ خاص اپنے اپنے معنی حقیقی پر دلالت کرنے میں مساوی ہیں، اول کو ترجیح علی الثانی حاصل نہیں ہوگی بلکہ دونوں برابر درجہ کے قطعی ہوں گے۔ تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجاز واحد کا احتمال جس کے لئے قرینہ نہ ہو بالکل مساوی فی الدلالت ہے اس کے ساتھ جہاں بلا قرینہ مجازات کثیرہ کے احتمالات ہوں، تو ثابت ہوا کہ عام اگرچہ اس کے اندر احتمالات کثیرہ ہو سکتے ہیں یہ مساوی للخاص ہو گا جس کے اندر احتمال واحد ہو سکتا ہے۔ ولا نسلم ان التخصیص شافع کی جانب سے جو یہ کہا گیا تھا کہ عام میں تخصیص شائع ذائع ہے لہذا یہ مورث شبهہ ہوگی، یہ اس کا جواب ہے کہ ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے کہ تخصیص جو مورث شبہ ہو سکتی ہے وہ عام میں بلا قرینہ شائع ذائع ہے۔ اور تخصیص مورث شبهہ وہ ہوتی ہے جو کلام مستقل موصول بالعام کے ساتھ ہو، اس قسم کی تخصیص بالکل قلیل اور نادر ہے۔ کیونکہ حال المخصص یعنی مخصص اگر عقل ہے یا اس جیسی چیز مثلا حس، فھو في حكم الاستثناء، تو یہ حکم استثنا ہے جیسے استثنا مابقی میں شبہ پیدا نہیں کرتا یہ بھی ایسے ہوگا، کیونکہ عقل جن کے عدم دخول کا موجب ہوگا وہ داخل نہیں ہوں گے اور اس کے ماسویٰ تحت العام قطعا داخل رہیں گے۔ وإن كان المخصص هو الكلام، مخصص اگر کلام ہے، اگر وہ متراخیا واقع ہے تو وہ ناسخ ہے، مخصص نہیں ہے، البتہ وہ مخصص جو مورث شبہ ہو سکتا ہے وہ صرف وہی ہے جو کلام مستقل ہو اور ہو موصولاً، اور اس قسم کا مخصص بالکل قلیل ہے۔ آپ کا کثیر اور شائع کہنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ فإذا ثبت هذا جب یہ ثابت ہوا کہ عام ہمارے نزدیک قطعی ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک قطعی نہیں ہے، تو خان تعارض الخاص والعام اگر خاص عام میں تعارض ہو جائے کہ ایک ثبوت حکم پر دال ہو دوسرا اسی حکم کی نفی پر، وإن لم يعلم التاریخ یعنی ہمیں ان کی تاریخ وقوع کا علم نہیں کہ ان میں سے کون مقدم فی الوقوع ہے اور کون مؤخر، تو ہم انھیں مقارنتہ پر محمول کریں گے اگرچہ نفس الامر میں ان دونوں میں سے کوئی متاخر ضرور ہو گا جو وہ ناسخ للمتقدم ہو گا، چونکہ ہمیں تاریخ معلوم نہیں ہے لہذا ان دونوں کو محمول على المقارنہ کیا جائیگا تاکہ کسی کی تقدیم و تاخیر سے ترجیح بلا مرجع لازم نہ آئے۔ فعند الشافعی امام شافعی کے نزدیک چونکہ عام قطعی نہیں ہے لہذا اس خاص کے ساتھ عام کی تخصیص کرلی جائے گی اور تعارض قائم نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ متعارضین میں متساوی فی الدرجہ ہونا شرط ہے۔
In this, there is no difference in the proof of the named thing, because this probability is baseless without evidence, so from this type of probability, there will be no difference in the certainty of the general. So the emphasis makes it muhkam. This is a response to the arguments of the opponents. The summary is that those who held to suspension (al-wāqifiyya) who were murderers by suspension, they presented in their argument that the emphasis of the general which is done with 'kull' and 'ajma' shows that the general in itself is not inclusive of all individuals. In response, it is said that emphasis with 'kull' is done so that the general becomes muhkam, i.e., the general had no probability arising from evidence, but there could be a probability not arising from evidence, so with emphasis, every type of probability is repelled and it reaches the level of muhkam. And also a response to what al-Shāfiʿī said, i.e., a response to his statement regarding specification. The gist is that we do not claim that there is absolutely no probability of specification in the general, neither one arising from evidence nor one not arising; rather we hold that the probability of specification arising from evidence does not exist. As for that not arising from evidence, which is not contrary to certainty, we do not claim its negation. For the negation of that not arising from evidence, emphasis with 'kull' and 'ajma' is done so that it becomes muhkam. This is understood just as a specific term (khāṣṣ) is absolutely certain but within it there is a probability of figurative usage; to repel that probability, emphasis with the word 'nafs' and 'ayn' is done. It is said 'Jā'ani Zaydun nafsuhu wa ʿaynuhu' so that the probability of figurative usage is repelled. Just as with this emphasis, there is no difference in the certainty of the specific, similarly with the emphasis of 'kull' and 'ajma', there will be no difference in the certainty of the general. If it is said: the probability of figurative usage... The summary of the question is that the general cannot be equal to the specific in certainty, because in the specific there is only a probability of figurative usage, and in the general there is this same probability of figurative usage and also another probability, i.e., probability of specification, so in the specific there is one probability and in the general there are two. Thus the specific is preponderant, so the specific achieves precedence over the general, so the specific is at the level of naṣṣ and the general is at the level of ẓāhir. Naṣṣ has precedence over ẓāhir. We say: Since the general's linguistic usage is for all named things, intending some and not others, which you call specification, that too is figurative. So the result is that in the specific there is one probability of figurative usage, and in the general there are two probabilities of figurative usage, and multiplicity of probabilities has no consideration. Observe: if there is a specific term, when one specific term has only one figurative meaning and another specific term has two or more figurative meanings, and no qarīnah exists for any of them, then these two specific terms are equal in indicating their real meanings. One will not have preponderance over the other; rather both will be of equal degree and certain. So it is known that the probability of a single figurative usage without qarīnah is completely equal in indication with it where there are probabilities of multiple figurative usages without qarīnah. So it is established that the general, even though it may have multiple probabilities within it, is equal to the specific which may have a single probability. And we do not concede that specification is widespread and common in the general, as was said by the Shāfiʿī side, hence it would cause doubt. This is its response: we do not concede that specification which can cause doubt is widespread and common in the general without qarīnah. And specification that causes doubt is that which is with an independent statement connected to the general. This type of specification is extremely rare and scarce. Because the case of the specifying agent (al-mukhaṣṣiṣ) – if it is intellect or something similar like sense, then it is like the ruling of exception. So this is the ruling of exception, just as exception in what remains does not create doubt, this will also be like it, because what intellect necessitates to be excluded will not be included, and everything else will definitely be included under the general. And if the specifying agent is speech, if it occurs separately then it is an abrogator (nāsikh), not a specifier. However, the specifier that can cause doubt is only that which is an independent statement and is connected, and this type of specifier is extremely rare. Your saying that it is abundant and widespread is not correct. So when this is established, that the general for us is certain and for Imām al-Shāfiʿī it is not certain, then in the case of conflict between the specific and the general, if a specific and general conflict such that one indicates the affirmation of a ruling and the other the negation of that same ruling, and the history is not known, i.e., we do not know which of them occurred earlier and which later, then we will treat them as contemporary, even though in reality one of them must be later and would be the abrogator of the earlier. Since we do not know the date, we will treat them as contemporary to avoid preponderance without basis arising from giving precedence or delay. According to al-Shāfiʿī, since the general is not certain, therefore the general will be specified by the specific, and conflict does not arise because for conflicting evidences, equality in degree is a condition.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a deep defense of the Hanafī position that ʿāmm (general) is qaṭʿī (definitive) in its indication over all its individuals, unless there is evidence for takhṣīṣ (specification). The author begins by rejecting a claim from the Wāqifiyya (probably those who suspended judgment) who argued that the use of taʾkīd (emphasis) with 'kull' or 'ajma' shows that ʿāmm is not inherently all-inclusive. The Hanafī response is that taʾkīd is meant to elevate ʿāmm to the level of muḥkam (firm, unambiguous), removing any probability that does not arise from evidence. The text then addresses Imām al-Shāfiʿī's view that ʿāmm is ẓannī (speculative) due to the widespread occurrence of takhṣīṣ. The Hanafī response clarifies that they do not deny the possibility of takhṣīṣ, but only takhṣīṣ that arises from evidence; probabilities without evidence do not affect certainty. Emphasis with 'kull' and 'ajma' is like emphasis with 'nafs' and 'ayn' for khāṣṣ (specific): it strengthens the real meaning and repels figurative probability. The passage then tackles an objection that ʿāmm cannot be equal to khāṣṣ in certainty because ʿāmm has two probabilities (figurative and specification). The Hanafī answer is that specification itself is figurative, so both are probabilities of the same type; multiplicity of probabilities does not reduce certainty when no qarīnah (contextual indicator) exists. A comparison is made: two khāṣṣ terms with different numbers of figurative probabilities are equal in certainty if no qarīnah tilts one. Similarly, ʿāmm with many probabilities is still equal to khāṣṣ with one. Next, the assertion that takhṣīṣ is widespread is rejected. The author distinguishes takhṣīṣ that causes doubt (connected independent statement) from types that do not (intellect, sense, separate abrogating text). Connected independent statements are rare, so the Hanafī position stands. Finally, the practical consequence: if a khāṣṣ and ʿāmm apparently conflict and the chronology is unknown, Hanafīs treat them as contemporary and reconcile (or give precedence based on other criteria? Actually the text says they are treated as contemporary to avoid arbitrary preference; the Shāfiʿī school, considering ʿāmm as ẓannī, would specify the ʿāmm with the khāṣṣ, thus no genuine conflict remains. The Hanafīs require equality in degree for conflict, which is not present if ʿāmm is ẓannī and khāṣṣ is qaṭʿī. This entire passage is a rigorous argument for the Hanafī view on the certainty of ʿāmm and its implications for textual interpretation.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A word that applies to all members of a class without restriction.
خاص (khāṣṣ): A word that applies to a specific individual or limited group.
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): Specification of a general term to exclude some individuals.
تأکید (taʾkīd): Linguistic emphasis used to reinforce the real meaning and remove figurative probability.
محکم (muḥkam): A text that is firm and unambiguous, not susceptible to abrogation or interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī scholars, why does using 'kull' or 'ajma' with a general term not indicate that the general is not all-inclusive?
A) Because it shows that the general is actually a specific term.
B) Because it serves as emphasis to make the general muḥkam, removing only probability not based on evidence.
C) Because it indicates that the general is speculative and needs specification.
D) Because it contradicts the original meaning of the general.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafī school holds that ʿāmm is qaṭʿī, and taʾkīd, multiplicity of probabilities, and the claim of widespread takhṣīṣ do not undermine this certainty.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
The Hanafi Argument for 'Aam as Qat'i and Conflict with Khaas
Hanafi usul defense of 'aam as qat'i and conflict resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument for 'aam being qat'i, analyze the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi method for resolving conflict between a general and a specific text when chronology is unknown.

Core Idea
Hanafi: 'Aam is certain; doubt-causing specification is rare, so 'aam and khaas conflict equally when contemporaneous.

This lesson unpacks a core methodological dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the certainty of general texts ('aam). The Hanafi school maintains that 'aam is qat'i (certain) unless a specific specifier creates doubt, and such specifiers are rare. In contrast, Shafi'is consider 'aam zanni (presumptive) due to the widespread occurrence of specification. This difference has direct implications for how conflicting texts are resolved, especially when the chronology of revelation is unknown. We will walk through the Hanafi proof and its practical application using the iddah verses as an example.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Analogy of Metaphorical Meanings
The author begins by comparing two specific words (khaas): one with only one possible metaphorical meaning, and another with multiple possible metaphorical meanings, with no contextual indicator (qarinah) pointing to any. Both are equal in certainty (qat'i) for their real meanings. This shows that the number of possible interpretations does not affect certainty when no qarinah exists.
This analogy is used to counter the Shafi'i argument that 'aam, having many potential individuals, is less certain than khaas.
2
Refute the Shafi'i Claim of Widespread Specification
The Shafi'is argue that specification (takhsis) of 'aam is common, creating doubt about its generality. The Hanafi response distinguishes specifiers: only an independent connected speech (kalam mustaqil mawsul) creates doubt; reason, sense, and delayed specifiers do not. Such specifiers are rare, so 'aam remains certain.
Exception (istithna') is an example of a connected specifier that does not create doubt in the remainder.
3
Contrast the Resolution of Ta'arud in Both Schools
When 'aam and khaas conflict and chronology is unknown, Hanafis treat both as contemporaneous (muqaran) because both are certain, leading to a genuine conflict. Shafi'is, viewing 'aam as zanni, specify it by the certain khaas, resolving the conflict. Hanafis then consider naskh if chronology is known.
The condition for ta'arud is equality in degree; Shafi'is deny this, Hanafis affirm it.
4
Apply to a Concrete Example: The 'Iddah Verses
The verses 'والذين يتوفون منكم' (2:234 – general 'iddah of four months and ten days for widows) and 'أولات الأحمال' (65:4 – specific 'iddah of delivery for pregnant women) conflict. Ali ibn Abi Talib combined both 'iddahs. Ibn Mas'ud considered the specific as abrogating the general for pregnant widows only, leaving the general certain for non-pregnant widows, illustrating the Hanafi view of remaining certainty after specification.
This shows the practical thamarah: in Hanafi, the general remains certain in its remaining scope; in Shafi'i, it becomes zanni.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: In a case where a general and specific conflict without known chronology, Hanafis must attempt to reconcile or apply tarih (weighing) or naskh, while Shafi'is simply specify the general. This affects the strength of the resulting ruling – certain vs. presumptive.
This impacts fatwa: a ruling derived from a general text may be considered definitive in Hanafi but not in Shafi'i.

نہیں ہوتا دیکھتے اذا کان لفظ خاص جب ایک لفظ خاص کے لئے صرف ایک معنی مجازی ہے اور دوسرے لفظ خاص کے لئے دو معنی مجازی میں یا اس سے اکثر اور قرینہ مجاز کسی میں موجود نہ ہو تو یہ دونوں لفظ خاص اپنے اپنے معنی حقیقی پر دلالت کرنے میں مساوی ہیں اول کو ترجیح علی الثانی حاصل نہیں ہوگی بلکہ دونوں برابر درجہ کے قطعی ہوں گے تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجاز واحد کا احتمال جس کیلئے قرینہ نہ ہو بالکل مساوی فی الدلالت ہے اس کے ساتھ جہاں بلا قرینہ مجازات کثیرہ کے احتمالات ہوں تو ثابت ہوا کہ عام اگرچہ اس کے اند را حتما کثیرہ ہو سکتے ہیں یہ مساوی للخاص ہو گا جس کے اندر احتمال واحد ہو سکتا ہے۔
ولا نسلم ان التخصیص شوافع کی جانب سے جو یہ کہا گیا تھا کہ عام میں تخصیص شائع ذائع ہے لہذا یہ مورث شبعہ ہوگی یہ اس کا جواب ہے کہ ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے کہ تخصیص جو مورث شبہ ہو سکتی ہے وہ عام میں بلا قرینہ شائع ذائع ہے اور تخصیص مورث شبھہ وہ ہوتی ہے جو کلام مستقل موصول بالعام کے ساتھ ہو اس قسم کی تخصیص بالکل قلیل اور نادر ہے کیونکہ خان المخصص یعنی مخصص اگر عقل ہے یا اس جیسی چیز مثلا حس فھو نی حکم الاستثناء تو یہ حکم استثنا ہے جیسے استثنا مابقی میں شبہ پیدا نہیں کرتا یہ بھی ایسے ہوگا کیونکہ عقل جن کے عدم دخول کا موجب ہوگا وہ داخل نہیں ہوں گے اور اس کے ماسویٰ تحت العام قطعا داخل رہیں گے وان كان المخصص مو الكلام مخصص اگر کلام ہے اگر وہ متراخیا واقع ہے تو وہ ناسخ ہے مخصوص نہیں ہے البتہ وہ مخصص جو مورث شبہ ہو سکتا ہے وہ صرف وہی ہے جو کلام مستقل ہو اور ہو موصولاً اور اس قسم کا مخصص بالکل قلیل ہے۔ آپ کا کثیر اور شائع کہنا صحیح نہیں ہے ناذا ثبت هذا جب یہ ثابت ہوا کہ عام ہمارے نزدیک اور قطعی ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک قطعی نہیں ہے تو خان تعارض الخاص والعام اگر خاص عام میں تعارض ہو جائے کہ ایک ثبوت حکم پر دال ہو دوسرا اسی حکم کی نفی پر خان لم يعلم التاريخ یعنی ہمیں ان کی تاریخ وقوع کا علم میں ہے کہ ان میں سے کون مقدم فی الوقوع ہے اور کون مؤخر تو ہم انھیں مقارنتہ پر محمول کریں گے اگر چہ نفس الامر میں ان دونوں میں سے کوئی متاخر ضرور ہو گا جو وہ ناسخ للمتقدم ہو گا چونکہ ہمیں تاریخ معلوم نہیں ہے لہذا ان دونوں کو محمول على المقارنتہ کیا جائیگا تاکہ کسی کی تقدیم و تاخیر سے ترجیح بلا مرجع لازم نہ آئے فعند الشافعی امام شافعی کے نزدیک چونکہ عام قطعی نہیں ہے لہذا اس خاص کے ساتھ عام کی تخصیص کرلی جائے گی اور تعارض قائم نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ متعارضین میں متساوی فی الدرجہ ہونا شرط ہے اور یہاں ایسے نہیں ہے کیونکہ خاص ان کے نزدیک قطعی ہے اور عام ظنی تو اس صورت میں بعد التخصیص یہ عام مخصوص عند البعض کے حکم میں رہے گا اور ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ دونوں قطعی ہیں لہذا حکم تعارض ثابت ہو گا نی قدر ما يقتا دلاہ اسی مقدار میں جس کو دونوں متناول ہیں جیسے والذین یتوفون منکم اور اولات الاحمال اجلعن میں حضرت علی کے نزدیک تعارض ہے تو انھوں نے ان میں صورۃ توفیق البعد الاجلین کے ساتھ نکالی تھی دان كان العام متاخرا اگر عام متاخر ہو گا تو یہ خاص کو منسوخ کر دے گا ہمارے نزدیک اور اگر خاص متاخر ہوگا پھر اگر موصولا اور متصلا واقع ہے تو مخصص ہوگا اب عام مخصصوص البعض ہو کر ظنی ہو جائیگا اگر خاص مترا خیا واقع ہے تو عام کو اسی مقدار میں جس کو خاص متناول ہے منسوخ کر دے گا خاص ناسخ للعام بالکلیہ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ صرف اسی مقدار میں جس کو خاص متناول تو اس صورت میں عام خصوص البعض ہو کر باقی میں ظنی نہیں ہو گا بلکہ باقی میں قطعی رہے گا جیسے حضرت ابن مسعود کے نزدیک اولات الاحمال ناسخ تھا والذین یتو فون کے لئے صرف حاملہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا کے حق میں اور والذین یتوفون غیر حاملہ کے حق میں قطعی ہے یہ عام مخصوص البعض یہ نہیں ہوگا جو مابقی میں ظنی ہو جائے ۔
It is not seen that: when there is a specific word, if one specific word has only one metaphorical meaning, and another specific word has two or more metaphorical meanings or more, and there is no contextual indicator for any of them, then these two specific words are equal in indicating their real meanings; the first does not have preference over the second, rather both are of equal degree of certainty. So from this it is known that the probability of a single metaphor for which there is no contextual indicator is exactly equal in indication to the situation where there are probabilities of multiple metaphors without contextual indicator. So it is proven that the general, even though it may have multiple probabilities within it, is equal to the specific which may have a single probability. And we do not accept that specification (takhsis) — from the Shafi'i side, what was said that specification in the general is widespread and common, so it creates doubt — this is its answer: we do not accept that specification which can create doubt is widespread in the general without a contextual indicator. And specification that creates doubt is that which occurs with an independent speech connected to the general. This type of specification is extremely rare and scarce. Because if the specifier is reason or something like it, e.g., sense, then it is like the ruling of exception; just as exception does not create doubt in the remainder, this will also be so because reason necessitates non-inclusion of those things, they will not be included, and what remains under the general is definitely included. And if the specifier is speech, if it occurs delayed, then it is an abrogator (nasikh), not a specifier. However, the specifier that can create doubt is only that which is an independent speech and is connected. This type of specifier is extremely rare. Your saying 'abundant and widespread' is not correct. So when this is established that the general in our view is certain, and in Imam Shafi'i's view it is not certain, then in case of conflict between the general and specific — if the general and specific conflict, one indicating the establishment of a ruling, the other indicating its negation — and we do not know their history (which occurred first), we will regard them as contemporary (muqaran), even though in reality one of them must be later, which would be abrogator of the earlier. Since we do not know the history, we will treat them as contemporary to avoid unjustified preference without basis. So according to Imam Shafi'i, since the general is not certain, the general will be specified by the specific, and no conflict will occur because for conflict, equality in degree is a condition, and here it is not so because the specific in his view is certain and the general is presumptive. In that case, after specification, this general becomes like a specified general in some views. And according to us, since both are certain, the ruling of conflict is established to the extent that both are applicable. For example, in the verses 'والذين يتوفون منكم' and 'أولات الأحمال' in the view of Ali there is conflict, so he resolved them by the method of combining considering both 'iddahs. If the general is later, it will abrogate the specific in our view. And if the specific is later, then if it is connected and continuous, it will be a specifier; then the general becomes specified in part and becomes presumptive. If the specific is delayed, it will abrogate the general only to the extent that the specific covers; the specific does not abrogate the general entirely, but only to the extent that it covers. In that case, the general becomes specified in part but does not become presumptive in the remainder; rather it remains certain in the remainder. For example, in the view of Ibn Mas'ud, 'أولات الأحمال' was an abrogator for 'والذين يتوفون' only concerning a pregnant woman whose husband dies, and 'والذين يتوفون' is certain for non-pregnant women. This general is specified in part, not one that becomes presumptive in the remainder.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi dispute with the Shafi'i school on the nature of the general (عام) and its certainty. The author first establishes that a specific word (خاص) that has one metaphorical meaning is equal in degree of certainty to another specific word that has multiple possible metaphorical meanings when no contextual indicator (قرینہ) is present. This analogy is used to argue that the general, even though it may have many potential individuals, is equal to the specific that has only one potential individual; thus the general is also certain (قطعی). Then the author refutes the Shafi'i claim that specification (تخصیص) in the general is widespread (شائع ذائع) and creates doubt. He argues that specification that creates doubt is only that which comes from an independent connected speech (کلام مستقل موصول) — such specifiers are rare. If the specifier is reason (عقل) or sense (حس), it is like an exception (استثناء) and does not create doubt; if it is a delayed connected speech, it is abrogation (نسخ), not specification. So the general remains certain unless a rare connected independent specifier appears. Since the general is certain in the Hanafi school while it is presumptive (ظنی) in the Shafi'i school, conflict (تعارض) between a general and a specific is handled differently. If we do not know which text came first, we assume they are contemporary (مقارنتہ) to avoid arbitrary preference. In Shafi'i view, since the general is presumptive, it is specified by the certain specific, so no conflict arises. In Hanafi view, both are certain, so conflict arises to the extent they both apply. The author then discusses scenarios: if the general is later, it abrogates the specific; if the specific is later and connected, it specifies the general (making it presumptive in that part); if the specific is later and delayed, it abrogates the general only in its scope, leaving the rest certain. The examples of the iddah verses (2:234 and 65:4) illustrate the conflict and its resolution by Ali and Ibn Mas'ud. Ali combined both iddahs, while Ibn Mas'ud considered the specific (أولات الأحمال) as abrogating the general (والذين يتوفون) only for pregnant widows, leaving the general applicable to non-pregnant widows as certain. The passage thus defends the Hanafi position that the general is certain and that specification is not widespread.

Key Terms
عام ('Aam): A word that covers all its individuals without restriction.
خاص (Khaas): A word that is specific to a particular individual or type.
تخصیص (Takhsis): The act of restricting a general term to some of its individuals.
قطعی (Qat'i): Certain, definitive; a text that is clear and not open to multiple interpretations without clear evidence.
ظنی (Zanni): Presumptive, not certain; open to interpretation or specification.
مقارنتہ (Muqaranah): Treating two texts as contemporaneous when chronology is unknown, to avoid unjustified preference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument, which type of specifier creates doubt (shubha) in the general?
A) A specifier that is reason ('aql)
B) A specifier that is an independent connected speech (kalam mustaqil mawsul)
C) A specifier that is a delayed speech (mutarakhkhil)
D) Any specifier that is not an exception (istithna')

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds 'aam as qat'i because doubt-creating specifiers are rare; therefore, conflict with a specific results in genuine ta'arud, resolved by tarih or naskh, not automatic specification.

Qasr al-Aam and Non-Independent Specifiers
Introduces qasr al-aam and non-independent specifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of non-independent specifiers (ghair mustaqil) as defined in Hanafi usul and distinguish them from independent specifiers.

Core Idea
Restricting the general requires a non-independent specifier: exception, condition, description, or limit.

This passage introduces the crucial concept of qasr al-aam (restricting the general). In Hanafi usul, the specifier that restricts the general must be 'non-independent' (ghair mustaqil) — meaning it is grammatically and conceptually tied to the original sentence. The author then enumerates the four classical types: exception, condition, description, and limit. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly interpreting legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term (amm)
In any legal statement, first locate the word or phrase that is general ('amm), i.e., it includes all individuals of its category without restriction.
For example, in 'Honor the students,' the word 'students' is general.
2
Check for a specifier (mukhassis)
Look for an element that restricts the general to only some of its individuals. This can be an exception, condition, description, limit, or other types.
The specifier may be independent (mustaqil) or non-independent (ghair mustaqil).
3
Classify the specifier as independent or non-independent
Determine whether the specifier is a complete independent statement or it depends on the original sentence for meaning. Non-independent specifiers are grammatically connected to the general statement.
If it is a separate sentence or a rational indication (like reason), it is independent.
4
If non-independent, identify which of the four types
The four types are: exception (istithna, e.g., 'except'), condition (shart, e.g., 'if'), description (sifat, e.g., 'pious'), and limit (ghaya, e.g., 'until').
Some scholars add substitution (badal), but the passage considers it a strong exception.
5
Apply: state how the specifier restricts the general
Explain the effect: the general term now applies only to those individuals satisfying the condition, excepted group, description, or up to a limit.
For example, 'Honor the students if they are punctual' restricts the honor to punctual students.

Source Text

فصل قصر العام على بعض ما يتناوله الي عام کو اس کے متناولہ افراد میں سے بعض پر مقصور و محصور کرنا لا يخلو من ان يكون بغیر مستقل اور غیر مستقل باصطلاح اصول ایسی کلام کو کہا جاتا ہے جو صدر کلام کے ساتھ تعلق رکھتی ہو اور نفسہ کلام تام اور حامل فائدہ تامہ نہ ہو والمستقل اور مستقل اس کے مقابلہ میں اس کو کہا جاتا ہے جو غیر مستقل جیسا نہ ہو پھر خواہ وہ کلام ہی نہ ہو جیسے عقل اور جس وعادہ یا کلام ہو کر مستقل ہو اور نام نیفسہ ہو۔ دھوای غیر المستقل یعنی غیر مستقل کے اندر مصنف نے اربعہ اقسام ذکر فرمائے ہیں استثنا - شرط - صفہ - غایت بعض نے بدل بعض کا اضافہ کیا ہے اور کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ محکم استثناء ہے لہذا الگ ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور ان کے علاوہ صلہ اور حال کا بھی اضافہ کیا گیا ہے لیکن حکم صفہ ہیں لہذا اکتفاء علی الا ربعہ صحیح ہے ۔ فالاستثناء تواستثنا قصر العام على بعض افرادہ کا موجب ہے اور شرط صدر کلام کو بعض تقادیر بر مقصور و محصور کر دیتی ہے ۔ نخوانت طالق ان دخلت الدار اگران دخلت الدار کی شرط نہ ہوتی تو عورت
Chapter: Restricting the general to some of what it includes. Restricting the general to some of its individuals must be by a non-independent specifier. 'Non-independent' in usul terminology is said of a speech that is connected to the opening speech and is not itself a complete speech carrying a complete benefit. And 'independent' (mustaqil) is the opposite: that which is not like non-independent, whether it is not speech at all, like reason and the like, or it is speech and is independent and by itself. Regarding non-independent, the author mentioned four types: exception (istithna), condition (shart), description (sifat), and limit (ghaya). Some have added substitution (badal), and it is said that it is a strong exception, so there is no need to mention it separately. Additionally, connection (sila) and state (hal) have also been added, but they have the ruling of description, so relying on the four is correct. So exception causes the restriction of the general to some of its individuals, and condition restricts the opening speech to some particular situations. 'You are divorced if you enter the house' — if the condition 'if you enter the house' were not present, the woman...
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section (فصل) on restricting the general to some of its individuals (قصر العام على بعض ما يتناوله). It explains that such restriction must be done by a 'non-independent' (غیر مستقل) specifier. The term 'non-independent' in usul refers to a speech that is grammatically or conceptually connected to a preceding speech and does not form a complete sentence by itself. The author lists four types: استثنا (exception), شرط (condition), صفة (description/qualification), and غایت (limit/end). Some scholars add بدل (substitution), but it is considered a strong exception, so it is not separate. Others add صلة (relative clause) and حال (circumstantial accusative), but they have the same ruling as description, so the four categories are sufficient. Each type works: exception restricts the general to its excluded individuals; condition restricts the general to the situation mentioned. For example, 'You are divorced if you enter the house'—the condition limits the divorce to the occurrence of entry. The passage ends mid-sentence with the example. This section is foundational for understanding how restrictions are applied in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
قصر العام (Qasr al-'Aam): Restricting the general term to some of its individuals by means of a specifier.
مستقل (Mustaqil): An independent speech that is complete in itself and can stand alone.
استثناء (Istithna): Exception, e.g., 'except' statements that remove some individuals from the general.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, restricting a general term (amm) requires a non-independent specifier, classified into four types: exception, condition, description, and limit.

Conflict Between General and Specific and Abrogation in Hanafi Usul
Explains Hanafi rules for resolving conflict between general and specific texts and the conditions for abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for resolving conflict between a general and a specific text and distinguish between takhsis and naskh based on timing and connection.

Core Idea
When general and specific conflict, if both are qat'i, reconcile; if later and disconnected, the specific abrogates the general only within its scope.

This passage from the usul al-fiqh text explains how to handle apparent contradictions between a general (amm) and a specific (khass) legal ruling. The Hanafi school insists that both general and specific texts from the Quran are definitive (qat'i) in transmission, so conflict must be resolved either by reconciliation (tarih) or by abrogation (naskh) if one text is later and disconnected. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper istinbat (derivation of rulings).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict scenario
Locate the two texts: one general (amm) covering multiple cases, and one specific (khass) covering a subset. Determine if they appear to conflict.
2
Classify each text's epistemological weight
Assess whether each text is qat'i (definitive in transmission) or zanni (presumptive). The Hanafi view holds that both Quranic texts are qat'i al-thubut, so they remain definitive even after specification.
Some scholars consider the specific as qat'i and the general as zanni after specification.
3
Determine order and connection
Identify which text came later chronologically, and whether the later text is connected (muttasil, i.e., part of the same context) or disconnected (munfasil, i.e., revealed separately).
4
Apply the Hanafi rule
If both are qat'i, conflict must be resolved by reconciliation (tarih) if possible, or by abrogation (naskh). If the later text is disconnected, it abrogates the earlier only in the scope of the specific, leaving the general definitive elsewhere.
If the later text is connected, it specifies (takhsis) the general, making it zanni in the specified part.
5
Distinguish from the opposing view
Compare with the view that the specific is qat'i and the general becomes zanni after specification, leading to different conclusions about abrogation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے اور یہاں ایسے نہیں ہے کیونکہ خاص ان کے نزدیک قطعی ہے اور عام ظنی تو اس صورت میں بعد التخصیص یہ عام مخصوص عند البعض کے حکم میں رہے گا اور ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ دونوں قطعی ہیں لہذا حکم تعارض ثابت ہو گا قدر ما يقتضيانہ اسی مقدار میں جس کو دونوں متناول ہیں جیسے والذین یتوفون منکم اور اولات الاحمال اجلہن میں حضرت علی کے نزدیک تعارض ہے تو انھوں نے ان میں صورت توفیق بعد الاجلین کے ساتھ نکالی تھی وان کان العام متاخرا اگر عام متاخر ہو گا تو یہ خاص کو منسوخ کر دے گا ہمارے نزدیک اور اگر خاص متاخر ہوگا پھر اگر موصولا اور متصلا واقع ہے تو مخصص ہوگا اب عام مخصوص البعض ہو کر ظنی ہو جائیگا اگر خاص متاخرا واقع ہے تو عام کو اسی مقدار میں جس کو خاص متناول ہے منسوخ کر دے گا خاص ناسخ للعام بالکلیہ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ صرف اسی مقدار میں جس کو خاص متناول تو اس صورت میں عام خصوص البعض ہو کر باقی میں ظنی نہیں ہو گا بلکہ باقی میں قطعی رہے گا جیسے حضرت ابن مسعود کے نزدیک اولات الاحمال ناسخ تھا والذین یتوفون کے لئے صرف حاملہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا کے حق میں اور والذین یتوفون غیر حاملہ کے حق میں قطعی ہے یہ عام مخصوص البعض یہ نہیں ہوگا جو مابقی میں ظنی ہو جائے۔
And it is not like this because according to them the specific is definitive and the general is presumptive, so in that case after specification this general becomes like a specified general according to some. And according to us, since both are definitive, the ruling of conflict is established to the extent that both indicate, like 'those who die among you' and 'those who are pregnant' until their term: there is conflict according to Ali, so he derived a mode of reconciliation between the two terms. If the general is later, it will abrogate the specific according to us. If the specific is later, then if it occurs connected and attached, it will be a specifier, and the general becomes specified to some and becomes presumptive. If the specific occurs separately, it will abrogate the general to the extent that the specific indicates. The specific does not abrogate the general entirely, but only to the extent that the specific indicates. In this case, the general becomes specified to some parts and remains definitive in the rest, not becoming presumptive in the remainder. Like according to Ibn Mas'ud, 'those who are pregnant' was abrogating for 'those who die' only in the case of a pregnant woman whose husband dies, and 'those who die' is definitive for non-pregnant women. This specified-before-parts general will not become presumptive in the remainder.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage addresses the conflict between a general ('amm) and a specific (khass) legal text. It first mentions the view of some scholars who consider the specific definitive and the general presumptive, so after specification the general becomes like a specified general. However, the Hanafi position is that both texts are definitive, leading to a genuine conflict that must be resolved. The example given is the two Quranic verses: 'وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنْكُمْ' (those who die among you, waiting four months and ten days) and 'وَأُولَاتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ' (pregnant women, their term until delivery). According to Imam Ali, there is conflict, and he reconciled by extending both terms. The passage then explains the rule regarding priority: if the general comes later, it abrogates the specific (Hanafi view). If the specific comes later, its effect depends on whether it is connected (muttasil) or disconnected (munfasil). If connected, it specifies the general, making it presumptive in the specified part. If disconnected, it abrogates the general only in the scope of the specific, leaving the general definitive in other parts, as exemplified by Ibn Mas'ud's view that 'أولات الأحمال' abrogates 'والذين يتوفون' only for pregnant women, while the latter remains definitive for non-pregnant women. The key distinction is between specification (takhsis) and abrogation (naskh).

Key Terms
عام (‘amm): A word that covers all individuals of its category without restriction
خاص (khass): A word that specifically denotes a limited set of individuals
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a previous ruling by a later text, applicable only when the later text is disconnected and cannot be reconciled
موصول (mawsul): Connected text; when the specific is part of the same context as the general
منفصل (munfasil): Disconnected text; when the specific is revealed independently of the general

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a disconnected specific text comes after a general text, what is its effect according to the Hanafi position?
A) It specifies the general, making it presumptive in both the specified and remaining parts.
B) It abrogates the general entirely.
C) It abrogates the general only to the extent of the specific text, leaving it definitive in the remainder.
D) It has no effect on the general.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: a later disconnected specific text abrogates the earlier general only in its own scope, leaving the general definitive elsewhere.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Qasr al-‘Amm: Restricting the General and Types of Mukhassis
Defines qasr al-‘amm and categorizes specifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two categories of mukhassis, apply the Hanafi rule for ghayah inclusion/exclusion, and classify specifiers as connected or independent.

Core Idea
A general term is restricted by a specifier; specifiers are either connected (exception, condition, description, limit) or independent (reason, custom, separate text).

This passage introduces the fundamental concept of qasr al-‘amm — confining a general ruling to only some of its individuals. Understanding this is essential for correctly interpreting Shari'ah texts that appear general. The author categorizes specifiers into those that are part of the original speech (ghayr mustaqill) and those that are external (mustaqill), and provides detailed rules, especially for limits (ghayah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
Recognize that specifiers (mukhassis) are divided into non-independent (connected to the general statement) and independent (external). Non-independent specifiers are further divided into four types: exception, condition, description, and limit.
Some scholars add substitution (badal) but the author considers it a strong exception.
2
Analyze each non-independent type
For each type (istithna', shart, sifat, ghayah), understand how it restricts the general. Use the examples given: conditional divorce, zakat on grazing camels, washing to elbows.
Also note that description (sifat) and limit (ghayah) are the most common in legal texts.
3
Apply the ghayah inclusion/exclusion rule
When a limit (ghayah) is of the same genus as the limited (maghya), it is included in the ruling. If of a different genus, it is excluded. For example, elbows (same genus as hands) are included in washing; night (different genus from day) is excluded from fasting.
This rule is specific to Hanafi usul and resolves apparent contradictions in texts.
4
Recognize independent specifiers
Independent specifiers are not part of the original speech. They include rational proof (e.g., 'Creator of everything' excludes Allah from creation), custom, and separate textual evidence. Also, the exclusion of children and insane from general obligations like prayer and zakat.
Independent specifiers are stronger in evidence but require careful identification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل قصر العام على بعض ما يتناوله یعنی عام کو اس کے متناولہ افراد میں سے بعض پر مقصور و محصور کرنا لا يخلو من ان يكون بغير مستقل أو بمستقل. وغير المستقل باصطلاح اصول ایسی کلام کو کہا جاتا ہے جو صدر کلام کے ساتھ تعلق رکھتی ہو اور بنفسہ کلام تام اور حامل فائدہ تامہ نہ ہو. والمستقل اس کے مقابلہ میں اس کو کہا جاتا ہے جو غیر مستقل جیسا نہ ہو پھر خواہ وہ کلام ہی نہ ہو جیسے عقل اور عادہ یا کلام ہو کر مستقل ہو اور تام بنفسہ ہو. ذوی غیر المستقل یعنی غیر مستقل کے اندر مصنف نے اربعہ اقسام ذکر فرمائے ہیں استثنا - شرط - صفہ - غایت. بعض نے بدل بعض کا اضافہ کیا ہے اور کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ محکم استثناء ہے لہذا الگ ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور ان کے علاوہ صلہ اور حال کا بھی اضافہ کیا گیا ہے لیکن حکم صفہ ہیں لہذا اکتفاء علی الاربعہ صحیح ہے. فالاستثناء قصر العام على بعض افرادہ کا موجب ہے. اور شرط صدر کلام کو بعض تقدیروں پر مقصور و محصور کر دیتی ہے. نحو: انت طالق ان دخلت الدار اگر ان دخلت الدار کی شرط نہ ہوتی تو عورت سر حال پر مطلقہ ہو جاتی خواہ دخول دار ہوتا یا نہ ہوتا لیکن اس شرط نے طلاق کو دخول دار کی تقدیر و حالت پر مقصور و محصور کر دیا ہے. والصفة توجب القصر اور صفتہ حکم کو ان افراد عام پر مقصور کردے گی جن کے اندر یہ صفت پائی جائیگی. نحو: فی الابل السائمة زکوة یعنی سائمہ پر زکوة واجب ہے نہ کہ غیر سائمہ. والغاية توجب اور غایت حکم کو اس بعض پر مقصور کر دے گی جس کے لئے یہ غایت حد بنا دی گئی جیسے ایدیکم الی المرافق میں ہاتھوں کو صرف مرافق تک دھونا واجب ہے اس سے متجاوز حصہ کا دھونا واجب نہیں ہے. وعلی ماذکر الغایۃ کبھی حکم کو مقصور کر دے گی ماوراء غایت پر معنی یہ غایت حکم معنا میں داخل نہیں ہوگی جیسے اتموا الصیام الی اللیل میں کہ لیل حکم صوم سے خارج ہے. ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اگر غایت از جنس مغیا ہو جیسے مرافق از جنس ایدی نہیں تو اس قسم کی غایت داخل فی حکم المغیا ہوگی اگر از خلاف جنس ہے تو پھر داخل نہیں ہے جیسے صوم دن کے وقت ہوتا ہے اور لیل از جنس نہار نہیں ہے لہذا یہ حکم صوم سے خارج ہو گی. اما بمستقل یا قصر العام على البعض مستقل کے ساتھ ہوگی اور اسی کو ہی تخصیص کہا جاتا ہے اور مستقل اسی کو کہتے ہیں جو غیر مستقل کی تعریف میں کہا گیا تھا ایسی کلام جو صدر کلام کے ساتھ متعلق اور تام بنفسہ نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں مستقل اس کو بھی کہا جائیگا جو سرے سے کلام ہی نہیں ہے جیسے عقل وغیرہ یا کلام تو ہے لیکن صدر کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہے اور تام بنفسہ ہے. وھو التخصص اما بالکلام او غیره. غیر الکلام اما العقل نحو خالق کل شیئ يعلم ضرورة ان الله مخصوص منه اى من الشیئ المخلوق یعنی عقل خود کہتا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ اس شئی میں جو مخلوق ہے داخل نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ تو خالق علی الاطلاق ہے اس کے سوا کوئی خالق نہیں ہے تو پھر یہ مخلوق میں کیسے داخل ہو سکتا ہے ورنہ اپنے آپ کے لئے خود خالق ہو جائے گا اور ایک شئی کا اپنے آپ کیلئے خالق ہونا عقلا محال ہے کیونکہ تقدم الشئی بالوجود علی نفسہ لازم آجائیں گا جو کہ باطل ہے. وتخصیص الصبی والمجنون یعنی خطابات شرعیہ جو کہ عام ہیں ان میں سے صبی اور مجنون کی تخصیص مثل اقیموا الصلوة اتوا الزکوة صوموا رمضان وغیرہ من الخطابات سے صبی اور مجنون کی تخصیص کی جاتی ہے اور ان احکام سے انھیں خارج کیا جاتا ہے من هذا القبیل. اما [؟] الحس [؟] یا وہ غیر کلام جو مخصص ہے وہ جیسے بلقیس کے متعلق ہے اوتیت [؟]
Chapter: Restricting the general to some of what it covers, i.e., confining the general to some of its individuals. It is either by non-independent or independent [specifier]. Non-independent in the terminology of usul refers to speech that is connected to the first part of the speech and is not complete in itself nor bears a complete benefit. Independent is what is not like non-independent; whether it is not speech at all, like reason and custom, or it is speech but independent and complete in itself. The types of non-independent: the author mentioned four categories: exception, condition, description, limit. Some added ‘substitution’ but it is said that this is a strong exception, so no need to mention separately. Also, connector and state were added, but their ruling is that of description, so relying on four is correct. Exception causes restriction of the general to some of its individuals. Condition restricts the first part of speech to certain estimations. Example: 'You are divorced if you enter the house' – if the condition 'if you enter the house' were not present, the woman would be divorced unconditionally whether she entered the house or not, but this condition restricts the divorce to the estimation and state of entering the house. Description necessitates restriction: the description will restrict the ruling to those individuals of the general in which this description exists. Example: 'Zakat is on grazing camels' – zakat is obligatory on grazing camels, not on non-grazing. Limit necessitates: the limit will restrict the ruling to that part for which it is made a limit. Like 'your hands to the elbows' – washing the hands is obligatory only up to the elbows, washing beyond that is not obligatory. And according to what was mentioned, the limit sometimes restricts the ruling to beyond the limit, meaning the limit is not included in the ruling. Like 'complete the fast to the night' – night is excluded from the ruling of fasting. The rule is: if the limit is of the same genus as the limited thing – like elbows are not of the same genus as hands – then this type of limit is included in the ruling of the limited; if it is of a different genus, then it is not included. As for fasting during the day and night is not of the same genus as day, so it is excluded from the ruling of fasting. As for independent, or restricting the general to some individuals with an independent [specifier], this is called specification. Independent is what was said in the definition of non-independent: speech that is not connected to the first part and is not complete in itself. Then independent also includes what is not speech at all, like reason, etc., or speech that is not connected to the first part and is complete in itself. It is specification either by speech or other. Non-speech: as for reason, like 'Creator of everything' – reason necessarily knows that Allah is excluded from the created things, because He is the absolute Creator, there is no creator other than Him. So how can He be included in creation? Otherwise He would be Creator of Himself, and a thing being its own creator is rationally impossible because that would require the thing to exist before itself, which is false. And specification of the child and the insane: i.e., the general legal addresses like 'establish prayer', 'give zakat', 'fast Ramadan', etc., from these addresses the child and insane are specified and excluded from these rulings, this is of this type. As for [؟] senses [؟] or other non-speech that is a specifier, it is like what is related to Bilqis [؟] she was given [؟]
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'qasr al-‘amm' (restricting the general) and categorizes specifiers (mukhassis) into two main types: independent (mustaqill) and non-independent (ghayr mustaqill). The author, following the standard Hanafi usul classification, explains that non-independent specifiers are those that are part of the same speech and not standalone; they include four types: exception (istithna'), condition (shart), description (sifat), and limit (ghayah). Each is illustrated with Shari'ah examples: exception limits the general to its exceptions; condition restricts the ruling to a contingency (like conditional divorce); description narrows the ruling to only those individuals with that attribute (zakat on grazing camels); limit sets a boundary for the ruling (washing hands to elbows). A key rule regarding limits: if the limit is of the same genus as the limited, it is included in the ruling; if of a different genus, it is excluded (e.g., night excluded from fast). Independent specifiers are not part of the original text; they include intellectual proof (such as the verse 'Creator of everything' necessarily excluding Allah from being created) and also the exclusion of children and the insane from general obligations like prayer, zakat, and fasting. The passage emphasizes that specification (takhsis) is a distinct operation from abrogation, as it merely clarifies the scope of the general without overriding its original authority.

Key Terms
مخصص (mukhassis): Something that restricts the general to some individuals; may be non-independent (connected) or independent (separate)
استثناء (istithna'): Exception from a general statement, e.g., 'the thieves except the hand'
غایت (ghayah): Limit that defines the endpoint of a ruling; its inclusion/exclusion depends on genus
شرط (shart): Condition that makes the ruling contingent upon its occurrence
صفة (sifah): Description or attribute that restricts the general to individuals possessing that attribute

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule given in the passage, how is the limit treated when it is of the same genus as the limited?
A) It is excluded from the ruling.
B) It is included in the ruling.
C) It is optional to include or exclude.
D) It indicates abrogation of the general.

Key Takeaway
General terms are specified by both connected and independent specifiers, and the inclusion of a limit in the ruling depends on whether it shares the same genus as the limited.

The Attribute (Sifah) as a Restrictor of General Rulings
Explaining that an attribute restricts a ruling to individuals possessing that attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that an attribute (sifah) restricts a general ruling (amm) to only those individuals possessing the attribute.

Core Idea
An attribute (sifah) restricts a general ruling to those individuals who possess that attribute.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi usul principle: when a ruling is tied to a specific attribute, it limits the ruling's applicability. The principle 'al-sifah tujib al-qasr' is fundamental in deriving fiqh rulings from general texts. We'll examine classical examples from divorce and zakat to understand how this restriction works in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Identify the principle 'al-sifah tujib al-qasr' – the attribute necessitates restriction. Understand that this means the ruling applies only to individuals who possess the mentioned attribute.
The principle is a tool for interpreting general (amm) texts.
2
Analyze the Divorce Example
Consider the condition 'if you enter the house, you are divorced'. The attribute 'entry' restricts the divorce to the state of entry; divorce does not occur without entry. This shows how a condition (which is a kind of sifah) restricts the ruling.
The example illustrates restriction by a circumstantial attribute.
3
Analyze the Zakat Example
The hadith 'On grazing livestock (sa'imah) zakat is obligatory' contains the attribute 'sa'imah'. According to the principle, zakat is only obligatory on grazing livestock, not on stall-fed (ma'lufah) livestock.
This is a classic fiqh application in Hanafi school.
4
Generalize the Rule
Understand the difference between a merely descriptive attribute (wasf) and a restrictive attribute (sifah muqayyidah). In Hanafi usul, any attribute attached to a ruling restricts it unless there is evidence to the contrary.
This principle is a cornerstone in the derivation of many fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سر حالت پر مطلقہ ہو جاتی خواہ دخول دار ہوتا یا نہ ہوتا لیکن اس شرط نے طلاق کو دخول دار کی تقدیر و حالت پر مقصور و محصور کر دیا ہے۔ والصفة توجب القصر اور صفة حکم کو ان افرادِ عام پر مقصور کردے گی جن کے اندر یہ صفتہ پائی جائیگی - نحوفى الاميل السائمة زكرة توفي سائمہ پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی بلکہ صرف سائمہ میں ہوگی
Upon that state, the woman becomes divorced whether intercourse occurred or not, but this condition restricts the divorce to the state and condition of the occurrence of intercourse. And the attribute necessitates restriction: the attribute will restrict the ruling to those general individuals in which this attribute is found. For example, in grazing cattle, zakat is not obligatory except on grazing (sa'imah) ones; it is only on sa'imah.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains a key usul principle: when a ruling is tied to a specific attribute (sifah), it restricts (qasr) the ruling to only those instances where the attribute is present. The author first gives an example from divorce: if a man says 'if you enter the house you are divorced' and the woman enters, divorce occurs, but the condition restricts the application to that particular state. Then he states the general rule: the quality confines the ruling. He then provides a fiqh example: the obligation of zakat on grazing livestock (sa'imah) means it is not obligatory on non-grazing (ma'lufah) livestock. This is a standard Hanafi usul principle used in deriving rulings from the texts.

Key Terms
الصفة (al-sifah): The attribute or quality attached to the ruling that restricts its application to individuals possessing that attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effect of an attribute (sifah) on a ruling according to this passage?
A) It expands the ruling to all individuals.
B) It restricts the ruling to only individuals possessing that attribute.
C) It has no effect on the ruling.
D) It abrogates the ruling.

Key Takeaway
The attribute in a ruling restricts its application to only those individuals bearing that attribute.

The Rule of Ghaya and Genus-Based Inclusion
Explaining the Hanafi rule of ghaya and genus-based inclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of ghaya to determine whether a limit is included in the ruling, using the criterion of genus similarity.

Core Idea
A limit restricts the ruling to what is before it; the limit's inclusion depends on whether it shares the genus of the limited.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi usul principle of al-ghayah (limit). A limit, such as 'to the elbows' in the wudu verse, confines the ruling. But is the limit itself included in the ruling? According to Hanafi usul, the answer depends on whether the limit is of the same genus as the limited thing. We will analyze two Quranic examples to understand this distinction and apply it as a tool for deriving fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ghaya in the text
Locate the limit phrase (إلى + noun) in the Quranic verse. For example, in 'أَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ', the phrase 'إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ' is the limit.
The limit indicates the endpoint of the commanded action.
2
Determine the ruling before the limit
Identify the action commanded up to the limit. In the wudu verse, the action is washing the hands (أَيْدِيَكُمْ) up to the elbows.
3
Apply the genus rule
Compare the genus of the limit (e.g., elbows) with the genus of the limited (e.g., hands). If they are of different genera, the limit is included in the ruling. If they are of the same genus, the limit is excluded.
The passage provides the rule: 'إذا كانت الغاية من جنس المغيا تدخل، وإلا فلا'.
4
Decide inclusion or exclusion
Based on genus similarity, conclude whether the limit is part of the commanded action. For the wudu verse, elbows (different genus) are included; for the fasting verse, night (different genus) is excluded.
This conclusion directly affects the fiqh ruling: washing elbows is wajib; fasting at night is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والغاية توجب اور غایت حکم کو اس بعض پر مقصود کر دے گی جس کے لئے یہ غایت حد بنا دیگئی جیسے ایدیکم الی المرافق میں ہاتھوں کو صرف مرافق تک دھونا واجب ہے اس سے متجاوز حصہ کا دھونا واجب نہیں ہے . و علی مادراء الغایۃ اور غایت کبھی حکم کو مقصور کر دے گی ماوراء غایت پر معنی یہ غایت حکم معنا میں داخل نہیں ہوگی جیسے اتموا الصیام الی اللیل میں کہ لیل حکم صوم سے خارج ہے ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اگر غایت از جنس مغیا ہو جیسے مرافق از جنس ایدی نہیں تو اس قسم کی غایت داخل فی حکم المغیا ہوگی اگر از خلاف جنس ہے تو پھر داخل نہیں ہے جیسے صوم دن کے وقت ہوتا ہے اور لیل از جنس نہار نہیں ہے لہذا یہ حکم صوم سے خارج ہو گی۔
And the limit necessitates: the limit will restrict the ruling to that part for which this limit is set as a boundary, like 'your hands to the elbows' — washing is obligatory only up to the elbows, washing beyond is not obligatory. And according to this, the limit [sometimes] restricts the ruling to what is before the limit, meaning the limit is not included in the ruling's meaning, like 'complete the fast until night' — night is excluded from the ruling of fasting. The rule is: if the limit is of the same genus as what is limited, like elbows are not of the same genus as hands, then this kind of limit is included in the ruling of the limited; if it is of a different genus, then it is not included, like fasting occurs during the day and night is not of the same genus as day, therefore it is excluded from the ruling of fasting.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage explains the usul principle of ghaya (limit). A limit (like 'to the elbows') restricts the ruling to the range before it. However, there is a subtle distinction: if the limit is of the same genus (jins) as the thing being limited, it is included in the ruling; otherwise it is excluded. The example given: in the Quranic verse 'wash your hands to the elbows', the elbows are not of the same genus as hands (they are different body parts), so the ruling of washing includes the elbows. In contrast, in 'complete the fast until night', night is of a different genus (darkness) than the day (light), so night is excluded from the fasting obligation. This is a rule used by Hanafi usulists to understand the scope of commands that include a limit.

Key Terms
الغاية (al-ghayah): A limit or endpoint that confines the ruling to what is before it; its inclusion in the ruling depends on whether it is of the same genus as the limited thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the verse 'complete the fast until night' (أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيْلِ), according to the Hanafi rule, is night included in the fasting obligation?
A) Yes, because the limit always includes itself.
B) No, because night is of a different genus than day, so it is excluded.
C) Yes, because the limit is of the same genus as the limited.
D) No, because the limit always excludes itself.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, whether a limit is included in the ruling depends on genus: if the limit is from a different genus than the limited, it is included; if from the same genus, it is excluded.

Independent Specifiers (Mustaqill) in Hanafi Usul
Classification of independent specifiers in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify independent specifiers (reason and custom) and apply them to restrict a general text in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Reason and custom can restrict a general text without being part of the speech itself.

In Hanafi usul, specification (takhsis) of a general text (amm) can come from sources outside the speech itself, known as independent specifiers (mustaqill). These include rational deduction and customary practice. Understanding how these operate allows you to apply general rulings correctly, as the Quran and Sunnah are often specified by reason and custom.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of mustaqill
An independent specifier is one that is not part of the original speech and can be complete in itself. It includes non-verbal factors like reason and custom.
Mustaqill is contrasted with ghayr mustaqill which is part of the speech.
2
Identify the rational specifier (العقل)
Reason (aql) can specify a general verse. Example: 'Creator of everything' (خالق كل شيء) necessarily excludes Allah from the 'everything' because He cannot be His own creation. This is a rational specification.
The rational specifier is considered independent because it does not rely on any textual addition.
3
Identify the customary specifier (العادة)
Custom (urf) can specify general terms. Example: 'Do not eat a head' (لا تأكل رأساً) in a particular custom excludes bird heads because people do not eat them, so the general 'head' is restricted to heads of livestock.
Custom must be general and stable to act as a mukhassis.
4
Apply the specifier to a general text
When you encounter a general text, check if there is a rational or customary reason to restrict it. If a clear reason or custom exists, the general is specified to exclude certain individuals.
This is a key tool in Hanafi usul for deriving rulings.

اد بمستقل یا قصر العام على البعض مستقل کے ساتھ ہوگی اور اسی کو ہی تخصیص کہا جاتا ہے اور مستقل اسی کو کہتے ہیں جو غیر مستقل کی تعریف میں کہا گیا تھا ایسی کلام جو صدر کلام کے ساتھ متعلق اور تام بنفسہ نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں مستقل اس کو بھی کہا جائیگا۔ جو سرے سے کلام ہی نہیں ہے جیسے عقل وغیرہ یا کلام تو ہے لیکن صدر کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہے اور تام بنفسہ ہے اس لئے کہا وھو ای التخصص اما بالكلام او غيره وهواى غیر الکلام اما العقل نحو خالق كل شئ يعلم ضرورة ان الله مخصوص منه اى من الشتى المخلوق یعنی عقل خود کہتا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ اس شئی میں جو مخلوق ہے داخل نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ تو خالق علی الاطلاق ہے اس کے سوا کوئی خالق نہیں ہے تو پھر یہ مخلوق میں کیسے داخل ہو سکتا ہے ورنہ اپنے آپ کے لئے خود خالق ہو جائے گا اور ایک شئی کا اپنے آپ کیلئے خالق ہونا عقلا محال ہے کیونکہ تقدم الشئی بالوجود علی نفسہ لازم آجائیں گا جو کہ باطل ہے ۔ وتخصيص الصبي المز یعنی خطابات شرعیہ جو کہ عام ہیں۔ ان میں سے صبی اور مجنون کی تخصیص مثل اقيموا الصلوة - اتوا الزكوة . صوموا رمضان وغير با من الخطابات سے صبی اور مجنون کی خصیص کی جاتی ہے اور ان احکام سے انھیں خارج کیا جاتا ہے من هذا القبيل اسی منا العقلی اما النجس یا وہ غیر کلام جو مخصص ہے وہ جس ہوگی جیسے بلقیس کے متعلق ہے اوتیت من كل شئی اب اس کل شئی سے متعدد اشیا خارج ہیں جو اس کے پاس نہیں تھیں نہ اس کے پاس رسالت و نبوت تھی نہ اس کے پاس زکوۃ تھی اور دنیا کی تمام اشیاء تو اس کے پاس نہیں تھیں اور اس کی بداہت جس شاہد اور مخصص ہے واما العادة يا مخصص غیر کلامی العادة ہوگی نحولا یا کل راساً عادہ اس سے عصفور و حمام کاراس خارج ہوگا کیونکہ اس کا اطلاق اس راس پر ہو گا جس کو تنور میں داخل کر کے بنایا اور کھایا جاتا ہے عرف اور عادہ میں اس کا اطلاق راس عصفور اور فاختہ پر نہیں کیا جاتا لہذا اس عام سے وہ خارج ہوں گے تو راس سے مراد راس غنم و بقر مراد ہوگا۔ واماكون بعض الافراد یا اس عام کے بعض افراد میں نقص في صدق المفہوم والمعنى ہے تو وہ لفظ ان افراد کے علاوہ دوسرے افراد پر صادق بالاولویت ہوگا نحو كل مملوك لى فهو حر تو اس لفظ مملوک میں مکاتب داخل نہیں کیونکہ اس میں مملوکیتہ ناقصہ ہے یدا ازاد ہے اور رقبہ مملوک ہے حتی کہ مولی اس کے مکاسب کا مالک نہیں بلکہ مکاتب خود آپ اپنے مکاسب کا مالک ہے۔ دسیمی مشککا اور اس کا نام مشکلک ہے یعنی لفظ مملوک مشکل ہے کہ اس کا صدق علی الأفراد بالتفاوت ہے۔ اوزاشدا اس کا عطف ناقصا پر ہے یعنی بعض افراد لفظ عام کے مفہوم سے کچھ زیادہ معنی رکھتے ہیں کا لفا لصة جسے لفظ فالکھہ یہ عنب پر صادق نہیں آئیں گا کیونکہ لفظ فاکھہ تفکر سے ماخوذ ہے جس کا معنی تلذذ ہے عند الامام فاکھہ اس کو کہا جائیگا جو صرف تلزر کی خاطر کھایا جائے اور اس میں غذائیت اور دوائیت نہ ہو تو عنب - تمر نخل - رمان ان کے اندر تلزز کے علاوہ غذائیت موجود ہے یعنی روٹی کی بجائے ان پر گزر اوقات ہو سکتا ہے تو ان کے اندر تفکہ سے زیادہ معنی موجود اگر کوئی شخص حلف اٹھاتا ہے لایا کل فاکھہ اور فاکھہ کے متعلق اس کی کوئی نیست وارادہ نہیں ہے تو تمر نخل اور عنب ورمان کھانے سے حانث نہیں ہوگا ۔ ففى غير المستقل عام اس قصر علی البعض کے بعد باقی افراد پر اس عام کا اطلاق علی سبیل الحقیقۃ ہوگا یا علی سبیل المجاز اور اس قصر کے بعد عام قطعی رہیگا یا ظنی ہو جائیگا۔ اس کی تفصیل کرتے ہوئے کیا ففی غیر المستقل یعنی اس صورت میں کہ جب وہ شئی جو موجب ہے قصر عام کی غیر مستقل ہو تو دهوای العام حقیقة فی البواتی یعنی اس وقت باقی پر عام کا اطلاق على سبيل الحقیقہ ہوگا لان الواضع الخ یہ اس اطلاق حقیقی کی دلیل ہے یعنی واضع
Or the restriction of the general to some parts occurs with an independent [specifier], and it is this that is called specification. And 'independent' is that which, in the definition of 'non-independent', was said to be speech that is not related to the primary speech and is not complete in itself; in that case 'independent' also refers to that which is not speech at all, like reason and so on, or it is speech but not related to the primary and is complete in itself. Therefore it is said: specification is either by speech or by other than speech. Other than speech includes reason, like 'Creator of everything' — it is known necessarily that Allah is excluded from that 'everything' meaning from the created things; reason says that Allah is not included among created things because He is the absolute Creator, there is no creator besides Him, so how could He be included? Otherwise He would be the creator of Himself, and a thing being the creator of itself is rationally impossible because it would entail the thing preceding itself in existence, which is false. And the specification of the minor and the insane: the general addresses of the Shari'ah like 'establish prayer', 'give zakat', 'fast Ramadan' etc., the minor and insane are excluded from these commands. This is of the same category as the rational. As for the other-than-speech specifier that is pure [?] like regarding Bilqis: 'she was given of every thing' — from this 'every thing' several things are excluded that she did not have; she had no prophethood, no zakat, etc. And as for custom: a non-speech specifier is custom, like 'do not eat a head' — by custom, the heads of sparrows and pigeons are excluded because the common usage refers to heads that are cooked in the oven and eaten; custom does not apply to heads of birds. So from the general 'head' they are excluded, and the intended meaning is heads of sheep and cows. And as for when some individuals have a deficiency in the applicability of the concept and meaning, then the word applies to other individuals with priority, like 'every slave of mine is free' — the mukatab (slave contract) is not included because his slavery is deficient; his hand is free and his neck is owned, but the master does not own his earnings; the mukatab owns his own earnings. This is called 'mushakkik' (equivocal), its name is 'mushkil' — meaning the word 'slave' is problematic because its applicability to individuals varies. Or like 'fruit' (fakihah) — the word does not apply to grapes because the word 'fakihah' is derived from 'tafakkuh' which means enjoyment; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'fakihah' is that which is eaten only for enjoyment, without being nutritious or medicinal. Grapes, dates, and pomegranates have nutritive value besides enjoyment, so if someone swears 'I will not eat fruit' without intending fruit, then eating dates, grapes, or pomegranates does not break the oath. So for the non-independent [specifier], after the restriction to some, does the general apply to the remaining in the literal sense or metaphorical? And after this restriction, is the general definitive or presumptive? The detail: when the cause of restriction of the general is non-independent, then the usage of the general on the remaining is literal because the word setter [wad'i]...
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This extensive passage is a detailed classification of mukhassis (specifiers) in Hanafi usul. It divides specifiers into two types: mustaqill (independent) and ghayr mustaqill (non-independent). Independent specifiers are those that are not part of the original speech; they can be rational ('aql), like the exclusion of Allah from generality of 'Creator of everything', or customary ('urf), like excluding bird heads from the word 'head' based on common usage. Non-independent specifiers are part of the speech itself, like conditions, attributes, or limits. The passage also discusses a third type: deficiency in the concept's applicability (naqs fi sidq al-mafhum), where a word does not fully apply to some individuals due to deficiency in meaning, like 'mukatab' not fully being a slave. The example of 'fakihah' (fruit) according to Imam Abu Hanifa: it excludes nutritious fruits. The passage ends by discussing the effect of a non-independent specifier on the remaining generality: it remains literal (haqiqah) and the general remains definitive (qat'i) or becomes presumptive (zanni)? The text begins to answer but is cut off.

Key Terms
المستقل (al-mustaqill): An independent specifier that is not part of the original speech; it can be reason, custom, or other non-speech factors.
العقل (al-aql): Reason as a source of specification, e.g., excluding Allah from general created things.
العادة (al-ada): Custom or common practice that can specify general terms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is an example of a rational (aql) independent specifier?
A) Excluding bird heads from the term 'head' based on custom.
B) Excluding Allah from the generality of 'Creator of everything'.
C) Excluding minors from general prayer commands.
D) Excluding dates from the term 'fruit' based on nutritional value.

Key Takeaway
Independent specifiers like reason and custom allow general texts to be restricted based on external evidence, preserving both the literal meaning and rational/customary context.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
Non-Independent Specifiers and the Deficiency Case (Ghayr Mustaqill and Naqs fi Sidq al-Mafhum)
Non-independent specifiers and deficiency in meaning in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish non-independent specifiers from deficiency cases and apply the Hanafi ruling on 'fakihah' in oaths.

Core Idea
Non-independent specifiers are part of the text; deficiency in meaning can also restrict a general term, as in 'fakihah' excluding nutritious fruits.

Not all specification comes from external sources. Non-independent specifiers (ghayr mustaqill) are conditions, attributes, or limits within the speech itself. Additionally, some words have a deficiency (naqs) in their applicability, so they do not fully apply to certain individuals. This lesson explores these concepts using the famous Hanafi example of 'fakihah' (fruit) and the case of a mukatab (a slave with a contract of manumission).

Guided Path
1
Define ghayr mustaqill
A non-independent specifier is part of the original speech, such as a condition (shart), attribute (sifah), or limit (ghayah). It restricts the general without being separate from the text.
Examples: 'If you travel, shorten prayer' restricts the general command of prayer.
2
Understand deficiency in applicability (naqs fi sidq al-mafhum)
Some words do not fully apply to certain individuals because those individuals lack some element of the meaning. Example: 'slave' (mamluk) does not fully apply to a mukatab because his slavery is deficient; he has partial freedom.
This is different from explicit specification; it's a built-in limitation.
3
Analyze the 'fakihah' case
Imam Abu Hanifa defines 'fakihah' (fruit) as items eaten purely for enjoyment, excluding nutritive fruits like dates and grapes. So if someone swears not to eat 'fakihah', eating dates does not break the oath because dates are not 'fakihah' by this definition.
This is based on linguistic derivation from 'tafakkuh' (enjoyment) and custom.
4
Determine effect on remaining generality
For non-independent specifiers, the general remains literal (haqiqah) for the remaining individuals, and the general remains definitive (qat'i) or presumptive (zanni) depending on the type of specifier.
The passage begins to discuss this but is cut off; however, the key is that specification does not render the general metaphorical.

Or the restriction of the general to some parts occurs with an independent [specifier], and it is this that is called specification. And 'independent' is that which, in the definition of 'non-independent', was said to be speech that is not related to the primary speech and is not complete in itself; in that case 'independent' also refers to that which is not speech at all, like reason and so on, or it is speech but not related to the primary and is complete in itself. Therefore it is said: specification is either by speech or by other than speech. Other than speech includes reason, like 'Creator of everything' — it is known necessarily that Allah is excluded from that 'everything' meaning from the created things; reason says that Allah is not included among created things because He is the absolute Creator, there is no creator besides Him, so how could He be included? Otherwise He would be the creator of Himself, and a thing being the creator of itself is rationally impossible because it would entail the thing preceding itself in existence, which is false. And the specification of the minor and the insane: the general addresses of the Shari'ah like 'establish prayer', 'give zakat', 'fast Ramadan' etc., the minor and insane are excluded from these commands. This is of the same category as the rational. As for the other-than-speech specifier that is pure [?] like regarding Bilqis: 'she was given of every thing' — from this 'every thing' several things are excluded that she did not have; she had no prophethood, no zakat, etc. And as for custom: a non-speech specifier is custom, like 'do not eat a head' — by custom, the heads of sparrows and pigeons are excluded because the common usage refers to heads that are cooked in the oven and eaten; custom does not apply to heads of birds. So from the general 'head' they are excluded, and the intended meaning is heads of sheep and cows. And as for when some individuals have a deficiency in the applicability of the concept and meaning, then the word applies to other individuals with priority, like 'every slave of mine is free' — the mukatab (slave contract) is not included because his slavery is deficient; his hand is free and his neck is owned, but the master does not own his earnings; the mukatab owns his own earnings. This is called 'mushakkik' (equivocal), its name is 'mushkil' — meaning the word 'slave' is problematic because its applicability to individuals varies. Or like 'fruit' (fakihah) — the word does not apply to grapes because the word 'fakihah' is derived from 'tafakkuh' which means enjoyment; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'fakihah' is that which is eaten only for enjoyment, without being nutritious or medicinal. Grapes, dates, and pomegranates have nutritive value besides enjoyment, so if someone swears 'I will not eat fruit' without intending fruit, then eating dates, grapes, or pomegranates does not break the oath. So for the non-independent [specifier], after the restriction to some, does the general apply to the remaining in the literal sense or metaphorical? And after this restriction, is the general definitive or presumptive? The detail: when the cause of restriction of the general is non-independent, then the usage of the general on the remaining is literal because the word setter [wad'i]...
