Commentary
This extensive passage is a detailed classification of mukhassis (specifiers) in Hanafi usul. It divides specifiers into two types: mustaqill (independent) and ghayr mustaqill (non-independent). Independent specifiers are those that are not part of the original speech; they can be rational ('aql), like the exclusion of Allah from generality of 'Creator of everything', or customary ('urf), like excluding bird heads from the word 'head' based on common usage. Non-independent specifiers are part of the speech itself, like conditions, attributes, or limits. The passage also discusses a third type: deficiency in the concept's applicability (naqs fi sidq al-mafhum), where a word does not fully apply to some individuals due to deficiency in meaning, like 'mukatab' not fully being a slave. The example of 'fakihah' (fruit) according to Imam Abu Hanifa: it excludes nutritious fruits. The passage ends by discussing the effect of a non-independent specifier on the remaining generality: it remains literal (haqiqah) and the general remains definitive (qat'i) or becomes presumptive (zanni)? The text begins to answer but is cut off.

Key Terms
غير المستقل (ghayr al-mustaqill): A non-independent specifier that is part of the original speech, such as a condition, attribute, or limit.
الفاكهة (al-fakihah): According to Imam Abu Hanifa, fruit eaten purely for enjoyment, excluding nutritious fruits.
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has a contract to purchase his freedom; his status is partially free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if someone swears 'I will not eat fruit (fakihah)' and then eats dates, what is the ruling?
A) The oath is broken because dates are fruit.
B) The oath is not broken because dates are not considered 'fakihah'.
C) The oath is broken only if he intended dates.
D) The oath is not broken unless he eats more than three dates.

Key Takeaway
Non-independent specifiers and deficiency in meaning restrict general terms based on internal textual features or incomplete applicability, as seen in the rulings on mukatab and 'fakihah'.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Effect of Specification on General Terms: Haqiqat, Majaz, and Certainty
Analyzing how general terms after specification are used literally or metaphorically and their certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between independent and non-independent specifiers and determine whether a specified general term is used literally or metaphorically and the level of certainty (qat'i or zanni).

Core Idea
Specification by non-independent specifiers (like custom) keeps the general literal and definitive; independent specifiers make it metaphorical and speculative—except for rational specifiers.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the effect of specification (takhsis) on a general term (amm) is not uniform. The passage you are about to study explains that the type of specifier—whether independent or non-independent—determines whether the term remains literal (haqiqah) or becomes metaphorical (majaz), and whether its probative value remains definitive (qat'i) or becomes speculative (zanni). This distinction has direct implications for legal proofs and oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of specifiers
The text divides specifiers into non-independent (ghair mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Note examples: custom (urf) and deficiency in meaning for non-independent; separate textual evidence or reason for independent.
Non-independent specifiers are essentially clarifications of the meaning inherent in the term or context, not external restrictions.
2
Analyze the effect of non-independent specifiers
When a specifier is non-independent, the general term remains literal because the word's coinage (wad') is for the remaining individuals after the specifier's operation. The text also states such a general is a definitive proof (qat'i) provided the exception is known.
Example: custom excludes heads of small birds from 'head' in an oath; the term stays literal for sheep heads.
3
Analyze the effect of independent specifiers
Independent specifiers make the general term metaphorical from the perspective of restriction (since the word 'all' is applied to part), but still literal from the perspective of encompassing the remaining. The proof becomes speculative (zanni).
Scholars universally agreed that independent specifiers yield zanni proofs, regardless of whether the specifier is verbal or non-verbal.
4
Apply the exception for rational specifiers
The text notes a key exception: if the specifier is reason (aql), the general remains definitive because rational specification is treated like an implicit exception. Example: Quranic addresses to believers exclude children and the insane by reason, yet remain qat'i.
This exception is crucial for foundational texts like the Quranic commands for prayer and fasting.

From 'every thing' now from this 'every' many items are excluded that were not with him, neither prophethood nor messengerhood was with him nor was zakah with him, and all worldly things were not with him. And its obviousness that which is evidence and specifier. And as for custom (al-ada) or a non-verbal specifier, custom will be like 'he swore not to eat any head' — from this, the head of sparrow and pigeon will be excluded because the application of 'head' is on the head that is put in the oven and cooked and eaten; in custom and habit, this term is not applied to the head of sparrow and dove. Therefore, they will be excluded from this general term, so 'head' means head of sheep and cattle. And as for some individuals having a deficiency in the truthfulness of the concept and meaning, that word will be valid for other individuals by priority. For example: 'Every slave I have is free' — in this, the word 'slave' (mamluk) does not include a mukatib because his slavehood is deficient; his hand is free but his neck is owned, such that the master does not own his earnings, rather the mukatib himself owns his earnings. ... So in the non-independent (ghair mustaqill) [specification], the general term after this restriction to some [individuals] will be applied to the remaining individuals in a literal sense or in a metaphorical sense, and after this restriction will the general remain definitive or become speculative. Detailing this: For the non-independent, i.e., when the thing that causes restriction of the general is non-independent, then the general remains literal in the remaining, because the coinage (al-wadi') ... This is proof for literal application: the coinage placed this word for the remaining after exclusion, so using the word in what it was coined for is literal. So this general that was restricted by non-independent [specifier] is a proof without doubt in the remaining, i.e., a definitive proof, provided the exception is known individuals; if the exception is unknown, then it will not be a definitive proof. For the independent, i.e., when the restrictor is independent, whether speech or non-speech, terminologically this is called specification (takhsis). Then the general term's application to the remaining is metaphorical because the word 'all' is applied to some from the perspective of restriction — this is using the word for part of what it is named for, so it is metaphorical. But from the perspective of encompassing (tawin?) it is literal, because the general's meaning was to encompass all named, and similarly this encompasses all remaining. So it is a proof that has uncertainty, i.e., it is a speculative proof, not definitive. And they did not differentiate [scholars] between the two types, i.e., whether the independent specifier is speech or non-speech, but they said absolutely that every general that has been specified by an independent specifier becomes a proof with uncertainty, i.e., speculative, not definitive. But here a distinction must be made: if the general is specified by reason (al-aql), then despite this specification the general remains definitive, not speculative, because it is in the ruling of an exception. Because this rational specification is like an exception, and based on reason, the exception is omitted. It is as if this matter is settled: that individuals excluded by a rational specifier are like an exception, and when the exception is known, the remainder remains a definitive proof. Allah's saying: 'O you who have believed, when you rise to prayer...' and similar general legal addresses from which reason excludes the child and the insane — these are definitive proofs despite this rational specification, to the extent that their denier is deemed a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary discusses the effect of specification (takhsis) on a general term. The author distinguishes between two types of specifiers: non-independent (ghair mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Non-independent specifiers are those that do not originate from the speaker's own independent statement, such as custom (urf) or a deficiency in the very meaning of the term for some individuals. For example, when someone swears not to eat 'any head', custom excludes heads of small birds like sparrows, so the general term 'head' remains literal and definitive for the remaining (heads of sheep, etc.). Similarly, the term 'slave' (mamluk) lacks full truthfulness for a mukatib (a slave under contract of manumission) because his ownership is partial, so the general excludes him by priority. In such cases, the general term remains literal and is a definitive proof (qat'i). The second type is independent specifier (mustaqill), which is an external evidence that restricts the general, such as a separate verse or logical evidence. In this case, the general term becomes metaphorical (majaz) in its application to the remaining individuals, because it is now used for part of what it was originally coined for. However, from the perspective of encompassing the remaining individuals, it is still literal. Its probative value becomes speculative (zanni), not definitive, because independent specification introduces uncertainty. The author notes that scholars generally held this view regardless of whether the independent specifier is verbal or non-verbal. However, a crucial exception is made: when the specifier is reason (aql), the general remains definitive. For example, the Quranic address 'O you who believe, when you rise to prayer' (5:6) is general to all believers, but reason necessarily excludes children and the insane. This rational specification is treated like an implicit exception, so the general remains a definitive proof. Denying such rulings can even lead to disbelief, indicating their certainty. This distinction is important in Hanafi usul for determining the strength of legal evidence.

Key Terms
مخصص غیر مستقل (mukhassis ghair mustaqill): A specifier that is not an independent evidence, such as custom (urf) or deficiency in meaning (naqs fi al-mafhum).
مخصص مستقل (mukhassis mustaqill): An independent specifier, whether textual or rational, that is external to the general term's own meaning.
حقیقت (haqiqah): Literal usage, when a word is used for what it was coined for.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage, when a word is used for something other than its original coinage.
قطعی (qat'i): Definitive proof that yields certainty.
ظنی (zanni): Speculative proof that does not yield certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a general term specified by an independent specifier (e.g., a separate verse)?
A) It remains literal and definitive.
B) It becomes metaphorical and speculative.
C) It becomes metaphorical but remains definitive.
D) It remains literal but becomes speculative.

Key Takeaway
The type of specifier (independent vs non-independent) determines whether a general term after specification is used literally (haqiqah) and is definitive (qat'i) or metaphorically (majaz) and speculative (zanni), with the exception of rational specifiers which keep it definitive.

Non-Independent Specifiers and Hujjiyyah of 'Amm
Explaining the rule for non-independent specifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a specifier is non-independent and state whether the general remains qat'i or not based on the condition of known exception.

Core Idea
A general specified by an explicit exception remains definitive if the exception is known.

In Hanafi usul, not all specification reduces the evidentiary value of a general text. This lesson introduces the first type of specifier—non-independent, such as an explicit exception—and explains that it preserves the general's definitiveness, provided the excepted individuals are specified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specifier type
Determine whether the specifier is part of the speech (like istithna') or an external evidence. Non-independent specifiers are those that are attached to the general statement, e.g., 'except'.
The passage calls this 'ghayr mustaqill'.
2
Check the condition of knowledge
If the excepted individuals are known, the general remains a definitive proof. If the exception is unknown, the general becomes speculative because the remainder is ambiguous.
The passage explicitly states the condition: 'بشرطیکہ استثنا معلومہ افراد کا ہو'.
3
Apply the rule
When the specifier is non-independent and the exception is known, the general is qat'i. Otherwise, it is zanni.

بالمستقل کر لی گئی ہے یا ایک ایسی حجت ہے جس میں شبہہ ہے یعنی یہ حجبت ظنیہ ہے قطعیہ نہیں ہے ۔ ولم يفرقوا بین گونہ او یعنی علماء نے اس میں فرق نہیں کیا کہ کا مخصص مستقل کلام ہو یا غیر کلام بلکہ علی الاطلاق قول کر دیا کہ ہر وہ عام جس کی تخصیص مخصص مستقل سے ہو جائے وہ ایسی دلیل بن جاتا ہے جس کے اندر شبہ پیدا ہو جاتا ہے یعنی ظنی ہو جاتا ہے قطعی نہیں رہتا ۔ لكن يجب هناك فرق لیکن اس مقام تخصیص میں فرق کرنا لازم و واجب ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر عام مخصوص بالعقل ہو یعنی مخصص عقل ہو تو اس تخصیص کے باوجود عام قطعی رسیگا ظنی نہیں ہوگا لانه في حكم الاستثناء کیونکہ یہ تخصیص عقلی بحکم استثناء ہوتی ہے اور اعتماد عقلی کی بنیاد پر استثنا محذوف ہوتا ہے ۔ على انه مفروغ عنه گویا یہ مسئلہ مفروغ عنہا ہے نے کہ عقلی مخصص کے ساتھ جو افراد خارج ہوتے ہیں وہ بحکم استثناء ہیں اور جب استثنا معلوم ہو تو باقی میں حجتہ قطعیہ رہیگا اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول پایہا الذین آمنوا اذا قمتم الى الصلوۃ اور اس جیسے خطابات شرعیہ عامہ جن سے عقلا صبی و مجنون مستثنیٰ ہیں یہ مجھے قطعیہ میں جتنا خطابات وارد بالفرائض میں باوجود اس تخصیص عقلی کے قطعیہ ہیں حتی کہ ان کے منکر کو کافر قرار دیا جائیں گے کیونکہ تخصیص بالعقل مورث شبہ نہیں ہوتی عقل جن کی تخصیص کا موجب ہوگاوہ ستثنیٰ ہو جائیں گے باقی بالقطع درج فی الخطاب رہیں گے ۔ اگر مخصص غیر کلامی عقل کے علاوہ عادۃ یا حس اور زیادہ معنی وغیرہ ہو تو پھر کہا جاتا ہے کہ عام قطعی نہیں رہے گا۔ کیونکہ عادات مختلف ہوا کرتی ہیں اور زیادہ ونقصان کے سمجھنے میں خفا ہوتا ہے اور حس تفاصیل ایشیاء پر پوری اطلاع حاصل نہیں کر سکتی الا یہ کہ قدر مخصوص کا علم قطعی نہو جاتے تو عام قطعی رہیگا والا فلا ۔ مصنف اس فرق کے ذکر کرنے میں منفرد ہے اور کسٹی نے ذکر نہیں کیا حالانکہ یہ فرق ضروری ہے ۔ ولنعم ما فرق واللہ درہ ۔
He himself placed this word for the rest from which some individuals have been excepted; therefore this use of the word for what it was placed is real. So the general [ʿāmm] which was restricted to some with a non-independent restriction is a proof in the remainder without doubt, that is, it is a definitive proof, not speculative, provided that the exception is of known individuals. If the exception is unknown, then it will not be a definitive proof. As for the independent, in the case where the restrictor is independent, whether it be speech or non-speech, then terminologically it is called specification [takhṣīṣ], whether the specifier is speech or non-speech. Then at that time the application of the general word to the remainder is of the category of metaphor, because the name of the whole is applied to a part from the perspective of restriction. So it is metaphor because it is use of the word for part of what it names. From the perspective of coverage it is real, meaning that it covers the remaining individuals universally, so in that respect it is real. So it is a proof with suspicion, i.e., it is a speculative proof, not definitive. And they did not distinguish between types, meaning the scholars did not differentiate whether the independent specifier is speech or non-speech; rather they stated absolutely that every general that has been specified by an independent specifier becomes a proof in which suspicion arises, i.e., it becomes speculative, not definitive. But there must be a distinction: if the general is specified by reason, i.e., the specifier is reason, then despite this specification the general will remain definitive, not speculative, because it is in the status of exception. For this rational specification is in the status of exception, and based on reason a deleted exception exists. It is as if settled, meaning this issue is settled, that those individuals excluded by a rational specifier are in the status of exception, and when the exception is known, the remainder remains a definitive proof. Allah's saying: 'O you who believe, when you stand for prayer' and similar general legal addresses from which the child and the insane are rationally excepted; these are definitive until the addresses about obligatory acts, despite this rational specification, are definitive, even to the point that their denier is declared an unbeliever, because specification by reason does not cause suspicion. Those whom reason necessitates exclusion will be excepted, the remainder definitively remain included in the address. If the non-verbal specifier is other than reason—custom, sense, or increase of meaning etc.—then it is said that the general will not remain definitive, because customs vary and understanding increase and decrease is hidden, and sense cannot obtain complete information of the details of things, unless the specified amount becomes definitive knowledge, then the general remains definitive. The author is unique in mentioning this distinction, and no one else mentioned it, though it is necessary. How excellent is this distinction, may Allah reward him.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage discusses the evidentiary value (hujjiyyah) of a general text (ʿāmm) after it has been specified (takhṣīṣ). The author distinguishes between two types of specifiers (mukhassis): non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). The first type, non-independent specifier, is exemplified by an explicit exception (istithnā') attached to the general statement. Since the general word was originally placed to include all individuals, and the exception carves out some, the use of the general word for the remainder is a real use (ḥaqīqah) because the word was placed for that meaning from the start. Thus the general remains a definitive proof (ḥujjah qaṭʿiyyah) as long as the excepted individuals are known. If the exception is unknown, the remainder becomes unknown and the proof loses its definitiveness. The second type, independent specifier, is an external evidence (whether textual or non-textual) that limits the general. In this case, the application of the general word to the remainder is metaphorical (majāz) from the perspective of restriction, but from the perspective of coverage it is still real because the general word encompasses the remaining individuals. However, due to the external restriction, the general becomes a speculative proof (ḥujjah ẓanniyyah). The author notes that earlier scholars did not differentiate between different kinds of independent specifiers; they ruled that any independent specification makes the general speculative. But the author argues for a crucial distinction: if the specifier is reason (ʿaql), the general remains definitive. Reason-based specification is akin to an implicit exception (istithnā' maḥdhūf), which, when the excepted individuals are known, does not affect the definitiveness of the general. Examples include the Qur'anic verse 'O you who believe, when you stand for prayer' which addresses all believers, but reason excludes children and the insane. Such general texts are so definitive that denying them may constitute disbelief. On the other hand, if the non-verbal specifier is custom (ʿādah), sense (ḥiss), or increase of meaning (ziyādah maʿnā), the general becomes speculative because these can vary or be ambiguous. The exception is if the specified amount is known definitively, then it remains qaṭʿī. The author concludes by praising his own unique contribution of this distinction.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A word that covers all its individuals without restriction.
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): The specification of a general term by an evidence that excludes some of its individuals.
مخصص (mukhaṣṣiṣ): The evidence that specifies the general, either independent or non-independent.
حجت قطعیہ (ḥujjah qaṭʿiyyah): A definitive proof that yields certain knowledge.
حجت ظنیہ (ḥujjah ẓanniyyah): A speculative proof that yields probable knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the hujjiyyah of a general text specified by a non-independent specifier when the excepted individuals are unknown?
A) Definitive (qaṭʿī)
B) Speculative (ẓannī)
C) Invalid (bāṭil)
D) It remains definitive but only in the remainder.

Key Takeaway
A general specified by a non-independent specifier remains a definitive proof only if the excepted individuals are known.

Independent Specifiers and the Unique Case of Reason-Based Takhsis
Explaining the rule for independent specifiers and the exception for reason

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between specification by reason and other independent specifiers, and determine the hujjiyyah of the general accordingly.

Core Idea
Specification by reason leaves the general definitive; other independent specifiers make it speculative.

Most specifiers that are external to the general statement (independent specifiers) reduce its evidentiary value to speculative. However, the author makes a crucial exception: when the specifier is reason (ʿaql), the general remains definitive. This lesson explores that distinction and its implications, using the example of the Qur'anic address to believers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specifier as independent
An independent specifier is not part of the general statement; it can be a separate text, custom, sense, or reason. The passage calls this 'mustaqill'.
2
Check if the specifier is reason (ʿaql)
If the specifier is reason (e.g., excluding children and insane from address because they lack capacity), the general remains qat'i. Reason-based specification is treated like an implicit exception (istithnā' maḥdhūf).
The passage says: 'لكن يجب هناك فرق' and explains the distinction.
3
Apply the default rule for other independent specifiers
If the independent specifier is not reason (e.g., custom, sense, or a separate text), the general becomes zanni. The only exception is if the specified amount is known definitively.
Customs vary, sense perceptions are limited, so these introduce uncertainty.

Commentary

عام (ʿāmm): A word that covers all its individuals without restriction.

مخصص (mukhaṣṣiṣ): The evidence that specifies the general, either independent or non-independent.

Al-Karkhi's Doctrine: General Text Specified by Verbal Specifier Has No Probative Value
Presenting al-Karkhi's view that a general specified by a verbal specifier is not a proof at all

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate al-Karkhi's argument that a general text specified by a verbal specifier has no probative value, and contrast it with the opposing view.

Core Idea
Al-Karkhi: a general text loses all probative force if specified by any verbal specifier — even if the exception is known.

In Hanafi usul, the effect of specification (takhṣīṣ) on a general text (ʿāmm) is a critical question. While many usulis hold that a specified general becomes speculative (ẓannī), the great Hanafi Imam al-Karkhi argued a more radical position: once any verbal specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ bi al-kalām) is attached, the general ceases to be a proof (ḥujjah) entirely. This lesson unpacks his reasoning for both known and unknown exceptions and introduces the dissenting view within the school.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two cases
Al-Karkhi divides the issue into two scenarios: when the amount specified (qadr mukhaṣṣaṣ) is known (e.g., musta'min exception) and when it is unknown (e.g., riba). Identify each from the text.
Musta'min is known because the exception is explicit; riba is unknown because the precise amount of prohibited interest is not specified.
2
Analyze the unknown case
Understand al-Karkhi's analogy: an unknown exception renders the entire statement ambiguous. Since specification is like exception, an unknown specified amount makes the general's remainder unknown, so no ruling can be derived.
The reasoning rests on the principle that exception (istithnā') clarifies exclusion; if the exception is unknown, the original statement's scope is unknown.
3
Analyze the known case
Even when the specified amount is known, al-Karkhi argues that the specifier implies a cause (ʿillah) for the exception. The extent of this cause is uncertain, so the remainder's scope becomes unknown, destroying probative value.
Example: the musta'min exception suggests a cause (e.g., protection), but we cannot know if it applies to other polytheists as well.
4
Contrast with the opposing view
'Some scholars' (البعض) hold that if the specified amount is known, the general remains a proof for the remainder. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: for al-Karkhi, no proof; for them, a speculative proof.
This difference fundamentally affects how one uses a general text after specification.

واما المخصوص با لکلام یعنی وہ عام جو مخصوص بالکلام ہو اور اس کے لئے مخصص کلام ہے عقل وغیرہ نہیں تو کرخی کے نزدیک وہ حجت اصلا نہیں ہے خواہ قدر مخصوص معلوم ہو جیسے مستامن جو اللہ تعالی کے قول اقتلوا المشرکین میں سے مخصوص اور خارج ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول ان احد من المشرکین استجارک فاجرہ کے ساتھ کیونکہ یہ آیت بیان کر رہی ہے۔ که مستامن اقتلوا کے حکم میں داخل نہیں ہے او مجهولا یا قدر مخصوص من العام مجہول ہو جیسے ریوا جو اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول اصل اللہ البیع سے مخصوص اور خارج ہے ان دونوں صورتوں کرخی کے نزدیک عام حجت نہیں رہتا۔ لانه ان كان مجهول الخمر یہ گرمی کی دلیل خلاصہ یہ کہ اگر مقدار مخصوص مجہول ہے تو باقی بھی مجہول ہو جائے گا معلوم نہیں ہو گا کہ حکم کے تحت باقی کتنا مقدار داخل ہے لان التخصیص کیونکہ تخصیص بمنزلہ استثناء کے ہے جو یہ بیان کرتی ہے کہ مخصوص تحت العام داخل نہیں جیسے استثناء بیان کرتا ہے کہ مستثنی صدر کلام میں داخل نہیں ہے اور استثناء جب مجہول ہو تو صدر کلام باقی کے حق میں مجہول ہو جائیگا لہذا اس سے حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا ۔ وان کان معلوما اگر قدر مخصوص معلوم ہونا لظاهران يكون معللاً تو ظاہر یہ ہے کہ یہ معلل بالتعلیل ہوگا کیونکہ یہ مخصص کلام مستقل ہے اور نصوص میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ معلل بالتعلیل ہوتی ہیں اور حکم منصوص میں کوئی نہ کوئی علت ضرور ہوتی ہے ۔ ولایدری کم یخرج آب معلوم نہیں ہو سکے گا کہ اس تعلیل و علت کے ساتھ کتنا خارج ہوئے ہیں جب خارج شدہ کا علم نہ ہوا تو باقی بھی مجہول ہو جائیگا لہذا ایسے عام کے ساتھ حجت قائم نہیں رہ سکتی وعند البعض اور بمن حضرات کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ اگر قدر مخصوص معلوم ہے تو عام ان مخصوص مقدار کے
As for what is specified by speech—i.e., the general that has been specified by a verbal specifier, not reason etc.—then according to al-Karkhi it is not a proof at all, whether the specified amount is known, like the musta'min (safe-conduct recipient) who is specified and excluded from Allah's saying 'Kill the polytheists' by His saying 'If any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection' because this verse explains that the musta'min is not included in the command to kill; or unknown, like riba (usury) which is specified and excluded from Allah's saying 'Allah has permitted trade'. In both cases, according to al-Karkhi, the general does not remain a proof. Because if the specified amount is unknown, then the remainder also becomes unknown; it will not be known how much of the remainder is included under the ruling. Since specification is in the position of exception, which explains that the specified is not included under the general, just as exception explains that the excepted is not included in the prior statement. When the exception is unknown, the prior statement becomes unknown with respect to the remainder, so a ruling cannot be established from it. And if it is known—that is, if the specified amount is known—then apparently it would be based on a cause (ta'līl), because this independent verbal specifier is textual, and the principle in texts is that they are based on causes, and a stated ruling necessarily has some cause. But it cannot be known how much is excluded by that cause; when the excluded is unknown, the remainder also becomes unknown, so such a general cannot serve as a proof. And according to some—i.e., some scholars—it is that if the specified amount is known, then the general [remains a proof] regarding the specified amount... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage presents the doctrine of Imam al-Karkhi (a leading Hanafi usuli scholar) regarding a general text that has been specified by a verbal specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ bi al-kalām). Al-Karkhi holds that such a general text has no probative value at all, whether the amount specified is known or unknown. The reasoning is twofold: First, if the specified amount is unknown (e.g., the exact amount of prohibited riba in the general permission of trade), then the remainder of the general is also unknown, similar to an unknown exception in a sentence. Just as an unknown exception renders the entire statement ambiguous, an unknown specification leaves the general's applicability unclear, so no ruling can be derived. Second, if the specified amount is known (e.g., the musta'min being excluded from the general command to kill polytheists), the general is still not a proof because the specification suggests that the general ruling was based on a cause or rationale (ʿillah). Since that cause may also apply to other cases beyond the specified ones, the extent of exclusion is uncertain; one cannot be sure how many individuals are excluded by that cause. Therefore, the general cannot provide certain knowledge. Al-Karkhi's view is stringent: any verbal specification (independent and separate) strips the general of all probative force. The passage then mentions that 'some scholars' (عند البعض) hold a different view: if the specified amount is known, the general remains a proof for the remainder. The text cuts off, but this likely refers to the majority Hanafi position that a known specification by a verbal specifier makes the general speculative (ẓannī) but not completely invalid.

Key Terms
مخصص بالکلام (mukhaṣṣiṣ bi al-kalām): A specifier that is speech (textual evidence) separate from the general statement.
قدر مخصوص (qadr mukhaṣṣaṣ): The amount or individuals specified out of the general.
مستامن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who is granted safe passage into Muslim territory.
ربوا (ribā): Usury or interest, prohibited in Islam.

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi, what is the status of a general text that has been specified by a verbal specifier?
A) It remains a definitive proof.
B) It becomes a speculative proof.
C) It is not a proof at all.
D) It depends on whether the specifier is from the Quran or Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Karkhi's doctrine that a general text specified by a verbal specifier is not a hujja at all challenges the common assumption that specification only weakens the general; it may completely nullify its probative value.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Effect of Verbal and Non-Verbal Specifiers on General Texts
Analyzing the effect of specifiers on the authority of general texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify specifiers as verbal or non-verbal, state the Hanafi position on the authority of a general after specification, and critically evaluate al-Karkhi's argument against the general's authority.

Core Idea
A general text after specification remains a valid proof, but its indication becomes zanni due to the doubt introduced by the specifier.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary examines how different types of specifiers affect the authority of general texts. It distinguishes between non-verbal specifiers (reason, custom, sense) and verbal specifiers, and presents a dispute between al-Karkhi and the Hanafi school regarding the latter. By analyzing this discussion, you will understand the nuanced Hanafi position that a specified general remains a hujjah but with shubhah.

Guided Path
1
Classify the specifier
Identify whether the passage discusses a verbal specifier (مخصص لفظي) or a non-verbal specifier. Note the different effects on the general's qat'iyyah.
Non-verbal specifiers other than reason cause the general to lose qat'iyyah unless the specified amount is known with certainty.
2
Identify the four views on verbal specification
List the positions of al-Karkhi, the first responding group, the second group, and the chosen Hanafi view (وعندنا).
Each view differs on whether the general remains a hujjah and under what conditions.
3
Trace the reasoning
For each view, understand the analogy with exception (istithna) and the role of ta'lil (causal reasoning). Note how al-Karkhi uses ta'lil to invalidate the general, and how the Hanafi response argues that specification is like exception and does not accept ta'lil.
The key point is whether the specifier can be subject to ta'lil like an independent text.
4
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: whether the specified general can be used as proof, and with what degree of certainty.
Al-Karkhi would not use it at all; the Hanafi view uses it as zanni evidence.
5
Appreciate the Hanafi position
Explain why the Hanafi view sees the general as a hujjah with doubt (shubhah), and why this is considered the most balanced approach.
The Hanafi view avoids both extremes of complete rejection or absolute certainty.

وعندنا تمكن فيه شبهة اور یہ مذہب مختار ہے یعنی ہمارے نزدیک یہ عام جس سے بعض مخصوص کر لیا گیا ہے خواہ مقدار مخصوص معلوم ہو یا مجہول یہ ایک ایسی دلیل ہے جس کے اندر شہر ممکن ہو چکا ہے ۔ لانه علم انه غير محمول کیونکہ معلوم ہو چکا کہ یہ عام اپنے ظاہر معنی یعنی ارادہ کل افراد پر محمول نہیں ہے تو اس وقت اس سے بعض افراد على سبيل المجاز مراد ہوں گے یعنی یہ اس کا معنی مجازی ہو گا مثلا جب اس عام کے کل افراد یکصد ہوں اور یہ معلوم ہو کہ پورے یکصد افراد تو مراد نہیں ہیں تو سو سے کم جتنا افراد میں سب مساوی میں اس میں کہ لفظ عام ان تمام میں مجاز ہو سکتا ہے لہذا کوئی عدد معین مراد نہیں ہو سکتا اور نہ تو ترجیح بلا مرجح لازم آئیگی مخصوص مجہول کی صورت میں ترجیح بلا مرح یقینا لازم آتی ہے اگر مخصوص معلوم ہو تو پھر بھی مجموع ما وراء مخصوص کو ظنی ترجیح ہو سکتی ہے قطعی تو نہیں ہو سکتی لہذا شبہ تو متمکن ہو جائیگا ۔ ثم ذكر ثمرة تمكن الشبعه فيه الخ
will go because specification by reason does not cause doubt; those which reason specifies become excluded, the rest remain in the text with certainty. If the specifier is non-verbal other than reason, such as custom, sense, or additional meaning, then it is said that the general will not remain qat'i because customs differ and understanding increase and decrease is hidden, and sense cannot obtain complete knowledge of details of things unless the knowledge of the specified amount becomes certain, then the general will remain qat'i. The author is unique in mentioning this difference and al-Karkhi did not mention it, even though this difference is necessary. How excellent is his differentiation, may Allah bless him. As for the one specified by speech, meaning the general that is specified by a verbal specifier and has a verbal specifier, not reason etc., then according to al-Karkhi it is not a proof at all, whether the specified amount is known, like the musta'min who is specified and excluded from Allah's saying 'Kill the polytheists' by Allah's saying 'If one of the polytheists seeks your protection, grant him protection' because this verse clarifies that the musta'min is not included in the ruling of 'Kill', or unknown, like riba which is specified and excluded from Allah's saying 'Allah has permitted trade'. In both cases according to al-Karkhi the general does not remain a proof. Because if the specified amount is unknown, the remainder also becomes unknown; the amount included under the ruling is not known. Because specification is like exception, which states that the specified is not included under the general, just as exception states that the excepted is not included in the scope of the statement. And when exception is unknown, the scope of the statement becomes unknown with respect to the remainder, so a ruling cannot be proven from it. And if the specified amount is known, it appears that it is subject to ta'lil (causal reasoning) because this verbal specifier is independent, and the principle regarding texts is that they are subject to ta'lil, and there must be some cause for a prescribed ruling. But it is not known how much is excluded by that cause; if the excluded is not known, then the remainder also becomes unknown, so such a general cannot be a proof. And according to some (other group), if the specified amount is known, the general remains a proof for the remainder as it was before specification, because it is like exception in that it clarifies that the specified amount is not included. Since it is like exception, it does not accept ta'lil because exception is not independent and does not accept ta'lil; similarly, specification being like exception does not accept ta'lil. So in the case of exception, the general remains a proof for the remainder as before, and similarly for specification. If the specified amount is unknown, the general does not remain a proof because specification is like exception and an unknown exception renders the remainder unknown. Therefore the general cannot remain a proof for the remaining individuals. And according to some (third view) concerning this general, there is a third school: if the specified amount is known, then as mentioned earlier, the general remains a proof for what is beyond the specified; if unknown, then the specifier itself falls and its ignorance does not transfer to the scope of the statement, unlike exception because it is not independent but is among the dependencies of the scope, so its ignorance transfers and renders the scope unknown. And according to us (our view), doubt has become entrenched in it, and this is the chosen school. According to us, this general from which some have been specified, whether the specified amount is known or unknown, is a proof in which doubt has become possible because it is known that this general is not carried on its apparent meaning (intending all individuals). So at that time, some individuals are intended figuratively (by way of majaz). For example, if the general has one hundred individuals and it is known that all one hundred are not intended, then the number less than one hundred is equal in that the general word can be used figuratively for all of them. Therefore no specific number can be intended, and preference without a preponderant factor would be necessitated. In case of unknown specified amount, preference without preponderant necessarily occurs; if the specified amount is known, then still the totality of what is beyond the specified can have a zanni (speculative) preference, not qat'i, so doubt becomes established. Then he mentioned the outcome of the establishment of doubt.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage from the commentary discusses the effect of different types of specifiers on the authority of general texts. It distinguishes between non-verbal specifiers (like reason, custom, sense) and verbal specifiers. For non-verbal specifiers, the general text loses its qat'i (definitive) status unless the specified amount is known with certainty. For verbal specifiers, the text presents four views: (1) Al-Karkhi's view that the general is not a proof at all, whether the specified amount is known or unknown; (2) Some scholars hold that if the specified amount is known, the general remains a proof for the remainder, but if unknown, it does not; (3) Another group holds that if the specified amount is unknown, the specifier itself is dropped, and the general remains a proof; (4) The chosen view (of the Hanafi school) is that the general after any verbal specification is a proof but with a doubt (shubhah) — it is not qat'i but zanni (speculative). The reasoning involves an analogy with exception (istithna): specification is like exception in clarifying non-inclusion, but unlike exception, verbal specifiers are independent and subject to causal reasoning (ta'lil). The chosen view argues that since the general's apparent meaning (all individuals) is known not to be intended, the remaining individuals are intended figuratively, which introduces doubt as to exactly how many are intended, even if the specified amount is known. Thus the general remains a valid proof but its indication is not certain.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A word that encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.
خاص (khāṣṣ): A word that denotes a specific individual or group.
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): The specification of a general term, removing some of its individuals from its scope.
مخصص (mukhaṣṣiṣ): The evidence that specifies a general text, either verbal (like an exception) or non-verbal (like custom).
حجت (ḥujjah): A proof or authoritative evidence that can be used to derive legal rulings.

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (وعندنا), what is the authority of a general text after verbal specification?
A) It is wholly invalid and cannot be used as proof.
B) It is a definitive proof (qat'i) for the remaining individuals.
C) It is a proof but with doubt (shubhah), making it zanni.
D) It remains a proof only if the specified amount is known.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a general text after specification remains a valid proof (hujjah) but with doubt (shubhah), making its indication speculative (zanni).

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
Hujjiyat al-'Amm after Takhsis: The Hanafi Position of Shubha
Explains the status of a general statement after specification and the Hanafi position of residual shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view on the probative value of a general statement after specification and apply the concept of shubha to determine its legal usability.

Core Idea
After specification, the general remains a proof but with shubha: it is not void, but its meaning becomes uncertain.

When a general text is specified, does it still carry authority? The Hanafi school says yes, but with a twist—the authority is now shaded by doubt (shubha) because the general no longer applies to all its literal instances. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this nuanced position, focusing on the dual analogy to istithna' and naskh, and the practical consequences for further specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What happens to a general statement when a specifier later restricts its application? Does the general lose all probative value or remain valid in the remainder?
This is the core issue addressed in the passage.
2
Examine the analogy to istithna'
The passage states that takhsis is like an exception: it clarifies what is not included but does not nullify the general. An exception does not accept ta'lil (legal reasoning).
This analogy supports the default rule that the general remains a proof in the remainder.
3
Consider the scenario of unknown specification
If the specified portion is unknown, some scholars argue the general cannot be a proof because an unknown exception renders the remainder unknown. The passage presents this as a third opinion.
This creates a challenge to the default rule.
4
Analyze the dual resemblance of the mukhassis
The mukhassis resembles both a nasikh (independent statement that falls without affecting the general) and an istithna' (non-independent, transferring ignorance). This conflict creates shubha.
This is the heart of the Hanafi position: shubha preserves the general's hujjiyya.
5
Determine the practical result
Despite shubha, the general remains actionable (wajib al-‘amal) and can still be specified by khabar wahid and qiyas.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the general retains the rank of an unspecified general in terms of further specification.

معلومہ کو شامل ہے۔ لمشبه الاول يصم تعلیل، تو مخصص معلوم ہونیکی صورت میں شہر اول کی بنیاد پر اس کی سلسل صحیح ہے چونکہ مصنت کی اس عبارت سے متبادر یہ تھا کہ متخصص کو چونکہ مشابہت
Specification: in the remainder, the proof remains valid as it was before specification, like its ruling was before. Because it is like an exception: this specification is like an exception in that it clarifies that the specified portion is not included. When it is like an exception, it does not accept legal reasoning (ta'lil), because an exception is an independent matter that does not accept reasoning. So similarly, specification, which is like an exception, will not accept reasoning. In the case of an exception, the general remains as a proof in the remainder, just as it was before the exception. So it will be the same in specification. If the specified portion is unknown, then the general is not a proof, because specification is like an exception, and an unknown exception renders the remainder unknown. Therefore the general cannot remain a proof in the remaining individuals. According to some, this is a third opinion regarding the aforementioned general. Summary: if the specified portion is known, as previously mentioned, the proof remains in what is outside the specified portion, as it was. If it is unknown, i.e., the specified portion is unknown, then this mukhassis itself falls, and its ignorance does not transfer to the beginning of the speech, unlike an exception, because an exception is not independent but is among the adjuncts of the beginning of the speech, so its ignorance transfers and renders the beginning of the speech unknown. According to us (Hanafis), it is possible that there is shubha (uncertainty) in it, and this is the chosen opinion. That is, in our view, this general from which some part has been specified, whether the specified portion is known or unknown, is a proof in which shubha has become possible. Because it is known that it is not carried on its apparent meaning, i.e., intending all individuals. So at that time, some individuals are intended metaphorically, i.e., it takes a metaphorical meaning. For example, if the total individuals of this general are one hundred, and it is known that all one hundred are not intended, then the less than one hundred individuals are equal in that the general term can be metaphorical for all of them. So no specific number can be intended, and an unjustified preference will not be necessary. In the case of an unknown specified portion, unjustified preference definitely occurs. If the specified portion is known, then the totality of what is outside the specified portion can have a speculative preference, but not definitive. Therefore shubha becomes established. Then he mentioned the result of the possibility of this shubha: that result is that, in our view, this general will take the rank of a general that has not been specified (i.e., the rank according to Imam Shafi'i), meaning its specification by a solitary report (khabar wahid) and analogy (qiyas) will be valid, but it does not nullify argumentation with it. That is, despite this shubha, holding and using this general as a proof is not nullified. Because the mukhassis resembles an abrogator (nasikh), since the mukhassis in its wording is similar to a nasikh because it is independent speech, self-contained in meaning, and conveys a ruling. If there had been no preceding general, it would have carried an independent ruling. So from this aspect, it is similar to a nasikh. And the exception has its ruling: the mukhassis establishes a ruling in what is outside the specified portion and clarifies that the specified portion is not included under the ruling. So from this aspect, it is likened to an exception, just as an exception establishes a ruling in everything except the excepted item and clarifies that the excepted item is not included in the ruling of the beginning of the speech. So this mukhassis has similarity to a nasikh in one respect and similarity to an exception in another respect. If this mukhassis is unknown, i.e., includes unknown individuals, then due to similarity to a nasikh, it itself falls, because an unknown nasikh itself falls, so its ignorance cannot transfer to the general ruling. And due to similarity to an exception, it causes ignorance in the general, because the ignorance of an exception necessitates transfer of ignorance to the beginning of the speech. So from this aspect, the proof with this general should fall. So doubt arises in this falling. Based on this doubt, its established probative value will not fall, but rather it will be actionable, even if it does not produce knowledge and certainty, just like a speculative proof (dalil zanni) is actionable even if it does not produce knowledge. Because before specification, the general was actionable and applicable. When it was specified, doubt arose whether it remains applicable or its application has become void. So due to doubt, its applicability is not void; it remains actionable. And if the mukhassis is known, i.e., it includes known individuals, then based on the first similarity, its chain is correct... (text ends here)
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of specification (takhsis) on a general statement ('amm) and the resulting probative status of the general. The author begins by stating the default rule: when a general is specified, the proof remains valid in the remainder (ma warā' al-mukhaṣṣaṣ), just as before specification. This is because takhsis is analogous to an exception (istithnā'), which clarifies that the excepted portion is not included. An exception does not accept legal reasoning (ta'līl) because it is not an independent ruling; similarly, the specified portion does not accept reasoning. However, if the specified portion is unknown (majhūl), the general cannot remain a proof because an unknown exception renders the remainder unknown. The text then presents a third opinion (attributed to 'some') that distinguishes between known and unknown specified portions: if known, the general remains proof; if unknown, the mukhassis itself falls without affecting the preceding general. The author then clarifies the Hanafi position (mukhtār): whether the specified portion is known or unknown, the general becomes a proof with possible shubha (uncertainty). This is because once a general is known not to apply to all individuals, its meaning becomes metaphorical (majāz), introducing uncertainty about which exact subset is intended. With an unknown specified portion, the analogy to an exception would force ignorance onto the entire general, but because the mukhassis also resembles a nasikh (abrogator) in being an independent statement, it may fall without affecting the general. This dual resemblance creates a conflict (shubha) that prevents the general's probative value from being completely nullified; it remains actionable (wājib al-ʿamal) despite not producing certainty. The practical outcome (thamara) is that such a general can be further specified by khabar wāḥid and qiyās (like an unspecified general according to Imam Shāfiʿī), but it still serves as a proof. The discussion emphasizes the Hanafi method of balancing textual indicators and the role of doubt in preserving established probative value.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A general term that covers all individuals of its category.
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): Specification, i.e., excluding some individuals from the general meaning.
مخصص (mukhaṣṣiṣ): The evidence that specifies the general.
شبہہ (shubha): Uncertainty or doubt that affects the probative value but does not nullify it completely.
حجیت (ḥujjiyya): Probative value or authority of a legal proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what happens to the probative value (hujjiyya) of a general statement ('amm) after it has been specified by an unknown mukhassis?
A) The general loses all probative value and becomes void.
B) The general retains probative value but with shubha (uncertainty), and remains actionable.
C) The mukhassis itself is invalid, and the general remains fully probative without any shubha.
D) The general becomes definitive (qat'i) in the remainder without any uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, specification does not nullify the general; it introduces shubha, but the general remains actionable and can be further specified.

Effect of an Unknown Specifier on the General Text
Analyzing the legal effect of a specifier that is unknown in its individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the effect of an unknown specifier (mukhassis majhul) on the general text (amm) according to the Hanafi school, and apply the principle that doubt does not invalidate established authority.

Core Idea
An unknown specifier creates doubt but does not drop the general text's binding authority.

In Hanafi usul, the relationship between a general text and a specifier is nuanced, especially when the specifier is unknown. This passage explores the subtle debate: a specifier that resembles both an abrogator (nasikh) and an exception (istithna') generates a conflict, but the Hanafi position maintains the general's authority. Understanding this helps us correctly apply general texts when specifications are unclear.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dual nature of the specifier
The passage explains that a mukhassis resembles a nasikh because it is an independent ruling, and resembles an istithna' because it clarifies what remains under the general. This dual resemblance creates tension.
2
Analyze the effect of an unknown specifier
When the mukhassis is majhul (covers unknown individuals), its resemblance to a nasikh would cause it to drop itself (since an unknown abrogation is void), but its resemblance to an istithna' would transfer ignorance to the general. This conflict produces doubt.
3
Determine the outcome: doubt does not invalidate
The doubt does not override the general's established authority (hujjiyyah). The general remains binding for action (wajib al-'amal) though it does not yield certainty. This is analogous to any speculative proof (dalil zanni) that is obligatory to act upon.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i perspective
The text notes that this status is similar to what Imam al-Shafi'i held for a general unspecified in some parts. However, the key Hanafi emphasis is that the general remains hujja despite the doubt.

وہی درجہ اس ممکن شبہ کا ثمرہ اور نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ ہمارے نزدیک اس عام کا نظیرہ ہو جائیگا جو عام غیر مخصوص البعض عنہ کا درجہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک تھا یعنی اس کی تخصیص خبر واحد اور قیاس کے ساتھ کرنی صحیح ہو جائیگی لكن لا يسقط الاحتجاج به یعنی با وجود اس شبہہ کے اس عام کے ساتھ حجت پکڑنا اور احتجاج ساقط نہیں ہوگا ۔ لان المخصص مشبہ الناسخ چونکہ مخصص اپنے صیغہ کے لحاظ سے ناسخ کے ساتھ مشابہ ہے کیونکہ یہ مخصص کلام مستأنف اور مستقل بالمفہوم اور مفید حکم ہے اگر اس سے متقدماً عام موجود نہ ہوتا تو یہ ایک مستقل حکم کا حامل تھا تو اس لحاظ سے مشابہہ بالناسخ ہوا ۔ والاستثناء بحکمہ چونکہ اس مخصص کا حکم یہ ہے کہ ماوراء مخصوص میں حکم ثابت کرتا ہے۔ اور مخصوص کے عدم دخول تحت الحکم کو واضح کرتا ہے تو اس لحاظ سے اس کو تشبیہ بالاستثناء ہوئی جیسے استثناء اثبات حکم ماعدا المستثنیٰ میں کرتا ہے اور یہ واضح کرتا ہے کہ مستثنیٰ صدر کلام کے حکم میں داخل نہیں ہے تو اس مخصص کو من وجہ مشابہت بالناسخ اور من وجہ مشابہت بالاستثناء ہوئی فان کان مجہولا اگر یہ مخصص مجہول ہے یعنی مجہول افراد کو شامل ہے تو مشابہت بالناسخ کی وجہ سے خود ساقط ہو جائیگا کیونکہ ناسخ مجہول خود ساقط ہو جاتا ہے لہذا اس کی جہالت متعدی الی الحکم العام نہیں ہو سکتی اور مشابہت بالاستثناء کی وجہ جہالت فی العام کا موجب ہے کیونکہ استثناء کی جہالت موجب ہوتی ہے تعدی جہالت الی صدر الکلام کی تو اس لحاظ سے اس عام کے ساتھ حجت ساقط ہو جانی چاہیئے تو اس سقوط عام میں شک واقع ہو جائیگا تو اس شک کی بنا پر جو اس کی حجیت ثابتہ تھی ساقط نہیں ہوگی بلکہ وہ موجب عمل ہو گا اگر چہ موجب علم و یقین نہیں ہو گا جیسے ظنی دلیل واجب العمل ہوتی ہے موجب علم نہیں ہوتی ۔ اذ قبل التخصیص چونکہ عام قبل از تخصیص معمول بہ اور قابل عمل تھا فلما خص جب اس کے اندر تخصیص ہوئی تو شک واقع ہوا کہ اس کا معمول بہ ہونا باقی ہے یا کہ اس پر عمل کرنا باطل ہو چکا ہے تو شک کی وجہ سے اس کا معمول بہ ہونا باطل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ واجب العمل رہیگا ۔
The same status: the fruit and result of this possible doubt will be that, according to us, this general will become like the general that is unspecified in some parts - the status that Imam al-Shafi'i held - i.e., its specification by khabar wahid and qiyas will become valid, but argumentation by it (the general) is not dropped. Because the specifier resembles the abrogator; since the specifier by its wording resembles the abrogator, because this specifier is an independent speech, self-contained in meaning, and conveys a ruling. If there were no preceding general, it would carry an independent ruling. So from this aspect, it resembles the abrogator. And by its ruling, it resembles the exception; because the ruling of this specifier is that it establishes the ruling over what is beyond the specified, and clarifies that the specified does not enter under the ruling. So from this aspect, it is likened to the exception, just as the exception establishes the ruling over what is excepted, and clarifies that the excepted does not enter under the ruling of the opening speech. Thus this specifier resembles the abrogator in one aspect and the exception in another. If it is unknown, i.e., this specifier is unknown, covering unknown individuals, then due to its resemblance to the abrogator, it will drop itself, because an unknown abrogator drops itself; therefore its ignorance cannot transfer to the general ruling. And due to its resemblance to the exception, it causes ignorance in the general, because the ignorance of the exception causes transference of ignorance to the opening speech. From this aspect, the argument by this general should drop, so doubt occurs in the dropping of the general. On the basis of this doubt, its established authority does not drop; rather it remains subject to action, although it does not bring knowledge and certainty. Just as a speculative proof is obligatory to act upon but does not bring knowledge. Since before specification, the general was acted upon and subject to practice, when specification occurs, doubt arises: whether its being acted upon remains or its practice has become invalid. Due to this doubt, its being acted upon does not become invalid; rather it remains obligatory to act upon.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis from a Hanafi usul commentary, examining the nature of a specifier (mukhassis) that creates a doubt (shubha) by resembling both a nasikh (abrogator) and an istithna' (exception). The author explains that when the specifier is unknown (majhul), meaning it covers unknown individuals, its resemblance to a nasikh would normally cause it to drop itself, but its resemblance to an exception would transfer ignorance to the general. This creates a conflict, resulting in doubt about whether the general text loses its authority. The Hanafi position is that the original authority of the general remains intact; it does not become invalid but continues to be binding for action, though it does not produce certainty. The example given is that of a speculative proof (dalil zanni) which is obligatory to act upon but does not yield knowledge. The passage reinforces that doubt does not override established legal force.

Key Terms
مخصص (mukhassis): A specifier that restricts the general meaning of a text.
مجهول (majhul): Unknown; a specifier with unknown individuals.
شبه (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity in legal reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the binding force (hujjiyyah) of a general text (amm) when an unknown specifier (mukhassis majhul) is introduced?
A) The general text becomes invalid and cannot be acted upon.
B) The general text remains binding for action, though it does not provide certainty.
C) The general text becomes absolutely certain.
D) The unknown specifier itself becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
An unknown specifier creates doubt, but the general text remains binding for action because established authority is not overturned by mere doubt.

The Two Doubts on Ta'lil of a Mukhassis
Refuting two doubts about ta'lil of a mukhassis and its effect on the general text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two doubts (shubhatayn) regarding ta'lil of a mukhassis and explain the Hanafi response that the 'amm remains a proof.

Core Idea
The mukhassis is an independent text; its ta'lil does not invalidate the 'amm.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the relationship between a general text ('amm) and its specifier (mukhassis) is crucial for accurate istinbat. A dispute arose with al-Jubba'i over whether the mukhassis can be given a ratio legis (ta'lil) via qiyas. This passage addresses two doubts that challenge the validity of that ta'lil and reaffirms the Hanafi position that the 'amm remains a proof after specification.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Articulate the Hanafi view: the mukhassis is an independent text (nass mustaqill), so its ta'lil by qiyas is valid and does not affect the probative value of the 'amm.
This is the baseline for understanding the dispute.
2
Identify the first doubt (shubha ula)
The first doubt: if ta'lil of the mukhassis is allowed, then by analogy other individuals could be excluded, leading to ignorance about what remains under the 'amm.
This doubt questions the scope of specification.
3
Identify the second doubt (shubha thaniya)
The second doubt: the mukhassis is like an exception (istithna'), and since ta'lil of an excepted item is invalid, ta'lil of the mukhassis should also be invalid.
This doubt analogizes the mukhassis to a mere exception.
4
Explain the Hanafi response and conclusion
The Hanafi response: the mukhassis is not an exception; it is an independent text with its own ruling. Its 'illa precisely defines the excluded individuals, so no uncertainty arises. Both doubts are refuted, and the 'amm remains a proof.
The passage concludes by distinguishing takhsis from naskh: in takhsis, ta'lil is valid; in naskh, it is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالناسخ هو فتعليل الناسخ بهذا الوجه لا يصح. نان تعليل الناسخ على هذا الوجه لا يصح ناسخ کی تعلیل اس طرح کرنا کہ اس علت قیاسیہ سے آئندہ بھی نسخ جاری رہے یہ صحیح نہیں تھا اس لئے مصنف نے اپنے قول بما یرید کے ساتھ اس کی مدافعت کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ شبه اول سے مراد من حیث انه ناسخ مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ بایں حیثیت کہ مخصص معلوم ایک ایسی نص ہے جو مستقل بنفسہ ہے اور مفید حکم ہے اس لئے اس کی تعلیل صحیح - كما هو عندنا جیسے احناف کے نزدیک نص مستقل کی تعلیل صحیح هے۔ فاذا صح تعلیلیه جب اس مخصص کی تعلیل عندنا وعند اکثر العلماء صحیح ہوئی تو معلوم ہو گا کہ اس تعلیل یعنی قیاس کے ساتھ کتنا خارج ہے اور کتنا تحت العام باقی ہے تو اس لحاظ سے فیما بقی تحت العام جہالت واقع ہو جائیگی۔ كما هو عند البعض اسی عند الجبائی وہ کہتا ہے کہ مخصص در حقیقت نص مستقل نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ بمنزلہ وصف کے ہے جو صدر کلام کے ساتھ قائم ہے جو اس پر دال ہے کہ یہ افراد صدر کلام کے حکم میں داخل نہیں ہیں تو یہ جب یہ عدم دخول پر دال ہوا تو لا تعلیل للعدم کما هو فى الاستثناء ندخل الشك في سقوط العام۔ شبہ ثانی یعنی شبه استثناء بایں حیثیت قائم ہے که مخصص بیان کرتا ہے کہ مخصوص افراد حکم عام میں داخل نہیں ہیں تو اس کی تعلیل صحیح نہیں ہے جیسے کہ جبائی کا مذہب ہے کہ جس طرح تعلیل مستثنی صحیح نہیں ہوتی اس مخصص کی بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ واخراج البعض یعنی بایں حیثیت کہ اس کی تعلیل صحیح ہے تو مخصص باقی کا اخراج بھی ہو سکتا ہے لہذا ما بقی تحت العام مجہول ہوا لہذا عام حجت نہ رہے لیکن بایں حیثیت کہ اس کی تعلیل صحیح نہیں ہے تو عام کو حجت رہنا چاہیے، چونکہ وہ قبل از تخصیص حجت تھا تو اب ان شبهین مذکورین کی بنا پر اس کے بطلان میں شک واقع ہوا لہذا شک کی بنا پر باطل نہیں ہو گا بلکہ اس کی حجیت باقی رہے گی. فظهر مبنا الفرق تو اس سے تخصیص اور نسخ کے درمیان فرق ظاہر ہوا کہ تخصیص میں تعلیل مخصص قیاس کے ساتھ صحیح ہے اور وہ مخصص جسے ناسخ کہا جاتا ہے جو بعض افراد عام کو منسوخ کرتا ہے اس کے اندر تعلیل قیاسی صحیح نہیں ہے.
As for the abrogator, the ta'lil of the abrogator in this manner is not valid. The ta'lil of the abrogator in this manner is not valid: that is, making ta'lil of it with a qiyasi 'illa such that abrogation would continue in the future is not correct. Therefore, the author, in his statement 'bima yurid', defended it, saying that the first doubt does not mean from the aspect that it is an abrogator, but rather it means from the aspect that the known specifier is an independent text that is self-standing and conveys a ruling, so its ta'lil is valid, as it is according to us, just as the ta'lil of an independent text is valid according to the Hanafis. So when its ta'lil is valid according to us and most scholars, then it will be known how many are excluded by this ta'lil (i.e., analogy) and how many remain under the general term. In that respect, there will be ignorance regarding what remains under the general term. As is according to some, i.e., according to al-Jubba'i, he says that the specifier is not really an independent text; rather, it is like a description that stands with the first part of the speech, indicating that these individuals are not included in the ruling of the first part of the speech. So when it indicates non-inclusion, then there is no ta'lil for non-existence, as is the case in exception. Hence, doubt enters into the fall of the general term. The second doubt, i.e., the doubt of exception, stands in that the specifier states that the specified individuals are not included in the general ruling, so its ta'lil is not valid, as is the school of al-Jubba'i: just as ta'lil of the excepted item is not valid, ta'lil of this specifier is also not valid. And the exclusion of some individuals: from the aspect that its ta'lil is valid, the specifier can also exclude the rest, so what remains under the general term becomes unknown, hence the general term is not a proof. But from the aspect that its ta'lil is not valid, the general term should remain a proof, since it was a proof before specification. Now, due to these two mentioned doubts, doubt enters regarding its invalidity, so it does not become invalid due to doubt; rather, its probative value remains. Thus the basis of the difference appears: that in specification, ta'lil of the specifier by analogy is valid, but for the specifier that is called an abrogator, which abrogates some individuals of the general, ta'lil by analogy is not valid.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of two doubts (shubhatayn) raised regarding the permissibility of giving a ratio legis (ta'lil) for a mukhassis (specifier) in relation to a general text ('amm). The context is the Hanafi position that a mukhassis, being an independent text (nass mustaqill), can be subject to ta'lil via qiyas, which helps determine how many individuals are excluded from the 'amm. The first doubt (shubha ula) is that if ta'lil of the mukhassis is allowed, then by analogy other individuals could also be excluded, leading to ignorance about what remains under the 'amm. The author refutes this by clarifying that the ta'lil does not lead to further exclusion beyond what the 'illa indicates; rather, it clarifies the extent of specification. The second doubt (shubha thaniya) likens the mukhassis to an exception (istithna'), arguing that just as the excepted item cannot be given a ta'lil, the mukhassis also cannot. Al-Jubba'i (a Mu'tazili) holds this view. The Hanafi response is that the mukhassis is different from exception because it is an independent text, not merely a connector. Consequently, the two doubts do not invalidate the probative value (hujjiyya) of the 'amm; the 'amm remains a proof for what is not specified. The passage concludes by highlighting the key difference between takhsis (specification) and naskh (abrogation): in takhsis, the mukhassis can be explained by qiyas, but in naskh, the nasikh (abrogator) cannot be explained by qiyas because that would allow continuous abrogation of other parts, which is not permissible.

Key Terms
تخصیص (takhsīṣ): Specification: excluding some individuals from the generality of a general term ('amm) by a specifier (mukhassis).
مخصص (mukhassis): Specifier: a text (or other evidence) that indicates that some individuals of a general term are not intended.
تعلیل (taʿlīl): Giving a ratio legis ('illa) for a ruling, often via qiyas (analogy).
شبه (shubha): Doubt: an argument that creates uncertainty about a legal ruling or principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what distinguishes ta'lil of a mukhassis from ta'lil of a nasikh?
A) Ta'lil of a mukhassis is invalid, while ta'lil of a nasikh is valid.
B) Both are valid and have the same effect on the general text.
C) Ta'lil of a mukhassis by qiyas is valid, but ta'lil of a nasikh by qiyas is not valid because it would allow continuous abrogation.
D) Ta'lil of a mukhassis is valid only if it is an independent text, while ta'lil of a nasikh is always invalid.

Key Takeaway
The mukhassis is an independent text; its ta'lil by qiyas is valid and does not invalidate the 'amm, which remains a proof for what is not excluded.

Takhsis by Qiyas vs. Naskh: The Hanafi Principle
Distinguishing takhsis and naskh regarding qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that qiyas can specify a general text but cannot abrogate it, and justify this distinction using the example of the widows' iddah verses.

Core Idea
Qiyas specifies by clarifying scope; naskh requires direct textual contradiction and equal strength.

In Hanafi usul, the relationship between qiyas and the general text (amm) is nuanced. While qiyas is a valid tool for specification (takhsis), it cannot abrogate (naskh) a verse or hadith. This lesson unpacks the logical basis: abrogation demands a direct conflict between two texts of equal rank, whereas specification is a form of clarification that does not invalidate the general. Understanding this distinction is crucial for sound istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish takhsis and naskh
Identify the two operations: takhsis excludes some individuals from a general ruling; naskh cancels the ruling for those individuals entirely.
Both affect the scope of the general, but their mechanisms differ.
2
Identify the condition for each
Takhsis requires a cause (illa) derived from a prior specifier; naskh requires a later contradicting text of equal authority.
The condition for naskh is stricter.
3
Apply the condition to qiyas
Qiyas can supply the illa for further specification after a textual specifier exists, but it cannot supply the textual strength needed for naskh.
Qiyas is weaker than nass.
4
Work through the widows' iddah example
Analyze how Quran 2:234 (general iddah) and 65:4 (pregnant widows) conflict; the later abrogates the earlier for pregnant widows. This is naskh by text, not by qiyas.
The conflict is between two verses, not between a verse and qiyas.
5
Confirm the principle
The general text remains authoritative except where the cause applies; probability of qiyas does not nullify it.
The general is not destroyed; it is only clarified.
