ہو سکتا اور اس کی تعلیل پیش نہیں کی جاسکتی لہذا عام باقی میں حجت برقرار اور ان کی تخصیص از حکم عام صحیح نہیں ہوگی دان عرفت فيه علة اگر قیاس کے ساتھ اس تخصیص کی علہ معلوم ہو چکی ہے تو پھر وہ ہر فرد جس کے اندر یہ علت موجود ہوگی تو قیاساً اس کی تخصیص کر لی جائیگی اور جن میں یہ علہ موجود نہیں ہوگی تو ان کی تخصیص نہیں کی جا سکتی ۔ فلا بطل العام و احتمال تعلیل کی بنا پر اس عام کی حجیت باطل نہیں ہوگی لہذا اس کی حجیت برقرار رہیگی ۔ فظهر مبنا الفرق تو اس سے تخصیص اور نسخ کے درمیان فرق ظاہر ہوا کہ تخصیص میں تعلیل مخصص قیاس کے ساتھ صحیح ہے اور وہ مخصص جسے ناسخ کہا جاتا ہے جو بعض افراد عام کو منسوخ کرتا ہے اس کے اندر تعلیل قیاسی صحیح نہیں ہے لیثبت النسخ یہ تعلیل صحیح ہوتی تو بعض دوسرے افراد کا نسخ قیاس سے لازم آتا جب تعلیل صحیح نہیں ہے تو اب یہ لازم پیش نہیں آئے گا صورته ان يرد نص الخ صورۃ نسخ یوں ہو سکتی ہے کہ ایک نص خاص وارد ہو جس کا حکم نص عام کے حکم کا مخالف ہو اور اس خاص کا ورود متراخی عین درود العام ہو یعنی خاص بعد العام مترا خیا وارد ہو تو ایسے خاص کو ناسخ للعام قرار دیا جاتا ہے لا مخصصا مخصص قرار نہیں دیا جاتا فان العام الذی نسیم بعض ما تناولے پس وہ عام جس کے بعض افراد خاص کے ساتھ منسوخ ہو چکے ہیں لا ینسخ بالقیاس یعنی تعلیل قیاسی کے ساتھ دیگر افراد میں آئندہ اس کا فسخ نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ قیاس نا سے نص نہیں ہو سکتا ادھر لا يعارضه کيونکہ قیاس نص کے ساتھ معارضہ نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ قیاس کا درجہ نص سے کم ہے اور کم درجہ معارض للقوی نہیں ہو سکتا لكن يخصصه لیکن قیاس تخصیص کر سکتا ہے ولا يلزم به المعارضة کیونکہ تخصیص میں معارضہ بین النص والقياس لازم نہیں آتا اصل و ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ نسخ بطریق معارضہ ہوتا ہے یعنی ناسخ اور منسوخ کے درمیان معارضہ قائم ہوتا ہے تو اس معارضہ کی بنا پر ناسخ جن افراد کو شامل ہوتا ہے ان کے اندر حکم عام کو منسوخ کر دیتا ہے جیسے والذین یتوفون منکم الا یہ بر متوفى عنها خواہ حاملہ ہو یا غیر حاملہ عدت اربعه اشهر وعشر لازم کرتی ہے اور واولات الاحمال اجلعن الایت یہ حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل کو قرار دیتی ہے تو یہ دونوں آیات حاملہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا کے حق میں معارض ہیں جیسے کہ ابن مسعود کی رائے تھی تو یہ آیت والذین یتوفون منکم کو حق حاملہ منسوخ کر دیگی اور متعارضین کے مابین مساویانہ قوت شرط ہے اور قیاس چونکہ نفس سے کم درجہ ہے لہذا یہ ناسخ نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا ناسخ تعلیل قیاسی نہیں ہو سکتی بخلاف تخصیص کے کہ اس کے اندر صورت معارضہ قائم نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس کے اندر صورۃ تبیین ہوتی ہے جب عام میں کسی مخصص مستقل کے ساتھ بیان ہو جاتا ہے کہ فلاں فلاں افراد مخصوص نہیں تو جو علہ قیاسیہ اس مخصص سے مستنبط ہو گی وہ اس مقدار کی تخصیص کر سکتی ہے جہاں تک اس علقہ مستنبطہ کی رسائی ہوگی اور بیان کرے گی کہ یہ افراد بھی داخل تحت الحکم نہیں ہیں لیکن یہ شرط ہے کہ عام پہلے کسی کلام مخصص کے ساتھ تخصیص شدہ ہو جائے۔ وههنا مسائل من الفروع اس مقام پر کچھ مسائل ہیں جو ماذکرنا کے ساتھ متناسب ہیں یعنی جو ہم نے استثناء اور نسخ و تخصیص کے جو احکام ذکر کئے ہیں ان کے ساتھ مناسبت رکھتے ہیں فنظیر الاستثناء استثناء کی نظیر میں دو مسئلے پیش کئے جیسے استثنا مستثنی کو صدر کلام کے حکم میں داخل ہونے سے روکتا ہے اسی طرح ہے یہ مسئلہ اذباع الحر والعبد بتمن یعنی حر اور عبد کو لا کر ایک ہی عقد میں ثمن واحد کے ساتھ فروخت کرتا کہتا ہے بعث بدین عندک بالف توحد داخل تحت الایجاب نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ ایک نئی تحت عقد المسیح
And excluding some, meaning in the sense that if its causal explanation is valid, then the remainder can also be excluded; therefore what remains under the general becomes unknown, so the general is no longer a proof. But in the sense that its causal explanation is not valid, the general should remain a proof because it was a proof before specification. Now due to these two mentioned possibilities, doubt arose about its invalidity, so it will not be invalid due to doubt, rather its authority remains. This is what they said and it is refuted by saying 'lammā kāna' etc. An objection arises here: since according to you and most scholars its causal explanation is valid, therefore according to you the authority of this general should be invalidated. Your claim is acceptable to you, but with the claim of the one who does not consider the causal explanation valid, your adherence is not correct. He refuted this doubt by saying that the possibility of causal explanation does not exclude the general from being a proof because qiyas—i.e., analogical reasoning—will exclude those for which it necessitates specification, and those for which it is not necessitated will remain. Because if the general is such that there is no cause of specification perceptible by qiyas within it, then it cannot be subjected to causal explanation and its causal explanation cannot be presented; therefore the general remains a proof and their specification from the ruling of the general will not be correct. If the cause of this specification is known through qiyas, then every individual possessing this cause will be specified by qiyas, and those not possessing it cannot be specified. Thus the general is not invalidated, and its authority remains despite the possibility of causal explanation. Hence the basis of the difference appears: specification differs from abrogation. In specification, the causal explanation of the specifying text through qiyas is valid, whereas in that specifier which is called abrogator—which abrogates some individuals of the general—the analogical causal explanation is not valid. If this causal explanation were valid, then abrogation of some other individuals would necessarily follow from qiyas. When it is not valid, this necessity does not arise. Its form is that a specific text comes whose ruling opposes the ruling of the general text, and this specific text comes after the general with delay, i.e., the specific comes after the general with separation; then such a specific is considered abrogator of the general, not a specifier. So the general whose some individuals have been abrogated by a specific cannot be abrogated by qiyas, i.e., it cannot be abrogated in other individuals by analogical causal explanation because qiyas cannot oppose the text. And qiyas does not oppose it because qiyas cannot conflict with the text, since qiyas is of a lower rank than the text, and a lower rank cannot oppose a stronger one. But it can specify, and conflict is not necessitated because in specification, conflict between the text and qiyas does not necessarily occur. The principle is that abrogation occurs through conflict: the abrogator and the abrogated conflict. By virtue of this conflict, the abrogator abrogates the general ruling in the individuals it includes. For example, 'And those who are taken in death among you' requires that the widow, whether pregnant or not, observe an iddah of four months and ten days. And 'And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth' sets the iddah of a pregnant woman as delivery. So these two verses conflict regarding a pregnant widow whose husband dies, as was the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud. Then the verse 'And those who are taken in death among you' would be abrogated concerning the pregnant woman. Equal strength between the conflicting texts is a condition, and since qiyas is lower in rank than the text, it cannot be an abrogator. Therefore an abrogator cannot be based on analogical causal explanation, unlike specification where conflict does not arise; rather, it is a form of clarification. When the general is clarified by an independent specifier that such-and-such individuals are not intended, then the analogical cause derived from that specifier can specify to the extent of that cause, clarifying that these individuals are also not included under the ruling. But the condition is that the general must first have been specified by some independent statement. And here are some subsidiary issues that are proportionate to what we have mentioned, i.e., related to the rulings we discussed concerning exception, abrogation, and specification. As an analogy of exception, two issues are presented: just as exception prevents the excepted from entering the ruling of the prefixed statement, similarly this issue: selling a free man and a slave together for a single price, one says 'I sold you the slave for such and such' but the free man does not enter under the offer because a free man is not subject to a contract of sale.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains a critical distinction between takhsis (specification) and naskh (abrogation) concerning the use of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author first addresses a problem: if a general text (amm) has been specified by qiyas in some cases, does that mean the general's authority is lost for all cases? The response clarifies that only cases where the cause (illa) found by qiyas applies are excluded; the general remains authoritative for other cases. The possibility of such qiyas does not nullify the general. The core distinction is then presented: in takhsis, qiyas can validly provide a cause to extend a specific ruling to other cases, thereby further specifying the general. In naskh, however, qiyas cannot abrogate a general text because abrogation requires a conflict between texts of equal strength. Since qiyas is weaker than a textual proof (nass), it cannot overcome a general text to abrogate it. To illustrate naskh, the author cites the well-known example of the two Quranic verses on widows' iddah: one mandates four months and ten days generally, the other specifies that for pregnant widows the iddah ends at delivery. These verses conflict, and the later verse abrogates the earlier for pregnant women. This conflict is between two texts, not between a text and qiyas. Finally, the passage transitions to subsidiary issues (masa'il al-furu') analogous to istithna' (exception), giving the example of selling a free man and a slave together—the free man cannot be sold, so he is not included in the contract, akin to exception rejecting part of the statement.

Key Terms
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification of a general text by excluding some individuals from its ruling through a separate evidence, including qiyas.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a ruling by a later text that contradicts it, requiring equal textual strength.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that extends a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause (illa).
تعلیل (ta'lil): Causal explanation; identifying the effective cause (illa) to apply analogical reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul text, why can qiyas not abrogate a general text (amm) even though it can specify it?
A) Because qiyas is weaker than a textual proof and abrogation requires equal textual strength.
B) Because qiyas can only be used in matters of worship, not in legal rulings.
C) Because the general text is always stronger than any qiyas.
D) Because abrogation requires consensus (ijma), not qiyas.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas can specify a general text by clarifying its scope, but it cannot abrogate it because abrogation requires direct textual conflict and equal strength.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Analogue of Istithna' in Sales Contracts
Presents two branch cases analogous to istithna' and naskh in sales (istithna' part complete, naskh part truncated).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the usul concept of istithna' (exception) to identify the legal ruling in a mixed sale contract, and explain why the sale is void due to jahl (ignorance of price) or an invalid condition.

Core Idea
Just as istithna' excludes an item from a general ruling, a free man cannot enter a sale contract even if included in the wording.

In usul al-Fiqh, istithna' is a linguistic tool that excludes a specific item from a general statement. The Hanafi school extends this concept to sales contracts: when a free man is sold together with a slave, the free man does not acquire the status of a valid object of sale, analogous to an exception. This passage explores two branch cases that illustrate this principle, demonstrating how fiqh rulings reflect usul rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two branch cases
Recognize the first case: selling a free man and a slave together for one price. The second case: selling two slaves with an explicit exception of one ('except this'). Both are presented as analogues of istithna'.
The first is an implicit analogue (no istithna' wording), the second is a real istithna'.
2
Analyze the legal effect in each case
In the first case, the free man does not enter the contract because he is not property. In the second case, the excepted slave does not enter. Determine the legal consequences: the sale becomes invalid.
The free man lacks the quality of being māl (property), so he cannot be a subject of sale.
3
Understand the analogy to istithna'
Just as istithna' prevents an excepted item from entering under the general ruling, here the free man (or excepted slave) does not enter the contract despite being included in the offer wording.
This is a talil (reasoning) comparable to the effect of istithna' in usul.
4
Identify the two reasons for invalidity
First, the sale becomes a sale by portion (bay' bi al-hissah) causing jahl (ignorance) of the price apportioned to each item. Second, the non-sold item (free man or excepted slave) becomes a condition for acceptance, which is a void condition (shart fasid).
Both reasons independently invalidate the sale.
5
Note the incomplete naskh analogue
The passage ends with 'And the analogue of naskh is...' but is cut off. Recognize that this lesson covers only the istithna' analogue.

And here are some branch issues that are appropriate with what we mentioned, i.e., they are related to the rulings we stated about istithna', naskh, and takhsis. So the analogue of istithna': two issues are presented. Just as istithna' prevents the excepted thing from entering under the ruling of the beginning of the speech, similarly is this issue: selling a free man and a slave for a price, i.e., he brings free and slave and sells them in one contract for one price. He says 'I sold you this and this for a thousand,' but the free does not enter under the offer, because an item can only enter under a contract of sale when it possesses the quality of being property and it is valuable, and this quality is not present in the free man. And similarly will be the case when vinegar and dates are sold together in one contract for one price. The second issue: when a man sells two slaves in one contract for a thousand and excepts one slave with 'except this' along with a portion of the thousand, i.e., the thousand is distributed over the price of the slave in the first case and if the free were a slave, its price, so the thousand is divided accordingly. Then the sale in both cases becomes void because in these two contracts, one of the two sold items is not included in the sale, so the sale becomes a sale by portion initially, i.e., from the beginning it is a sale by portion, and the price of one thousand has to be divided over the prices of the two sold items. The second reason for invalidity is that which is not sold becomes a condition for the acceptance of the sold, because the contract is one, accepted at one time, so this is a void condition; therefore the sale is void. In the first issue, where the free is mixed in the sale, it is not a real exception, but it is analogous to exception, because just as exception prevents the excepted from entering under the ruling of the beginning of the speech, similarly in this issue the free does not enter under the offer, even though the beginning of the speech includes it, so it is like an excepted thing. In the second issue, when two slaves are sold and one is excepted with 'except this', here real exception exists. Since in these two contracts one individual does not enter the sale, the sale in the other is also not valid. There are two reasons: first, if the sale in the other is considered valid, then it becomes a sale by portion of the price initially, which is void because ignorance of price at the time of sale is necessary; a sale by portion initially is void, although valid after the fact, as in the issue that is the analogue of naskh. Second, the sale in the other slave occurs with a condition that opposes the requirement of the contract, because what is not sold — in the first case the free, and in the second case the slave that was excepted — becomes a condition for the acceptance of the sold, so this sale is void. And the analogue of naskh is when...
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage provides two branch examples illustrating the usul concepts of istithna' (exception) and naskh (abrogation) as applied to sales contracts. The first example is analogous to istithna': selling a free man together with a slave for a single price. In Hanafi law, a free man cannot be the object of sale because he is not property. Hence, the offer does not include him, even though the literal wording includes him. This resembles the effect of an exception, which excludes a specific individual from a general ruling. The second example involves an explicit exception of one slave when selling two slaves. This is a genuine istithna'. The sale is invalid for two reasons: first, it becomes a sale by portion (with an unknown price share), leading to ignorance of the price; second, the excepted item becomes a condition for accepting the sold item, which is a void condition as it contradicts the nature of a sales contract. The passage ends by noting that there is also an analogue of naskh, which is mentioned in the next part.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): A linguistic exception that excludes a specific item from a general statement.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation, used here analogically for partial exclusion in contracts.
بیع بالحصہ (bay' bi al-hissah): A sale where the price is apportioned among items without specifying the share for each, leading to uncertainty (jahl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second example (sale of two slaves with exception of one), why is the sale void?
A) Because exception (istithna') is not allowed in sales.
B) Because it leads to either a sale by portion (jahl) or an invalid condition.
C) Because the excepted slave is not property.
D) Because the price cannot be divided.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school extends the usul concept of istithna' to sales: a free man cannot be sold, just as an excepted item is excluded from a general ruling.

Analogy of Takhsis: Sale with Option in One of Two Items
Explains validity of sale with option compared to specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of takhsis by analogy to a sale with option (khiyar) and state the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
An option in a sale restricts ownership like takhsis restricts a general ruling, but terms must be known.

This passage illustrates how the Hanafi school uses analogy (qiyas) to connect a fiqh case to usul al-fiqh. The case of selling two slaves with an option in one is compared to takhsis, naskh, and istithna. Understanding this analogy deepens your grasp of how general rulings are specified without complete invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Case
The case: selling two slaves for a fixed price with a condition that the buyer or seller has a 3-day option (khiyar) on one of them. Recognize that the option applies to a specific slave, not both.
The option is a stipulated choice (khiyar al-shart).
2
Distinguish the Two Analogies
The option resembles naskh in the cause (the offer of sale includes the option-slave) and istithna in the ruling (ownership of that slave is excluded until the option expires or is exercised). Trace how the text uses 'fi al-sabab' (in cause) and 'fi al-hukm' (in ruling).
Naskh abrogates part of a ruling; istithna excludes an item from a statement.
3
Determine the Conditions for Validity
Both the subject of the option (which slave) and its price (portion of the lump sum) must be known. If either is unknown, the sale fails due to resemblance to an unknown istithna, which invalidates the contract.
Unknown terms create gharar (uncertainty), a cause of invalidity in sales.
4
Understand the Resemblance to Takhsis
Takhsis specifies a general ruling without nullifying it. Here, the option specifies that one slave is not immediately owned, while the other is. The analogy shows how usul principles govern fiqh cases.
This is a classic example of expansion (probe) of usul to muamalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونظیر التخصیص تخصیص کی نظیر یہ مسئلہ ہے اذا باع عبدمین بالف على انه بالخيار في احدهما یعنی دو غلام بعقد واحد ایک ہزار میں فروخت کرتا ہے لیکن ایک غلام میں بائع یا مشتری تین دن تک خیار شرط کرتا ہے تو یہ بیع صحیح ہو گی بشرطیکہ محل خیار معلوم اور متعین ہو اور اس کے ثمن بھی معلوم ہوں ۔ لان المبيع بالخيار کیونکہ مبیع بالخيار ایجاب بیع میں تو داخل ہے جو کہ سبب ہے لاالحکم اور حکم میں یعنی ملک میں داخل نہیں ہے یعنی یہ غلام ملک مشتری میں داخل نہیں [نصار؟] فی السبب كالنسخ وفی الحكم كالاستثناء یعنی سب میں تو [ہمبز لہ؟] نسخ کے ہوا جیسے نسخ ایک کلام مستقل اور مقترن ہو کر نسخ فی الافراد کرتی تھی یہ ایسے ہے وفی الحکم کا لا استثناء اور حکم میں یعنی ملک میں ہمنزلہ استثناء کے ہے جیسے استثناء صدر کلام کے حکم سے مستثنی کو خارج کر لیتا ہے اور اس کے عدم دخول کو واضح کرتا ہے یہ خیار بھی ایسے ہے کہ واضح کر رہا ہے کہ یہ محل خیار داخل فی الحکم نہیں ہے فاذ اجمل لحد صاحب محل خیار اور ثمن میں سے کوئی ایک نئی مجہول ہو تو یہ بیع صیح نہیں ہوگی ۔ لشبه الاستثنا یعنی به استثناء کی وجہ سے کہ جب استثناء مجہول ہو تو کلام کو باطل کر دیتا ہے ایسے یہاں بھی ہو گا کہ ایجاب ختم ہو جائیں گا میں صحیح نہیں ہوگی واذا اعلم كل واحد منهما جب محل خیار اور اس کے ثمن دونوں معلوم ہوں تو یہ بیع صحیح ہو جائیگی یشبہ النسخ جیسے نسخ کے ساتھ معلومہ افراد میں حکم منسوخ ہو جاتا تھا اور باقی میں حکم باقی رہتا تھا یہاں بھی ایسے ہوگا ولم يعتبر مهنا شبه الاستثناء یعنی شبه استثناء کو یہاں اعتبار نہیں کیا
And the analogy to specification: the example of specification is this issue: when he sells two slaves for a thousand on condition that he has an option in one of them, i.e., he sells two slaves in one contract for one thousand but stipulates an option for the seller or buyer for three days in one slave, then this sale is valid provided that the subject of the option is known and specified, and its price is also known. Because the item sold with option enters into the offer of sale, which is the cause, not the ruling, and in the ruling i.e., ownership it does not enter, meaning this slave does not enter the ownership of the buyer. So it becomes in the cause like naskh and in the ruling like istithnā’. That is, in the cause it is similar to naskh just as naskh used to abrogate in individuals, and in the ruling it is like istithnā’ because istithnā’ excludes the excepted from the ruling of the opening statement and clarifies its non-entry. This option also is such that it clarifies that this subject of option does not enter the ruling. So if the subject of option and its price are unknown, the sale is not valid due to the resemblance to istithnā’, because when istithnā’ is unknown it invalidates the speech. Similarly here, the offer becomes invalid and it is not valid. And when both of them are known, the sale becomes valid, resembling naskh, just as with naskh, among known individuals the ruling is abrogated and in the rest the ruling remains. Here also it will be so, and the resemblance to istithnā’ is not considered here.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of selling two slaves for a lump sum with an option (khiyar) in one of them. The Hanafi ruling is that such a sale is valid provided that both the slave subject to the option and its price are known and specified. The reasoning is that the item with option enters the cause (the offer) but not the ruling (ownership), similar to how naskh (abrogation) affects the cause but leaves the rest intact, and similar to istithnā’ (exception) in that it excludes that item from the ownership transfer. If the option subject or its price is unknown, the sale is invalid because it resembles an unknown exception, which makes the contract void. This illustrates the usul principle of takhsis (specification) where a general ruling is specified by a condition without invalidating the remainder.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyār): An option given to one of the parties to confirm or cancel the sale within a specified period.
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): Specification of a general ruling, removing some individuals from its application.
استثناء (istithnā’): An exclusion of something from the generality of a statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, a sale of two slaves with an option in one is valid when:
A) The option is known but the price is unknown
B) Both the option subject and its price are known
C) The option is unknown
D) The price is known but the option subject is unknown

Key Takeaway
The sale with option in one of two items is valid when the option subject and price are known, analogizing to takhsis in usul al-fiqh.

Analogy of Sale with Khiyar to Takhsis and Naskh
Explaining legal analogy of khiyar sale to usul principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the dual analogy (naskh and istithna) underlying the Hanafi validation of a sale with khiyar, and apply the condition for its validity.

Core Idea
A sale with option in one item is valid like takhsis: included in cause but excluded from ruling.

This passage from a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih explains why a sale of two items with a condition of option in one is valid in the Hanafi school. It draws an analogy to the usul concepts of naskh (abrogation) and istithna (exception), showing that the option item is included in the offer (like naskh changes the ruling for some) but excluded from ownership (like istithna excludes from the ruling). The validity hinges on both the subject of option and its price being known.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fiqh case
Read the passage and state the exact scenario: sale of two slaves for a thousand with a condition of option (khiyar) in one of them.
The option is for three days.
2
Recognize the dual nature of the option item
Note that the option item is included in the offer (cause) but not in ownership (ruling). This gives it similarity to both naskh and istithna.
Naskh changes an established ruling for some individuals; istithna clarifies non-inclusion.
3
Trace the analogy to takhsis
Takhsis has both aspects: in wording it resembles naskh, in ruling it resembles istithna. The author says the sale with khiyar is like takhsis.
This analogy is used to validate the contract.
4
Apply the condition for validity
The sale is valid only when both the subject of option (which slave) and its price are known. If either is unknown, the sale is invalid due to similarity to an unknown istithna.
Contrast with the case of free+slave (pure istithna) which is always invalid per Abu Hanifa.
5
Summarize the usul principle
The dual similarity argument shows how a contractual condition can be validated by analogy to takhsis, a key Hanafi usul concept.
This exemplifies the use of 'illah (effective cause) in deriving rulings.

افراد میں حکم منسوخ ہو جاتا تھا اور باقی میں حکم باقی رہتا تھا یہاں بھی ایسے ہوگا ولم يعتبر مهنا شبه الاستثناء یعنی شبه استثناء کو یہاں اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا یوں کہا جاتا کہ جب محل خیار مستثنی از بیع ہوا تو قبول الايجاب في غير المبيع شرط فاسید ہے چونکہ عقد واحد ہے اس لئے مشتری تو اسی صورت میں بقبول واحد قبول کرے گا تو غیر مبیع کی قبولیت شرط کرنا یہ مفسد للعقد ہے ۔ تو اس شبہ کو اس مقام پر بمقابلہ حر اپنجاب کے تحت بھی داخل نہیں ہو سکتا تو وہ پوری نظیر استثناء ہے لہذا وہاں جائز نہیں ہوگی بیع کسی میں بھی ۔ وبیان مناسبتها بالتخصیص وہ یوں کہ جیسے تخصیص باعتبار صیغہ کے مشابہ بالنسخ ہوتی ہے اور حکم شرط کے ساتھ واپس کرنا سابقہ عقد کو تبدیل کرنا ہے فیکون کا لفخ جیسے وہ حکم عام کو تبدیل کرتا ہے۔ ومن حيث انه غیر داخل فی الحکم اور بائیں حیثیت کہ محل خیار داخل فی الحکم نہیں تھا تو اس کا بخیار شرط رد کرنا یہ بیان ہوگا اس کا کہ یہ داخل نہیں تھا تو اس لحاظ سے یکون کالاستثناء جیسے استثناء مستثنی کے عدم دخول کا بیان کرتا ہے ۔ واذا كان له شبهان جب اس مسئلہ کو دونوں شبہ ہوئے تو یہ بمنزلہ تخصیص کے ہوگا جس کو شبہ بالنسخ اور شبہ بالاستثناء ہوتا ہے فرعاية الشبهین دونوں شبہ کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے ہم نے کہا کہ اگر محل خیار اور اس کے ثمن یہ دونوں معلوم ہوں تو بیع صحیح ہوگی والا فلا - وهذه المسئلة على اربعة عقد اور ایک ہی ایجاب کے ساتھ علی انه ای البائع او المشترى بالخيار في ذاك یعنی بائع یا مشتری کو ذاک میں خیار ہے ہذا میں نہیں ہے رہنا ۔ ذاک اگرچہ اسم اشارہ ہیں لیکن آسانی کی خاطر ہم ان دونوں لفظوں کو ان دو غلاموں کے نام فرض کر کے تحریر کر رہے ہیں الگ نام فرض کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے) والثانی یہ دوسری صورت ہے کہ محل خیار معلوم ہے یعنی زاک
This is that when a person sells two slaves for a thousand, and one slave dies before delivery at the seller's place, then the contract of sale remains valid for the remaining living one by share. So this issue is appropriate with naskh because the meaning of naskh is to change a ruling after it has been established. Since that slave who died before delivery had entered under the sale and the ruling of sale was established for him, but when he died in the seller's possession before delivery, the sale is annulled concerning him, so the ruling changed after establishment. As for the other, the living one, the sale is not invalidated even though it is also a sale by share, but it is not initial rather it remains, and this does not corrupt the contract even though ignorance of price exists here, but it is accidental which occurred after the validity of the contract, the sale will not become invalid with it, just as after naskh the ruling remains for the rest. And the analogy of takhsis: the analogy of takhsis is this issue: when he sells two slaves for a thousand on the condition that he has the option in one of them, meaning two slaves in one contract sold for a thousand, but he stipulates option for the seller or buyer for three days in one slave, then this sale is valid provided that the subject of option is known and specified and its price is also known. Because the sold item with option is included in the offer of sale which is the cause, not in the ruling, i.e., in ownership, meaning this slave does not enter the ownership of the buyer. So in terms of cause it is like naskh, and in terms of ruling it is like istithna. That is, in the cause it is analogous to naskh, just as naskh abrogates some individuals through an independent and connected speech, this is like that. And in terms of ruling, i.e., in ownership, it is like istithna, just as istithna excludes the excepted from the ruling of the preceding speech and clarifies its non-inclusion, this option is also like that, clarifying that this subject of option is not included in the ruling. So if one of the subject of option and price becomes unknown, the sale is not valid due to the similarity to istithna, because when istithna is unknown it invalidates the speech, similarly here the offer will be concluded and not valid. And when each of them is known, the sale is valid, resembling naskh, just as with naskh the ruling is abrogated for known individuals and remains for the rest, here too it will be so. And here the similarity to istithna is not considered. It is said that when the subject of option is excluded from the sale, then accepting the offer for what is not sold is an invalid condition; because the contract is one, so the buyer will accept with one acceptance, so stipulating acceptance for what is not sold corrupts the contract. So this similarity is not given weight compared to naskh in this place. Unlike the case of a free person and a slave: unlike the case where a free person and a slave are sold together, even if the share of price for each is stated, according to Abu Hanifa it is invalid; there the free person cannot even enter under the contract, so it is a pure analogy to istithna, therefore the sale is not permissible for either. And the explanation of its appropriateness with takhsis: it is like that, just as takhsis in terms of wording resembles naskh and in terms of ruling resembles istithna, similarly this mentioned issue: because the one in which there is option is included in the offer and not included in the ruling. So from the aspect that it is included in the offer, the return of this contract with the condition of option is changing the previous contract, so it becomes like naskh, just as it changes the general ruling. And from the aspect that it is not included in the ruling, the return of it with the condition of option is an explanation that it was not included, so from this perspective it is like istithna, just as istithna explains the non-inclusion of the excepted. And when it has two similarities, this issue becomes like takhsis which has similarity to naskh and similarity to istithna. So considering both similarities, we said that if the subject of option and its price both are known, the sale is valid; otherwise no. And this issue has four aspects. One of them: that the subject of option and its price both are known, like when he sells this and that, i.e., he sells those two slaves for two hundred, this for one hundred and that for one hundred, in one transaction and one offer, on condition that he (the seller or buyer) has the option in that (Zak), not in this (Haza). 'Zak' although is a demonstrative pronoun, but for ease we are writing both words as names of the two slaves, no need to assume separate names. And the second: this is the second case that the subject of option is known, i.e., Zak
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage from a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih explains the usul analogies underlying the validity of a sale with a condition of option (khiyar) in one of two items sold in a single contract. The author first gives an example of a sale of two slaves where one dies before delivery. This is likened to naskh (abrogation) because the initial ruling of sale for the deceased slave is changed, while the ruling for the living slave remains. Then he presents the main case: a sale of two slaves with a condition of option in one of them. The condition of option makes that slave included in the offer (cause) but not in the ruling (ownership). This dual nature gives it similarity to both naskh (changing the ruling for some) and istithna (exception, where the excepted is not included). If both the subject of option and its price are known, the sale is valid, giving weight to the naskh aspect. If unknown, it is invalid like an unknown istithna. The author contrasts this with the case of selling a free person and a slave together, which is pure istithna and invalid per Abu Hanifa. Finally, he introduces four possible scenarios, detailing the first where both option and price are known and valid.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Changing a ruling after it has been established, specifically in the context of sale where the contract is annulled for one commodity.
تخصیص (takhsis): A ruling that combines aspects of naskh (in terms of wording) and istithna (in terms of ruling), used here to validate a sale with khiyar.
استثناء (istithna): Exclusion of something from the ruling of a speech, used here to explain that the subject of option is not included in ownership.
خیار (khiyar): Option to annul or confirm a sale within a specified period, here stipulated for one of two items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi analogy, what must be known for the sale with khiyar to be valid?
A) Only the subject of option
B) Only the price
C) Both the subject of option and its price
D) The time period only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a sale with khiyar in one item by analogizing it to takhsis, provided the option subject and its price are known.

Types of General Words in Hanafi Usul
Classifying general terms based on wording and inclusiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify general words (amm) into types based on form and meaning, and identify the legal implications of each type in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
General words are either general in form and meaning, or only in meaning—each type has distinct rules for legal interpretation.

In Hanafi usul, understanding how a general term (amm) functions is crucial for deriving rulings from texts. Not all general words behave the same way. Some are general in their wording and cover all individuals, while others are general only in meaning and may refer to a group as a whole. This lesson dissects the classification from the commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two main categories
Identify that words of generality are either general in both form and meaning (e.g., 'al-rijal') or general only in meaning.
The first type is straightforward; the second requires further subdivision.
2
Identify the example of form+meaning
The plural with definite article (جمع معرف باللام) like 'الرجال' is general in both form and meaning.
Indefinite plural is general only in meaning.
3
Understand group words (general only in meaning)
Words like 'القوم' (the people) refer to a group as a whole and cannot apply to a single individual; they are in the meaning of a plural even if not plural in form.
These words are general in meaning but not in form.
4
Understand distributive generality
Words like 'من' in a conditional sentence (e.g., 'من يأتني فله درهم') include every individual separately on a distributive basis (شمول).
Each person who comes gets a dirham regardless of number or sequence.
5
Note the alternative type (بدل)
The passage mentions an alternative basis (على سبيل البدل) but does not elaborate; it likely refers to words that cover alternatives rather than all individuals.
This is a third subcategory not fully discussed here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الفاظ العموم وهي اما عام الج یعنی یہ الفاظ یا تو بلحاظ صیغہ اور بلحاظ معنی ان دونوں حیثیت سے عام ہوگا جیسے الرجال یعنی جمع معرف بالام اور جو معرف بالام نہیں ہوگی وہ جمع منکر ہے اما عام بمعناہ یا تو صرف بلحاظ معنی کے عام ہوگا اور بلحاظ صیغہ عام نہیں ہوگا وھذا اور یہ جو صرف بحسب المعنی عام ہے یا تو مجموع کو شامل ہو گا اور سر ایک ایک فرد پر اس کا اطلاق نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ کا درحط والقوم کہ ان لفظ کا اطلاق فرد منفرد پر نہیں ہو سکتا بلکہ اس کا اطلاق جماعتہ پر ہوگا ۔ وهو من معنی الجمع یعنی اس قسم کے الفاظ بھی جمع کے معنی اور حکم میں ہیں اگر چہ لفظاً او صیغہ جمع نہیں ہیں ۔ أو كل واحد عام بالمعنی ہر ایک ایک کو شامل ہو گا علی سبیل الشمول یعنی یہ ایک ایک جتنا ہوں تمام کو شامل ہو جائیگا۔ نحو من یا تینی فله در هم یہ ہر آنے والے کو شامل ہوگا خواہ وہ ایک ہویا دو اور دو سے زائد سب کو شامل ہو گا جتنا افراد آئیں گے سب ایک ایک درھم کے مستحق ہوں گے خواہ مجتمعا ہوں یا متعاقبا اگر صرف ایک فرد آتے تو بھی مستحق ہوگا ۔ او علی سبیل البدل
Section on the words of generality. They are either general in form and meaning, like 'al-rijal' (the men) i.e., the plural with definite article, and what does not have the definite article is an indefinite plural, but it is general in meaning; or it is general only in meaning and not in form. And that which is general only in meaning either includes the totality and cannot be applied to each individual, like 'al-rahṭ' (the group) and 'al-qawm' (the people), because these words cannot be applied to a single individual but only to the group. And these words are from the meaning of the plural, i.e., they are in the meaning and legal status of the plural even if they are not plural in form. Or each individual—general in meaning includes every single one on a distributive basis, i.e., it includes all of them, however many they are. Example: 'man ya'tini falahu dirham' (whoever comes to me, for him is a dirham)—this includes every comer, whether one or two or more; all individuals who come each are entitled to a dirham, whether they come together or successively; if only one individual comes, he is also entitled. Or on an alternative basis (ala sabil al-badal).
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of words of generality (alfaz al-'umum). The author, likely Sadr al-Shariah or a commentator, categorizes general words into two main types: those that are general in both form (sigha) and meaning (ma'na), such as the plural with definite article (e.g., 'al-rijal'), and those that are general only in meaning but not in form. The latter type is further subdivided: (a) words that refer to a group as a whole and cannot be applied to individuals, like 'al-qawm' (people) or 'al-rahṭ' (group); these carry the meaning of a plural even though their form is not literally plural; and (b) words that are general in meaning and include every individual on a distributive basis (shumul), such as 'man' (whoever) in a conditional sentence, which gives a dirham to each person who comes, regardless of number. The passage also mentions the alternative (badal) type, though it does not elaborate. This classification is fundamental in Hanafi usul for understanding how general terms (amm) operate, especially in interpreting legal texts where the scope of inclusiveness matters for deriving rulings.

Key Terms
عام (amm): A word that includes all individuals of its category by its form or meaning.
صیغہ (sigha): The linguistic form of a word (e.g., plural with definite article).
شمول (shumul): Distributive inclusiveness, covering each individual separately.
بدل (badal): Alternative; one of two or more possibilities (mentioned but not explained).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
General words in Hanafi usul are not monolithic; their classification into form-and-meaning vs. meaning-only, and further into distributive vs. collective, determines how they apply in legal texts.

Classification of General Words (Alfaz al-'Umum) in Hanafi Usul
Classifies general words by form and meaning with subcategories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given general word as 'amm bil-sigha wal-ma'na or 'amm bil-ma'na faqat, and further categorize the latter into aggregate, shumul, or badal.

Core Idea
A general word may be general in form and meaning, or only in meaning; the latter includes aggregate, inclusive shumul, and substitutional badal.

In this passage, the commentator expands the definition of general words (alfaz al-'umum) according to Hanafi usul. You will learn to distinguish between words that are general both in form (sigha) and meaning, like definite plurals, and those that are general only in meaning, such as collective nouns and conditional particles. This classification is foundational for understanding how general texts (amm) are treated in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main types
First, determine whether a word is general in both form and meaning (e.g., definite plural with 'al') or only in meaning (e.g., singular words denoting a group, conditional particles). The passage gives 'al-rijal' as an example of the first type.
Words with indefinite plural or singular are not 'amm bil-sigha wal-ma'na.
2
Distinguish subcategories of 'amm bil-ma'na faqat
For words general only in meaning, decide if they denote an aggregate (cannot apply to individuals, like 'al-qawm'), include every individual on the basis of shumul (like 'man yatini' without 'awwal'), or on the basis of badal (like 'man yatini awwala').
The passage provides examples: aggregate words govern the whole group; shumul gives each individual; badal gives only the first.
3
Understand the rule for plural
The plural form (e.g., 'al-rijal') and words with plural meaning (like 'al-qawm') apply to three or more. The minimum is three. When used with a specific number, the word includes all individuals of that number.
Example: If a man has ten slaves and says 'abidi aharr', all ten become free.
4
Apply to examples
Practice with provided examples: 'man yatini falahu dirham' (shumul), 'man yatini awwala falahu dirham' (badal), 'al-qawm' (aggregate), and the manumission scenario.
The passage emphasizes that 'amm' includes all, not probabilities.

نقوله يطلق على الثلثة الم یعنی جمع اور القوم والربط کا اطلاق تین اور تین سے زرائد الی مالا نہایت ہر عدد معین پر صحیح ہے ۔ فاذا اطلق على عدد معین تو جب اس کا اطلاق کسی عدد معین پر کیا جائے تو اس کے جمیع افراد کو شامل ہوگا مثلا ایک شخص کے کل عبید تین ہیں اور کہتا ہے عبیدی احرار تو اس کے تینوں غلام ازاد ہو جائیں گے اور دوسرے آدمی کے دس غلام ہیں اور وہ بھی عبیدی احرار بولتا ہے تو اس کے دس کے دس غلام آزاد ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ جس عدد کے لحاظ سے اس کا اطلاق ہو گا اس کے جمیع احاد کو شامل ہو جائیگا کیونکہ عام کی تعریف میں شمول لجميع الافراد ماخوذ ہے وليس المراد یعنی ہمارے اس قول سے یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ یہ لفظ تین کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور تین سے زائد کا بھی کیونکہ یہ مفہوم تو مخالف عموم ہے مثلا اسی صورۃ مذکورہ میں جب اس کے دس غلام تھے تو یوں کہا جائے کہ اس لفظ عبید میں جیسے تین کا احتمال ہے ایسے چار کا اور پانچ وچھ وغیرہ کا بھی احتمال ہے تو یہ ابہام ہو ا عموم نہ ہوا کیونکہ یہ عموم کے منافی ہے بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ قاتل کے تین یا تین سے زائد جتنا غلام ہوں یہ لفظ عبید ان تمام کو شامل ہو جائیگا البتہ یہ لفظ جمع دو اور ایک کو شامل نہیں ہوگا لان اقل الجمع ثلثة چونکہ جمع کے کم سے کم افراد تین ہیں اس لئے تین سے کم پر اس کا اطلاق نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ اس کا اطلاق تین اور اس سے زائد پر ہو گا اگر ایک شخص حلف اٹھاتا ہے لا یتزوج
Section on its words [i.e., general words]. [Alfaz al-umum] are either: (1) general in both form and meaning, like 'al-rijal' (the men) – i.e., a definite plural with 'al'; a indefinite plural is not general in meaning. Or (2) general only in meaning, not in form – this [type] which is general in meaning only either (a) includes the whole group and cannot apply to each individual, like 'al-rabat' and 'al-qawm' – these words cannot apply to a single individual but only to a group; these also have the meaning and ruling of a plural although not plural in form. Or (b) includes each and every individually (shumul), like 'man yatini falahu dirham' – this includes every person who comes, whether one, two, or more; all are entitled to one dirham each, whether they come together or successively; if only one comes, he is entitled. Or (c) on the basis of substitution (badal), i.e., includes each one as a replacement, not inclusively – like 'man yatini awwala falahu dirham'; here the condition is 'first', so it can apply to any individual (Zayd, Amr, Bakr, etc.), but in actuality only the one who comes first is entitled; if a group comes simultaneously, none is entitled; if successively, the first is entitled. Then: the plural (al-jam') and words with its meaning apply to three and above. So plural like 'al-rijal' and 'al-nisa' and those which have the meaning of plural – i.e., the general which includes the aggregate, like 'al-rabat' and 'al-qawm' – their application is to three and above without limit. This is the madhhab of most Companions, jurists, and linguists. We say: it applies to three and above. So when it is applied to a specific number, it includes all individuals of that number. For example, a man has exactly three slaves and says 'my slaves are free' (عبيدي أحرار), all three become free. Another man has ten slaves and says the same, all ten become free. Because in the definition of general ('amm), inclusion of all individuals is inherent. It is not meant that this word has probability for three and also for more, because that would be ambiguity, not generality. Rather, the meaning is that whatever number the speaker has, three or more, the word 'slaves' includes all of them. However, this plural word does not include two or one, because the minimum of plural is three. So it applies to three and above. If a person swears 'la yatazawwaj...'
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the definitions and categories of general words (alfaz al-'umum) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The commentator begins by dividing general words into two types: those that are general in both form (sigha) and meaning (ma'na), e.g., a definite plural like 'al-rijal'; and those that are general only in meaning but not in form. The latter type is further subdivided into: (i) words that denote a collective aggregate and cannot refer to individuals, such as 'al-rabat' (a group) and 'al-qawm' (a people); (ii) words that include every individual on the basis of comprehensiveness (shumul), like the conditional 'man yatini falahu dirham' (whoever comes to me has a dirham) – this includes every person, whether one or many; and (iii) words that include on the basis of substitution (badal), like 'man yatini awwala falahu dirham' (whoever comes to me first has a dirham) – this applies to any possible individual, but actual entitlement is only for the first. Then the passage discusses the nature of the plural form: it applies to three or more (the minimum of plural is three). When a plural word is used regarding a specific number of items, it covers all of them. For example, if a man has exactly three slaves and says 'my slaves are free', all three become free; if another has ten slaves and says the same, all ten become free. This is because the definition of 'amm requires inclusion of all individuals. The passage clarifies that this does not mean the word has multiple probabilities (like three, four, five, etc.) – that would be ambiguity, not generality. Rather, it means the word covers whatever number the speaker actually has, as long as it is three or more. Plural words never include two or one.

Key Terms
عام بالصيغة والمعنى ('amm bil-sigha wal-ma'na): A word that is general in both its form (e.g., definite plural with al) and its meaning, like 'al-rijal' (the men).
عام بالمعنى فقط ('amm bil-ma'na faqat): A word that is general only in meaning, not in form; includes words like 'al-qawm' (the people) which denote a group but are singular in form, and conditional particles like 'man'.
على سبيل البدل ('ala sabili al-badal): A type of general meaning where the rule applies to only one individual from the set, like the first comer in an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum number of individuals for a plural (جمع) to apply?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
General words in Hanafi usul are classified as 'amm bil-sigha wal-ma'na (definite plurals) and 'amm bil-ma'na faqat (aggregate, shumul, or badal); plural minimum is three and covers all individuals of the intended number.

Minimum for Plural and Limits of Specification
Analyzing the dispute on plural minimum and takhsis limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rules on the minimum number for a true plural (three) and the limits of specification (takhsis) to classify general terms and determine the permissible reduction of their scope.

Core Idea
True plural requires three; specification of general terms cannot reduce a true plural below three, but singular-like terms can be specified to one.

This passage addresses a key Hanafi usul dispute about the definition of plural and the limits of specification. The Hanafi school holds that a true plural (jam') indicates three or more, based on linguistic consensus. Opponents cite a hadith that seems to call two a jama'ah. The author explains the Hanafi response by reinterpreting the hadith in specific contexts. Then the passage moves to the rules of takhsis (specification): general terms like 'al-rijal' can only be specified down to three; only terms that are singular in meaning (like 'al-ta'ifah') or used in specific contexts (like exception) can be reduced to one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the core dispute is whether two persons constitute a 'jama'ah' (group) that qualifies as a plural. The Hanafi school argues the minimum for a true plural is three, based on linguistic consensus.
The dispute is about literal (haqiqi) application, not metaphorical.
2
Analyze the opponent's proof
Opponents use the hadith 'al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah' (two and above are a group) and the usage of the pronoun 'na' for two persons. Understand their claim that two is a plural.
The hadith appears to directly support their position.
3
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author provides three contextual interpretations of the hadith (inheritance, imamah, travel) to harmonize it with linguistic consensus. The pronoun 'na' is mushtarak (shared) between dual and plural, not proof that dual is a plural.
These interpretations preserve the consensus of linguists.
4
Apply the rule on specification limits
General terms like 'al-rijal' can only be specified down to three because specification must preserve the plural quality. Exception by istithna' can reduce to one, as in 'akrim al-rijala illa al-jimala'.
Specification via independent text (istithna) is different from general takhsis.
5
Distinguish singular-like terms
Terms like 'al-ta'ifah' and 'al-nisa' in a negative context function like singulars; they can be specified to one. Understand the treatment of collective nouns with 'al' for generality.
The 'al' must be for istighraq (inclusion), not 'ahd (covenant).

الواحد ہو سکیگی ۔ ومنها الى من الفاظ العام المجمع المعرف باللام الم یعنی الفاظ معموم میں سے جمع معرف باللام ہے بشرطیکہ کوئی معہود اور متعین فرد نہ ہو جس کی طرف لام سے اشارہ کرنا مطلوبہ ہو ورنہ تو اس الافراد ہوتا ہے اور بلا قرینہ بعض افراد نہیں لئے جاسکتے لعدم الاولوية کیونکہ اس بعض کے اندر کوئی اولویت موجود نہیں ہے تو پھر بعض کو مراد قرار دینا اور دوسرے بعض کو نظر انداز کرنا ترجیح بلا مرچ ہوگی ۔ متعین الکل تو
The application of 'qulub' (hearts) to two hearts is metaphorical, just as the plural is applied to the singular metaphorically, like in 'qala lahum al-nas'. So the dispute is about real application, not metaphorical. And the hadith is interpreted except that it is a refutation of their third proof: 'al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah'. The gist of the reply is that the hadith pertains to inheritance, and in inheritance, by consensus, the minimum number for the plural starts from two. Or it is about the imam leading prayer: when there are two followers, the imam should stand ahead of them as with more than two, unlike when there is one follower who stands to the imam's right. Or it is about travel companions: after the strengthening of Islam, the Prophet prohibited one or two traveling alone, saying 'al-wahidu shaytan, wal-ithnani shaytanan, wal-thalathatu rakb'. When Islam strengthened, he allowed two to travel, saying 'al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah'. Thus the hadith relates to rulings and matters, not to linguistic usage. These interpretations are necessary so that there is no conflict between the consensus of linguists and hadith. And they cannot hold on to things like 'fa'alna', which is a reply to another proof of those who apply the plural to two. 'Fa'alna' is coined for the plural, and the pronoun is for the plural, so it applies to two as well as three or more. In reply, it is said that they cannot hold on to it because it is shared: the first person plural pronoun is shared between plural and dual; it is coined for both. It is not that the dual is a plural, but rather it is coined for the dual. Hence, specifying the plural is a follow-up: the author said that the minimum number for the plural is three, and this is a note and clarification. Thus, words like 'al-rijal' which have a plural meaning, and words that are in the meaning of plural like 'al-ribat' and 'al-qawm', their specification can only go down to three, not to two or one, because in specification, the quality of being plural must remain. If its specification down to less than three were valid, then the plural form would exit from signifying the plural, and that would be a change, rather abrogation. And what is meant is specification by an independent [text]: specification means that which is with an independent [text], as previously clarified. But it is noted that restricting the general to some, which is by exception, can reduce the plural form to one, as in 'akrim al-rijala illa al-jimala' if only one man remains, he becomes the subject of the ruling. 'Al-mufrad' is in the genitive, and it is conjoined to the plural. The point is that a true singular like 'al-rajul' and words that are not actually singular but are in the meaning of a singular, like those where the plural is used but the singular is meant, e.g., 'la atazawwaju al-nisaa' – here 'al-nisaa' is plural but it cannot mean all women, rather it means one woman. Their specification can go down to one. This word 'al-nisa' occurs in a negative context, so it is correct to mean 'one woman', because generality is impossible, so the 'lam' is for genus, and negation of a genus is negation of all individuals, so its meaning is 'la atazawwaju imra'ah'. 'Al-ta'ifah' is like a singular: Ibn Abbas interpreted 'ta'ifah' in Allah's saying 'falawla nafara min kulli firqatin minhum ta'ifah' as a singular, meaning 'falawla nafara min kulli firqatin minhum wahid'. Because 'ta'ifah' is a fragment of a thing, whether one or more, so it can apply to one and above. Thus its specification can go down to one. And among the words of general application is the collective noun defined by 'al', provided there is no specific individual referred to by the 'al' for covenant; otherwise, the 'al' would be for covenant and would not include all individuals. Since generality requires inclusion. Because what is defined by 'al' in a collective cannot be the essence itself, since the plural form indicates individuals, and without a clue, some individuals cannot be taken due to lack of priority, because there is no priority in those individuals, so to take some and ignore others would be preference without preponderance. Clearly all.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh analysis of the minimum number for the plural (jama') and the specification (takhsis) of general terms ('amm). It begins by addressing a dispute: some argue that the plural can apply to two (as in 'qulub' applied to two hearts by metaphor). The author refutes this by noting that the dispute is about literal (haqiqi) application, not metaphorical. Then it tackles the hadith 'al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah' – which opponents use to claim that two constitute a group. The author gives three possible interpretations: (1) it relates to inheritance where the minimum for shares starting from two heirs; (2) it relates to the imam leading prayer, where two followers require the imam to stand ahead; (3) it relates to travel companions, where initially solo or duo travel was prohibited then duo allowed after Islam's strength. These interpretations harmonize the hadith with the consensus of linguists that the plural minimum is three. Next, the author refutes another proof using the first-person plural pronoun 'fa'alna', arguing it is shared between dual and plural, not evidence for dual being plural. The core ruling: the minimum for a true plural is three (thalaathah). Specification of general terms like 'al-rijal', 'al-ribat', 'al-qawm' can only reduce the number to three, not to two or one, because specification requires preservation of the plural quality; reducing further would effectively nullify the plural meaning. However, there is an exception: specification via an independent text (istithna' = exception) can reduce to one, e.g., 'akrim al-rijala illa al-jimala' may leave only one man included. Then the author explains that true singulars ('al-mufrad') and words that function like singulars (e.g., 'al-nisa' in a negation context meaning 'one woman') can be specified to one. Similarly, 'al-ta'ifah' is like a singular, as per Ibn Abbas, meaning a fragment that can be one person, so its specification can go to one. Finally, the passage discusses 'al-jam' al-mu'arraf bi al-lam' (collective noun with definite article for generality). For it to be general, the 'al' must be for istighraq (inclusion of all individuals), not for 'ahd (covenant specifying a particular set). Because the plural form indicates individuals, and without a clue, selecting some individuals arbitrarily would be unjustified preference (tarjeeh bila murajjih). This is a key Hanafi usul principle: general terms are qat'i in their generality until there is evidence for specification. The passage reflects deep linguistic and legal reasoning typical of Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): A plural form indicating three or more; the minimum for a true plural is three.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): The act of restricting a general term ('amm) to some of its individuals by evidence, while maintaining the term's general nature.
العام (al-'amm): A term that, without context, potentially covers all individuals of its category.
الاستثناء (al-istithna'): An exception that excludes one or more individuals from the general ruling, and can reduce the scope to one even for true plurals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul position presented in this passage, what is the minimum number that constitutes a true plural (jama')?
A) Two
B) Three
C) One
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a true plural requires at least three, and specification of general terms cannot reduce a true plural below three except by an independent exception, while singular-like terms can be specified to one.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Generality of the Definite Plural in Hanafi Usul
Analyzing the types of definite article and proving the generality of the definite plural

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of lam al-ta'rif, apply the Hanafi prioritization ('ahd > istighraq > tabi'ah), and derive the ruling of generality for the definite plural using rational and consensus proofs.

Core Idea
The definite plural indicates generality only when no specific referent exists; otherwise, it denotes a known individual.

In this passage, the commentator explains a foundational usul rule: the definite article (lam al-ta'rif) on a plural noun does not automatically indicate generality. Rather, the primary use is to refer to a known specific referent ('ahd). Only when no such referent exists does the lam indicate istighraq (all individuals of the genus). The passage provides both rational and consensus-based proofs to establish this hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the four categories of lam al-ta'rif
List the four functions: external 'ahd, mental 'ahd, istighraq (generality), and tabi'ah (definition of essence). Note the Hanafi order of priority: 'ahd (both types) first, then istighraq, then tabi'ah.
2
Trace the argument for 'ahd as original
Understand why 'ahd is prioritized: the lam brings a new benefit (fa'idah jadidah) of specifying a known referent, which is more definite than generality. Without 'ahd, no new benefit would be gained if the lam merely repeated the essence.
The passage states: 'laka al-'ahd huwa al-asl'
3
Analyze the rational proof for istighraq
When no 'ahd exists (neither external nor mental), no individual has preference over another. Thus, to avoid arbitrary selection, all individuals must be included – this is istighraq (generality).
This is the first proof (dalil 'aqli).
4
Evaluate the consensus proof
After the Prophet's death, the Ansar said 'muna amir wa minkum amir' (from us an amir and from you an amir). They used 'amir' in a general sense without a specific referent, showing that when no 'ahd is present, the word implies generality.
This is the second proof (ijma).
5
Apply to examples
Test the rule on phrases like 'la atazawwaju al-nisa'' (I will not marry women). In a negative context, istighraq is impossible because it would mean all women, so the lam is for tabi'ah, meaning 'a woman'. This exception shows the importance of context.

استغراق تو متعذر ہے لہذا یہ لیام برائے جنس ہو گا اور نفی جنس بنفی جمیع الافراد ہوتی ہے لہذا اس کا معنی لا اتزوج امراۃ ہو گا۔ والطائفة كالمفرد یعنی لفظ طائفہ بمنزلہ مفرد کے ہے وبهذا فسر ابن عباس ابن یا زیادہ لہذا اس کا اطلاق واحد اور فصاعدا پر ہوگا پس اس کی تخصیص الى الواحد ہو سکیگی ۔ ومنها الى من الفاظ العام المجمع المعرف باللام الم یعنی الفاظ معموم میں سے جمع معرف باللام ہے بشرطیکہ کوئی معہود اور متعین فرد نہ ہو جس کی طرف لام سے اشارہ کرنا مطلوبہ ہو ورنہ تو اس صورت میں لام برائے عہد ہو جائیگا اور جمیع افراد کو شامل نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ حالانکہ عام میں شمول ضروری ہے۔ لان المعرف کیونکہ جو معرف شئی ہے وہ جمع میں نفس ماہیت نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ صیغہ جمع دال علی الافراد ہوتا ہے اور بلا قرینہ بعض افراد نہیں لئے جاسکتے لعدم الاولوية کیونکہ اس بعض کے اندر کوئی اولویت موجود نہیں ہے تو پھر بعض کو مراد قرار دینا اور دوسرے بعض کو نظر انداز کرنا ترجیح بلا مرچ ہوگی ۔ متعین الکل تو اب یہی متعین ہوا کہ کل افراد مراد ہوں گے اسی کو عموم کہتے ہیں اعلم ان لام التعريف الخ یعنی لام تعریف اما للعهد الخارجی یا تو عہد خارجی کے لئے ہوگا یا عہد ذہنی کے لئے یا استغراق جنس کے لئے یعنی جنس کے جمیع افراد کو شامل ہوگا اسے لام استغراق کہتے ہیں یا تعریف طبیعہ کے لئے ہو گا یعنی ماہیتہ من حیث ھی ھی مراد ہوگی جسے لام طبیعہ یا لام جنس کہا جاتا ہے لکن العهد هو الاصل یعنی لام تعریف کے اندر اصل عہد ہے خواہ خارجی ہویا عہد ذہنی پھر اس کے بعد استغراق پھر تعریف طبیعۃ لان اللفظ الذی کیونکہ وہ لفظ جس پر لام تعریف داخل ہوتا ہے وہ بغیر لام کے دال علی الماعیہ ہے تو لام کے داخل ہونے کے بعد لام کو فائدہ جدیدہ پر چھول کرنا بہتر ہے چونکہ لام کے بغیر وہ لفظ دال علی الماہیتہ تھا اور لام کے بعد بھی یہی دلالہ علی الماحیہ مقصود ہو تو پھر فائدہ جدیدہ تو نہ ہوا اس لئے نام کو تعریف ماہیت کے لینا بہتر نہیں ہے ۔ والفائدة الجدیدہ اور فائدہ جدیدہ یا تو تعریف عہد کا ہو سکتا ہے یا استغراق جنس کا یعنی جمیع افراد کے شمول کا اور پھر تعریف عہد اولى من الاستغراق ہے لانه از ذکر کیونکہ جب بعض افراد جنس کا ذکر موجود ہے خواہ خارجا ہو یا ذھنا تو لام کو اسی بعض پر حمل کرنا اولی اور بہتر ہے بانسبت اس کے کہ جمیع افراد پر محمول کریں کیونکہ اس صورت میں بعض کا مراد ہوتا متیقن اور کل افراد کا مراد ہونا محتمل ہے متیقن اولیٰ من المحتمل ہے۔ تو جمع محلی باللام کو تعریف ماہیتہ پر علی سبیل الحقیقة محمول کرنا ممکن نہیں کیونکہ جمع کی وضع افراد ماہیتہ کے لئے ہے نہ کہ نفس ماہیت کے لئے الا یہ کہ حقیقی معنی ترک کر کے مجاز لیں تو پھر جمع سے مراد نفس ماہیت علی سبیل المجاز ہو سکتی ہے علی سبیل الحقیقہ ممکن نہیں ہے اور پھر جب کوئی فرد معہود نہ فی الخارج ہے نہ فی الذین تو اس وقت بعض افراد مراد نہیں ہو سکتے کیونکہ ایک بعض کو بہ نسبت دوسرے بعض کے کوئی اولویت حاصل نہیں ہے تو اس وقت میں اب استغراق کے سوا کوئی چارہ نہیں ہے لہذا محمول علی الاستغراق ہوگا جو جمیع افراد کو شامل ہوگا یہی عموم ہوتا ہے تو یہ دلیل عقلی ہوئی کہ جمع معرف باللام عموم کے لئے ہے۔ مصنف " کے نزدیک عہد ذہنی بھی مقدم على الاستغراق ہے حلافا للبعض . ولتمسكهم یہ جمع محلی بالام کے عام ہونے کے لئے دوسری دلیل ہے جو کہ اجماعی ہے خلاصہ اس کا یہ کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی وفات کے بعد خلافت کے بارہ میں بین الصحابه اختلاف ہوا انصار کہتے تھے منا امير و منکم امير کہ ایک امام المسلمین ہم انصار
Specification cannot extend to one because specification requires preservation of collectivity. If its specification were valid to less than a third, then the plural form's indication of the plural would be removed; then this would be rather abrogation. And the meaning of specification is specification by an independent [specifier], as clarified earlier that specification is that which is with an independent [specifier]. However, a notification was made that restricting the general to some [individuals] via exception can be to one in the plural form. For example, 'If it is said: 'Honor the men except the camels' and in that situation there is only one man, then he would be the subject of that ruling. And the singular in the genitive [phrase]: the word 'al-mufrad' is genitive and its conjunction is on the plural. The purpose is that the real singular like 'al-rajul' and what is in its meaning, and a word that is not literally singular but in meaning is[?]... like 'la atazawwaju al-nisa'' where the word 'al-nisa' is plural but the intended meaning is not all women, rather it means one woman; its specification can extend to one. This word 'al-nisa'' occurs in a negative context; it is correct that it means 'one woman' because generalization is impossible, so this lam is for the genus, and negation of the genus is by negation of all individuals, so its meaning becomes 'la atazawwaju imra'atan' (I will not marry a woman). And 'al-ta'ifah' is like the singular: the word 'ta'ifah' is like the singular. With this Ibn Abbas interpreted: Ibn Abbas interpreted the word 'ta'ifah' in the verse 'Why should not a company from every party of them go forth?' as singular, meaning 'Why should not one from every party of them go forth?' because 'ta'ifah' is a portion of the thing, whether one or more, so its application is to one and above, so its specification to one is possible. And among them is the category of general expressions: the plural with the definite article, i.e. among the expressions of 'umum is the plural defined by alif-lam, on condition that there is no specified and definite individual to which the lam refers; otherwise the lam would be for 'ahd (specified referent) and would not include all individuals, whereas generality requires inclusion. Because the defined thing: the plural form indicates individuals, and some individuals cannot be taken without a context due to lack of preference, because there is no preference in that some over others, so taking some as intended and ignoring others would be preference without a preference. So it is determined that all individuals are intended; this is called 'umum. Know that the definite article is either for external 'ahd, or mental 'ahd, or istighraq of the genus (including all individuals of the genus) called lam istighraq, or definition of the nature (the essence as such) called lam tabi'ah or lam jins. But the original is 'ahd, whether external or mental, then after that istighraq, then definition of the nature. Because the word on which the definite article enters indicates the essence without the lam, so after the lam enters, it is better to consider the lam as bringing a new benefit. Since without the lam the word indicates the essence, and after the lam the same indication of the essence is intended, then there is no new benefit, so it is not better to take the lam for definition of the nature. And the new benefit can only be either 'ahd definition or istighraq of the genus (i.e. inclusion of all individuals). And 'ahd definition is more preferable than istighraq because when the mention of some individuals of the genus is present, whether externally or mentally, it is more appropriate to apply the lam to that some than to apply it to all individuals, because in that case intending some is definite and intending all is probable, and the definite is preferable to the probable. So it is not possible to apply the plural with lam to definition of the nature in a real sense because the plural is placed for individuals of the essence, not for the essence itself, unless one abandons the literal meaning and takes it metaphorically; then the plural could mean the essence metaphorically, but not literally. And when there is no individual that is 'ahd, neither externally nor mentally, then some individuals cannot be intended because one some has no preference over another some; then there is no recourse but istighraq. So it is applied to istighraq, which includes all individuals; this is 'umum. So this is a rational proof that the definite plural is for generality. According to the author, mental 'ahd is also advanced over istighraq, contrary to some. And 'they also hold' this is the second proof for the generality of the definite plural, which is based on consensus. Its summary is that after the death of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), disagreement occurred among the Companions regarding the caliphate. The Ansar said: 'From us an amir and from you an amir' i.e. one leader of the Muslims from us Ansar.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a usul rule: the generality (umum) of the definite plural (al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam). The commentator explains that specification (takhsis) of a general term must preserve the collectivity of the plural; reducing it to one would be abrogation (naskh). However, exceptional specification via istithna' can validly single out one individual because the exception makes that individual the intended referent. He then discusses singular words that are like plurals in meaning but can be specified to one, like 'ta'ifah' in Ibn Abbas's interpretation. The core discussion is about the definite article lam al-ta'rif on a plural noun. The lam can serve four purposes: external 'ahd (a specific known referent), mental 'ahd (a specific referent in mind), istighraq jins (including all individuals of the genus), and ta'rif al-tabi'ah (defining the essence as such). The original (asl) is 'ahd, because it brings a new benefit (fai'dah jadidah) of identifying a particular referent. If no 'ahd exists (neither external nor mental), then istighraq is necessary due to lack of preference among individuals; this is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) for generality. A second proof is ijma' (consensus): the Companions after the Prophet's death disagreed about leadership, with the Ansar saying 'muna amir wa minkum amir' (from us an amir and from you an amir), using 'amir' in a general sense. This shows that the definite singular 'al-amir' implies generality when no 'ahd is present. The passage emphasizes that mental 'ahd also precedes istighraq, according to the author (as opposed to some others).

Key Terms
الجمع المعرف باللام (al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam): A plural noun with the definite article al-, which indicates generality (umum) of all individuals of that genus unless there is a specified referent ('ahd).
لام التعريف (lam al-ta'rif): The definite article in Arabic, which can be for external 'ahd, mental 'ahd, istighraq (generality), or tabi'ah (definition of essence).
عہد ('ahd): A known specific referent, either externally (khariji) or mentally (dhihni), that is intended by the definite article.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the original (asl) usage of the definite article (lam al-ta'rif) when attached to a noun?
A) It is for istighraq (generality).
B) It is for 'ahd (specified referent).
C) It is for tabi'ah (definition of essence).
D) It is for jins (genus).

Key Takeaway
The definite plural indicates generality only when no specific referent ('ahd) exists; otherwise, it is restricted to that referent.
